37 New Sec. 75. (a) On its own after a petition has been filed under
38 section 65, and amendments thereto, or on verified petition by a person
39 interested in an adult's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
40 guardian for the adult if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
41 establish probable cause that:
42 (1) Appointment of an emergency guardian is necessary to prevent
43 imminent and substantial harm to the adult's physical health, safety or
HB 2359 48
1 welfare;
2 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
3 circumstances; and
4 (3) a basis for appointment of a guardian under section 64, and
5 amendments thereto, exists.
6 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency guardian for an adult
7 may not exceed 30 days, and the emergency guardian may exercise only
8 the powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency
9 guardian's authority may be extended up to three times for not more than
10 30 days per extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions
11 for appointment of an emergency guardian in subsection (a) continue.
12 (c) Immediately upon filing of a petition for appointment of an
13 emergency guardian for an adult, the court shall appoint an attorney to
14 represent the respondent in the proceeding. Except as otherwise provided
15 in subsection (d), reasonable notice of the date, time, and place of a
16 hearing on the petition must be given to the respondent, the respondent's
17 attorney and any other person the court determines.
18 (d) The court may appoint an emergency guardian for an adult
19 without notice to the adult and any attorney for the adult only if the court
20 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the respondent's physical health,
21 safety or welfare will be substantially harmed before a hearing with notice
22 on the appointment can be held. If the court appoints an emergency
23 guardian without giving notice under subsection (c), the court must:
24 (1) Give notice of the appointment not later than 48 hours after the
25 appointment to:
26 (A) The respondent;
27 (B) the respondent's attorney; and
28 (C) any other person the court determines; and
29 (2) hold a hearing on the appropriateness of the appointment not later
30 than five days after the appointment.
31 (e) Appointment of an emergency guardian under this section is not a
32 determination that a basis exists for appointment of a guardian under
33 section 64, and amendments thereto.
34 (f) The court may remove an emergency guardian appointed under
35 this section at any time. The emergency guardian shall make any report the
36 court requires.
37 New Sec. 76. (a) A guardian for an adult is a fiduciary. A guardian
38 shall strive to assure that the personal, civil and human rights of the
39 individual subject to guardianship are protected. Except as otherwise
40 limited by the court, a guardian for an adult shall make decisions regarding
41 the support, care, education, health and welfare of the adult subject to
42 guardianship to the extent necessitated by the adult's limitations and in
43 accordance with the guardian's plan under section 79, and amendments
HB 2359 49
1 thereto.
2 (b) A guardian for an adult shall promote the self-determination of the
3 adult and, to the extent reasonably feasible, include the adult in decision
4 making, and encourage the adult to participate in decisions, act on the
5 adult's own behalf, and develop or regain the capacity to manage the
6 adult's personal affairs. In furtherance of this duty, the guardian shall:
7 (1) Become or remain personally acquainted with the adult and
8 maintain sufficient contact with the adult, including through regular
9 visitation, to know the adult's abilities, limitations, needs, opportunities
10 and physical and mental health;
11 (2) to the extent reasonably feasible, identify the values and
12 preferences of the adult and involve the adult in decisions affecting the
13 adult, including decisions about the adult's care, dwelling, activities or
14 social interactions; and
15 (3) make reasonable efforts to identify and facilitate supportive
16 relationships and services for the adult.
17 (c) A guardian for an adult at all times shall exercise reasonable care,
18 diligence and prudence when acting on behalf of or making decisions for
19 the adult. In furtherance of this duty, the guardian shall:
20 (1) Take reasonable care of the personal effects and service or support
21 animals of the adult and bring a proceeding for a conservatorship or
22 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship if necessary to protect
23 the adult's property;
24 (2) if authorized by the court under section 78, and amendments
25 thereto, expend funds and other property of the adult received by the
26 guardian for the adult's current needs for support, care, education, health
27 and welfare;
28 (3) conserve any funds and other property of the adult not expended
29 under paragraph (2) for the adult's future needs, but if a conservator has
30 been appointed for the adult, pay the funds and other property at least
31 quarterly to the conservator to be conserved for the adult's future needs;
32 and
33 (4) monitor the quality of services, including long-term care services,
34 provided to the adult.
35 (d) In making a decision for an adult subject to guardianship, the
36 guardian shall make the decision the guardian reasonably believes the
37 adult would make if the adult were able unless doing so would
38 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
39 interests of the adult. To determine the decision the adult subject to
40 guardianship would make if able, the guardian shall consider the adult's
41 previous or current directions, preferences, opinions, cultural practices,
42 religious beliefs, values and actions, to the extent actually known or
43 reasonably ascertainable by the guardian.
HB 2359 50
1 (e) If a guardian for an adult cannot make a decision under subsection
2 (d) because the guardian does not know and cannot reasonably determine
3 the decision the adult probably would make if able, or the guardian
4 reasonably believes the decision the adult would make would
5 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
6 interests of the adult, the guardian shall act in accordance with the best
7 interest of the adult. In determining the best interest of the adult, the
8 guardian shall consider:
9 (1) Information received from professionals and persons that
10 demonstrate sufficient interest in the welfare of the adult;
11 (2) other information the guardian believes the adult would have
12 considered if the adult were able to act; and
13 (3) other factors a reasonable person in the circumstances of the adult
14 would consider, including consequences for others.
15 (f) A guardian for an adult shall notify the court immediately if the
16 condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable of exercising
17 rights previously removed.
18 New Sec. 77. (a) Except as limited by court order, a guardian for an
19 adult may:
20 (1) If authorized by the court under section 78, and amendments
21 thereto, apply for and receive funds and benefits for the support of the
22 adult, unless a conservator is appointed for the adult and the application or
23 receipt is within the powers of the conservator;
24 (2) establish the adult's place of dwelling;
25 (3) consent to health, including mental health, or other care, treatment
26 or service for the adult;
27 (4) if a conservator for the adult has not been appointed, commence a
28 proceeding including an administrative proceeding, or take other
29 appropriate action to compel another person to support the adult or pay
30 funds for the adult's benefit; and
31 (5) receive personally identifiable healthcare information regarding
32 the adult.
33 (b) The court by specific order may authorize a guardian for an adult
34 to consent to the adoption of the adult.
35 (c) The court by specific order may authorize a guardian for an adult
36 to litigate as petitioner or respondent an action for divorce, dissolution or
37 annulment of marriage of the individual subject to guardianship, including
38 negotiation of a settlement thereof.
39 (d) In determining whether to authorize a power under subsection (b)
40 or (c), the court shall consider whether the underlying act would be in
41 accordance with the adult's preferences, values and prior directions and
42 whether the underlying act would be in the adult's best interest.
43 (e) In exercising a guardian's power under subsection (a)(2) to

1 establish the adult's place of dwelling, the guardian shall:

4 (f) In exercising a guardian's power under subsection (a)(3) to make
5 healthcare decisions, the guardian shall:

12 (3) take into account:
13 (A) The risks and benefits of treatment options; and

16 New Sec. 78. (a) A guardian for an adult may not initiate the
17 commitment of the adult to a mental health facility except in accordance
18 with the care and treatment act for mentally ill persons, K.S.A. 59-2945 et
19 seq., and amendments thereto.
20 (b) A guardian for an adult may not restrict the ability of the adult to
21 communicate, visit or interact with others, including receiving visitors and
22 making or receiving telephone calls, personal mail or electronic
23 communications, including through social media, or participating in social
24 activities, unless:
25 (1) Authorized by the court by specific order;
26 (2) a protective order or a protective arrangement instead of
27 guardianship is in effect that limits contact between the adult and a person;
28 or
29 (3) the guardian has good cause to believe restriction is necessary
30 because interaction with a specified person poses a risk of significant
31 physical, psychological or financial harm to the adult and the restriction is:
32 (A) For a period of not more than seven business days if the person
33 has a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult; or
34 (B) for a period of not more than 60 days if the person does not have
35 a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult.
36 (c) A guardian for an adult may not consent, on behalf of the adult, to:
37 (1) Any psychosurgery, removal of any bodily organ or amputation of
38 any limb, unless such surgery, removal or amputation has been approved
39 in advance by the court, except in an emergency and when necessary to
40 preserve the life of the adult or to prevent serious and irreparable
41 impairment to the physical health of the adult;
42 (2) the sterilization of the adult, unless approved by the court
43 following a due process hearing held for the purposes of determining
HB 2359 53
1 whether to approve such, and during which hearing the adult is represented
2 by an attorney appointed by the court;
3 (3) the performance of any experimental biomedical or behavioral
4 procedure on the adult, or for the adult to be a participant in any
5 biomedical or behavioral experiment, without the prior review and
6 approval of such by either an institutional review board as provided for in
7 title 45, part 46 of the code of federal regulations, or if such regulations do
8 not apply, then by a review committee established by the agency,
9 institution or treatment facility at which the procedure or experiment is
10 proposed to occur, composed of members selected for the purposes of
11 determining whether the proposed procedure or experiment:
12 (A) Does not involve any significant risk of harm to the physical or
13 mental health of the adult, or the use of aversive stimulants, and is
14 intended to preserve the life or health of the adult or to assist the adult to
15 develop or regain skills or abilities; or
16 (B) involves a significant risk of harm to the physical or mental
17 health of the adult, or the use of an aversive stimulant, but that the
18 conducting of the proposed procedure or experiment is intended either to
19 preserve the life of the adult, or to significantly improve the quality of life
20 of the adult, or to assist the adult to develop or regain significant skills or
21 abilities, and that the guardian has been fully informed concerning the
22 potential risks and benefits of the proposed procedure or experiment or of
23 any aversive stimulant proposed to be used, and as to how and under what
24 circumstances the aversive stimulant may be used, and has specifically
25 consented to such;
26 (4) the withholding or withdrawal of life-saving or life-sustaining
27 medical care, treatment, services or procedures, except:
28 (A) In accordance with the provisions of any declaration of the adult
29 made pursuant to the provisions of K.S.A. 65-28,101 through 65-28,109,
30 and amendments thereto; or
31 (B) if the adult, prior to the court's appointment of a guardian, has
32 executed a durable power of attorney for healthcare decisions pursuant to
33 K.S.A. 58-625, et seq., and amendments thereto, and that durable power of
34 attorney has not previously been revoked by the adult, and it includes any
35 provision relevant to the withholding or withdrawal of life-saving or life-
36 sustaining medical care, treatment, services or procedures, then the
37 guardian shall have the authority to act as provided for in that power of
38 attorney, even if the guardian has revoked or amended that power of
39 attorney pursuant to the authority of K.S.A. 58-627, and amendments
40 thereto; or
41 (C) in the circumstances where the adult's treating physician certifies
42 in writing to the guardian that the adult is in a persistent vegetative state or
43 is suffering from an illness or other medical condition for which further
HB 2359 54
1 treatment, other than for the relief of pain, would not likely prolong the life
2 of the adult other than by artificial means, nor would be likely to restore to

4 New Sec. 79. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment and when
5 there is a significant change in circumstances, or the guardian seeks to
6 deviate significantly from the existing guardian's plan, a guardian for an
7 adult shall file with the court a plan for the care of the adult. The plan must
8 be based on the needs of the adult and take into account the best interest of
9 the adult as well as the adult's preferences, values and prior directions, to
10 the extent known to or reasonably ascertainable by the guardian. The
11 guardian shall include in the plan:
12 (1) The living arrangement, services and supports the guardian
13 expects to arrange, facilitate or continue for the adult;
14 (2) social and educational activities the guardian expects to facilitate
15 on behalf of the adult;
16 (3) any person with whom the adult has a close personal relationship
17 or relationship involving regular visitation and any plan the guardian has
18 for facilitating visits with the person;
19 (4) the anticipated nature and frequency of the guardian's visits and
20 communication with the adult;
21 (5) goals for the adult, including any goal related to the restoration of
22 the adult's rights, and how the guardian anticipates achieving the goals;
23 (6) whether the adult has an existing plan and, if so, whether the
24 guardian's plan is consistent with the adult's plan; and
25 (7) a statement or list of the amount the guardian proposes to charge
26 for each service the guardian anticipates providing to the adult.
27 (b) A guardian shall give notice of the filing of the guardian's plan
28 under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to the adult subject
29 to guardianship, any attorney representing the adult subject to
30 guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and
31 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
32 determines. The notice must include a statement of the right to object to
33 the plan and must be given at the time of the filing.
34 (c) An adult subject to guardianship and any person entitled under
35 subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the guardian's plan may
36 object to the plan in writing no later than 21 days after the filing.
37 (d) The court shall review the guardian's plan filed under subsection
38 (a) and determine whether to approve the plan or require a new plan. In
39 deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall consider an objection
40 under subsection (c) and whether the plan is consistent with the guardian's
41 duties and powers under sections 76 and 77, and amendments thereto. The
42 court shall review an initial guardian's plan at the review hearing
43 scheduled under section 73(b), and amendments thereto. When reviewing
HB 2359 56
1 subsequent guardian's plans, the court has discretion whether to set the
2 matter for hearing but may not approve the plan until 30 days after the
3 filing.
4 (e) After the guardian's plan filed under this section is approved by

6 to guardianship, any attorney representing the adult subject to
7 guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and
8 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
9 determines.
10 New Sec. 80. (a) A guardian for an adult shall file with the court at
11 least annually and at any other time the court directs a report in a record
12 regarding the condition of the adult and accounting for funds and other
13 property in the guardian's possession or subject to the guardian's control.
14 (b) A report under subsection (a) must state or contain:
15 (1) The mental, physical and social condition of the adult;
16 (2) the living arrangements of the adult during the reporting period;
17 (3) a summary of the supported decision making, technological
18 assistance, medical services, educational and vocational services and other
19 supports and services provided to the adult and the guardian's opinion as to
20 the adequacy of the adult's care;
21 (4) a summary of the guardian's visits with the adult, including the
22 frequency of the visits;
23 (5) action taken on behalf of the adult;
24 (6) the extent to which the adult has participated in decision making;
25 (7) if the adult is living in a mental health facility or living in a
26 facility that provides the adult with healthcare or other personal services,
27 whether the guardian considers the facility's current plan for support, care,
28 treatment or habilitation consistent with the adult's preferences, values,
29 prior directions and best interest;
30 (8) anything of more than de minimis value which the guardian, any
31 individual who resides with the guardian, or the spouse, parent, child or
32 sibling of the guardian has received from an individual providing goods or
33 services to the adult;
34 (9) any circumstance that may constitute a conflict of interest
35 between the guardian and the adult. A conflict of interest occurs where the
36 guardian has some personal, business or agency interest that could be
37 perceived as self-serving or adverse to the position or best interest of the
38 adult, including, but not limited to, being paid for providing caregiver
39 services to the adult;
40 (10) if a guardian has been granted financial authority under section
41 78(c), and amendments thereto, an accounting that lists property included
42 in the adult's estate and the receipts, disbursements, liabilities and
43 distributions during the period for which the report is made;
HB 2359 57
1 (11) a copy of the guardian's most recently approved plan under
2 section 79, and amendments thereto, and a statement whether the guardian
3 has deviated from the plan and, if so, how the guardian has deviated and
4 why;
5 (12) plans for future care and support of the adult;
6 (13) a recommendation as to the need for continued guardianship and
7 any recommended change in the scope of the guardianship, including
8 whether the condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable
9 of exercising rights previously removed; and
10 (14) whether any co-guardian or successor guardian appointed to
11 serve when a designated event occurs is alive and able to serve.
12 (c) A guardian for an adult shall file a special report with the court
13 upon the occurrence of any of the following:
14 (1) A change of address of the guardian;
15 (2) a change of residence or placement of the adult;
16 (3) a significant change in the health or impairment of the adult;
17 (4) the acquisition by the adult of any real property, or the receipt or
18 accumulation of other property or income by the adult or by the guardian
19 on behalf of the adult, which causes the total value of the adult's estate to
20 equal or exceed $25,000;
21 (5) the death of the adult; or
22 (6) a change in the circumstances of the guardian or the adult that
23 may constitute a conflict of interest. A conflict of interest occurs where the
24 guardian has some personal, business or agency interest that could be
25 perceived as self-serving or adverse to the position or best interest of the
26 adult.

33 adult subject to guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section
34 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other
35 person the court determines. The notice and report must be given not later
36 than 14 days after the filing.

40 (1) The report provides sufficient information to establish the
41 guardian has complied with the guardian's duties;
42 (2) the guardianship should continue; and

1 (g) If the court determines that there is reason to believe a guardian

21 New Sec. 81. (a) The court may remove a guardian for an adult for
22 failure to perform the guardian's duties or for other good cause and appoint
23 a successor guardian to assume the duties of guardian.
24 (b) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether to remove a
25 guardian for an adult and appoint a successor guardian on:

30 hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts was
31 filed during the preceding six months;

33 the welfare of the adult which supports a reasonable belief that removal of
34 the guardian and appointment of a successor guardian may be appropriate;
35 (3) determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
36 interest of the adult; or

21 New Sec. 83. (a) On petition and after notice and hearing, the court
22 may appoint a conservator for the property or financial affairs of a minor if
23 the court finds by a preponderance of evidence that the minor owns funds
24 or other property exceeding $25,000 in value derived from court
25 settlements, death transfers or sources other than the minor's employment
26 earnings or accounts established under the uniform transfers to minors act,
27 and either:
28 (1) The minor owns funds or other property requiring management or
29 protection that otherwise cannot be provided;
30 (2) the minor has or may have financial affairs that may be put at
31 unreasonable risk or hindered because of the minor's age; or
32 (3) appointment is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide funds
33 or other property needed for the support, care, education, health or welfare
34 of the minor.
35 (b) On petition and after notice and hearing, the court may appoint a
36 conservator for the property or financial affairs of an adult if the court
37 finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
38 (1) The adult is unable to manage property or financial affairs
39 because:
40 (A) Of a limitation in the adult's ability to receive and evaluate
41 information or make or communicate decisions, even with the use of
42 appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
43 decision making; or
HB 2359 61
1 (B) the adult is missing, detained or unable to return to the United
2 States;
3 (2) appointment is necessary to:
4 (A) Avoid harm to the adult or significant dissipation of the property
5 of the adult; or
6 (B) obtain or provide funds or other property needed for the support,
7 care, education, health or welfare of the adult or of an individual entitled to
8 the adult's support; and
9 (3) the adult's identified needs cannot be met by a protective
10 arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive alternative.
11 (c) The court shall grant a conservator only those powers necessitated
12 by demonstrated limitations and needs of the adult and issue orders that
13 will encourage development of the adult's maximum self-determination
14 and independence. The court may not establish a full conservatorship if a
15 limited conservatorship, protective arrangement instead of conservatorship
16 or other less restrictive alternative would meet the needs of the adult.

7 (D) a guardian or conservator acting for the respondent in this state or
8 another jurisdiction;
9 (E) a trustee or custodian of a trust or custodianship of which the
10 respondent is a beneficiary;
11 (F) the fiduciary appointed for the respondent by the department of
12 veterans affairs and any curator appointed under K.S.A. 73-507, and
13 amendments thereto;
14 (G) an agent designated under a power of attorney for healthcare in
15 which the respondent is identified as the principal;
16 (H) an agent designated under a power of attorney for finances in
17 which the respondent is identified as the principal;
18 (I) a person known to have routinely assisted the respondent with
19 decision making in the six-month period immediately before the filing of
20 the petition; and
21 (J) if the individual for whom a conservator is sought is a minor:
22 (i) An adult not otherwise listed with whom the minor resides; and
23 (ii) each person not otherwise listed that had primary care or custody
24 of the minor for at least 60 days during the two years immediately before
25 the filing of the petition or for at least 730 days during the five years
26 immediately before the filing of the petition;
27 (4) (A) The name, age, date of birth, gender, address, place of
28 employment and relationship to the respondent, if any, of the proposed
29 conservator;
30 (B) the reason the proposed conservator should be selected; and
31 (C) any potential conflict of interest including any personal or agency
32 interest of the proposed conservator that may be perceived as self-serving
33 or adverse to the position or best interest of the respondent;
34 (5) a general statement of the respondent's property with an estimate
35 of its value, including any insurance or pension, and the source and
36 amount of other anticipated income or receipts;
37 (6) the reason conservatorship is necessary, including a description
38 of:
39 (A) The nature and extent of the respondent's alleged need;
40 (B) if the petition alleges the respondent is missing, detained or
41 unable to return to the United States, the relevant circumstances, including
42 the time and nature of the disappearance or detention and any search or
43 inquiry concerning the respondent's whereabouts;
HB 2359 63
1 (C) any protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other
2 less restrictive alternative for meeting the respondent's alleged need which
3 has been considered or implemented;
4 (D) if no protective arrangement or other less restrictive alternatives
5 have been considered or implemented, the reason it has not been
6 considered or implemented; and
7 (E) the reason a protective arrangement or other less restrictive
8 alternative is insufficient to meet the respondent's need;
9 (7) whether the petitioner seeks a limited conservatorship or a full
10 conservatorship;
11 (8) if the petitioner seeks a full conservatorship, the reason a limited
12 conservatorship or protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is
13 not appropriate;
14 (9) if the petition is for a limited conservatorship, a description of the
15 property to be placed under the conservator's control and any requested
16 limitation on the authority of the conservator;
17 (10) whether the respondent needs an interpreter, translator or other
18 form of support to communicate effectively with the court or understand
19 court proceedings; and
20 (11) the name and address of an attorney representing the petitioner,
21 if any.
22 New Sec. 85. (a) On filing of a petition under section 84, and
23 amendments thereto, for appointment of a conservator, the court shall set a
24 date, time and place for a hearing on the petition.
25 (b) A copy of a petition under section 84, and amendments thereto,
26 and notice of a hearing on the petition must be served personally on the
27 respondent. If the respondent's whereabouts are unknown or personal
28 service cannot be made, service on the respondent must be made by
29 substituted service, as ordered by the court. The notice must inform the
30 respondent of the respondent's rights at the hearing, including the right to
31 an attorney and to attend the hearing. The notice must include a
32 description of the nature, purpose and consequences of granting the
33 petition. The court may not grant a petition for appointment of a
34 conservator if notice substantially complying with this subsection is not
35 served on the respondent. The court may order any of the following
36 persons to serve the notice upon the respondent:
37 (1) The petitioner or the attorney for the petitioner;
38 (2) the attorney appointed by the court to represent the respondent;
39 (3) any law enforcement officer; or
40 (4) any other person whom the court finds to be a proper person to
41 serve this notice.
42 (c) In a proceeding on a petition under section 84, and amendments
43 thereto, the notice required under subsection (b) must be given to the
HB 2359 64
1 persons required to be listed in the petition under section 84(b)(1) through
2 (3), and amendments thereto, and any other person interested in the
3 respondent's welfare the court determines. Failure to give notice under this
4 subsection does not preclude the court from appointing a conservator.
5 (d) After the appointment of a conservator, notice of a hearing on a
6 petition for any other order under sections 83 through 118, and
7 amendments thereto, together with a copy of the petition, must be given to:
8 (1) The individual subject to conservatorship, if the individual is 12
9 years of age or older and not missing, detained or unable to return to the
10 United States;
11 (2) the conservator; and
12 (3) any other person the court determines.
13 New Sec. 86. While a petition under section 84, and amendments
14 thereto, is pending, after preliminary hearing and without notice to others,
15 the court may issue an order to preserve and apply property of the
16 respondent as required for the support of the respondent or an individual
17 who is in fact dependent on the respondent. The court may appoint an
18 emergency conservator to assist in implementing the order.
19 New Sec. 87. (a) If the respondent in a proceeding to appoint a
20 conservator is a minor, the court may appoint a court liaison to investigate
21 a matter related to the petition or inform the minor or a parent of the minor
22 about the petition or a related matter.
23 (b) If the respondent in a proceeding to appoint a conservator is an
24 adult, the court may appoint a court liaison. The duties and reporting
25 requirements of the court liaison are limited to the relief requested in the
26 petition. The court liaison must be an individual with training or
27 experience in the type of abilities, limitations and needs alleged in the
28 petition.
29 (c) (1) A court liaison appointed under subsection (b) for an adult
30 shall interview the respondent in person and in a manner the respondent is
31 best able to understand:
32 (A) Explain, in general, the petition, and the nature and purpose of
33 the proceeding, including the potential loss of rights as a result of the
34 proceeding; and
35 (B) obtain the respondent's views about the appointment sought by
36 the petitioner, including views about a proposed conservator, the
37 conservator's proposed powers and duties and the scope and duration of
38 the proposed conservatorship.
39 (2) These explanations and discussions are not intended to be a
40 substitute for the attorney appointed to represent the respondent to inform
41 the respondent of the respondent's rights and the nature and purpose of the
42 proceeding.
43 (d) A court liaison appointed under subsection (b) for an adult may be
HB 2359 65
1 assigned any or all of the following duties, in the discretion of the
2 presiding judge:
3 (1) Interview the petitioner and proposed conservator, if any;
4 (2) review financial records of the respondent, if relevant to the court
5 liaison's recommendation under subsection (e)(1);
6 (3) investigate whether the respondent's needs could be met by a
7 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive
8 alternative and, if so, identify the arrangement or other less restrictive
9 alternative; and
10 (4) investigate the allegations in the petition and any other matter
11 relating to the petition as directed by the court, including, but not limited
12 to, the respondent's family relationships, past conduct, the nature and
13 extent of any property or income of the respondent, whether the
14 respondent is likely to injure self or others and other matters as the court
15 may specify.
16 (e) A court liaison appointed under subsection (b) for an adult shall
17 file a report with the court at least 10 days prior to the hearing on the
18 petition or other hearing as directed by the court. Unless otherwise ordered
19 by the court, such report must include:
20 (1) A recommendation:
21 (A) Regarding the appropriateness of conservatorship, or whether a
22 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive
23 alternative for meeting the respondent's needs is available;
24 (B) if a conservatorship is recommended, whether it should be full or
25 limited; and
26 (C) if a limited conservatorship is recommended, the powers to be
27 granted to the conservator, and the property that should be placed under
28 the conservator's control;
29 (2) a statement of the qualifications of the proposed conservator and
30 whether the respondent approves or disapproves of the proposed
31 conservator;
32 (3) a statement whether the respondent is able to attend a hearing at
33 the location court proceedings typically are held;
34 (4) a statement whether the respondent is able to participate in a
35 hearing and which identifies any technology or other form of support that
36 would enhance the respondent's ability to participate; and
37 (5) any other matter the court directs.
38 (d) The costs of an investigation by a court liaison shall be assessed
39 as provided for in section 42, and amendments thereto.
40 New Sec. 88. (a) Unless the respondent in a proceeding for
41 appointment of a conservator is represented by an attorney, the court shall
42 appoint an attorney to represent the respondent, regardless of the
43 respondent's ability to pay. The court shall give preference in the
HB 2359 66
1 appointment of an attorney to any attorney who has represented the
2 respondent in other matters if the court has knowledge of that prior
3 representation or to an attorney whom the respondent has requested. Any
4 appointment made by the court shall terminate after the conservator's plan
5 has been approved and after any appeal from the appointment of a
6 conservator, unless the court continues the appointment by further order.
7 Thereafter, an attorney may be appointed by the court if requested, in
8 writing, by the adult subject to conservatorship, the conservator or upon
9 the court's own motion.
10 (b) An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding for
11 appointment of a conservator shall:
12 (1) Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes;
13 (2) advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably
14 ascertainable; and
15 (3) if the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable,
16 advocate for the result that is the least-restrictive in type, duration and
17 scope, consistent with the respondent's interests.
18 (c) An attorney representing the respondent shall interview the
19 respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to
20 understand:
21 (1) Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature,
22 purpose and effect of the proceeding, the respondent's rights at the hearing
23 on the petition and the general powers and duties of a conservator;
24 (2) determine the respondent's views about the appointment sought by
25 the petitioner, including views about a proposed conservator, the
26 conservator's proposed powers and duties and the scope and duration of
27 the proposed conservatorship; and
28 (3) inform the respondent that all costs and expenses of the
29 proceeding, including respondent's attorney fees, may be paid from the
30 respondent's assets.
31 (d) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent a parent of a
32 minor who is the subject of a proceeding under section 84, and
33 amendments thereto, if the court determines the parent needs
34 representation.
35 New Sec. 89. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
36 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
37 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a conservator, the court
38 shall order an examination and evaluation of the respondent to be
39 conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric hospital, community
40 mental health center or community developmental disability organization,
41 or by a licensed physician, psychiatrist, psychologist, physician assistant,
42 nurse practitioner, social worker or other professional appointed by the
43 court who is qualified to evaluate the respondent's alleged cognitive and
HB 2359 67
1 functional abilities and limitations and will not be advantaged or
2 disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition or otherwise have a
3 conflict of interest.
4 (b) Unless otherwise specified by the court, the report of the
5 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:
6 (1) The respondent's name, age and date of birth;
7 (2) a description of the respondent's physical and mental condition;
8 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
9 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
10 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
11 (4) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
12 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;
13 (5) a list and description of any prior assessments, evaluations or
14 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
15 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;
16 (6) the date and location where this examination and evaluation
17 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals
18 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
19 qualifications;
20 (7) a statement by the professional that the professional has
21 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
22 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results
23 of that examination and evaluation, and the professional's opinion with
24 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
25 conservator and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance
26 and participation at the hearing on the petition; and
27 (8) the signature of the professional who prepared the report.
28 (c) The professional shall file with the court, at least five days prior to
29 the date of the trial, such professional's written report concerning the
30 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made
31 available by the court to counsel for all parties.
32 (d) In lieu of entering an order for an examination and evaluation as
33 provided for in this section, the court may determine that the report
34 accompanying the petition is in compliance with the requirements of this
35 section and that no further examination or evaluation should be required,
36 unless the respondent, or such person's attorney, requests such an
37 examination and evaluation in writing. Any such request shall be filed with
38 the court, and a copy thereof delivered to the petitioner, at least four days
39 prior to the date of the trial. Accompanying the request shall be a statement
40 of the reasons why an examination and evaluation is requested and the
41 name and address of a qualified professional or facility willing and able to
42 conduct this examination and evaluation. If the court orders a further
43 examination and evaluation, the court may continue the trial and fix a new
HB 2359 68
1 date, time and place of the trial at a time not to exceed 30 days from the
2 date of the filing of the request.
3 New Sec. 90. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
4 hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, may not proceed unless
5 the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably feasible for the
6 respondent to attend a hearing at the location court proceedings typically
7 are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to hold the hearing at an
8 alternative location convenient to the respondent or allow the respondent
9 to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual technology.
10 (b) A hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, may
11 proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court finds by clear
12 and convincing evidence that:
13 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
14 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
15 of failing to do so;
16 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
17 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services or
18 technological assistance; or
19 (3) the respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and
20 attendance would be harmful to the minor.
21 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under section 85, and
22 amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the respondent's choosing,
23 assistive technology or an interpreter or translator, or a combination of
24 these supports. If assistance would facilitate the respondent's participation
25 in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to the respondent, the court
26 shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.
27 (d) The respondent has a right to retain an attorney to represent the
28 respondent at a hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto.
29 (e) At a hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, the
30 respondent may:
31 (1) Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents;
32 (2) examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator or
33 court liaison; and
34 (3) otherwise participate in the hearing.
35 (f) Unless excused by the court for good cause, a proposed
36 conservator shall attend a hearing under section 85, and amendments
37 thereto.
38 (g) A hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, must be
39 closed on request of the respondent and a showing of good cause.
40 (h) Any person may request to participate in a hearing under section
41 85, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the request, with or
42 without a hearing, on determining that the best interest of the respondent
43 will be served. The court may impose appropriate conditions on the
HB 2359 69
1 person's participation.
2 New Sec. 91. (a) The existence of a proceeding for or the existence of
3 conservatorship is a matter of public record unless the court seals the
4 record after:
5 (1) The respondent, the individual subject to conservatorship or the
6 parent of a minor subject to conservatorship requests the record be sealed;
7 and
8 (2) either:
9 (A) The petition for conservatorship is dismissed; or
10 (B) the conservatorship is terminated.
11 (b) (1) The following court records are a matter of public record
12 unless sealed by the court:
13 (A) Letters of conservatorship;
14 (B) orders suspending or removing a conservator; and
15 (C) orders terminating a conservatorship.
16 (2) All other court records of a conservatorship proceeding are not a
17 matter of public record except as further provided.
18 (3) The following persons may access court records of the proceeding
19 and resulting conservatorship, including the conservator's plan under
20 section 103, and amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under
21 section 105, and amendments thereto:
22 (A) An individual subject to a proceeding for a conservatorship,
23 whether or not a conservator is appointed;
24 (B) an attorney designated by the individual;
25 (C) a person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and amendments
26 thereto, or a subsequent order; and
27 (D) a licensed attorney, abstractor or title insurance agent.
28 (4) A person not otherwise entitled to access to court records under
29 this section for good cause may request permission from the court for
30 access to court records of the conservatorship, including the conservator's
31 plan and report. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest
32 of the respondent or individual subject to conservatorship or furthers the
33 public interest and does not endanger the welfare or financial interests of
34 the respondent or individual.
35 (c) A report under section 87, and amendments thereto, of a court
36 liaison or professional evaluation under section 89, and amendments
37 thereto, is confidential and must be sealed on filing, but is available to:
38 (1) The court;
39 (2) the individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation,
40 without limitation as to use;
41 (3) the petitioner, court liaison and petitioner's and respondent's
42 attorneys, for purposes of the proceeding;
43 (4) unless the court directs otherwise, an agent appointed under a
HB 2359 70
1 power of attorney for finances in which the respondent is identified as the
2 principal; and
3 (5) any other person if it is in the public interest or for a purpose the
4 court orders for good cause.
5 New Sec. 92. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
6 court in appointing a conservator shall consider persons qualified to be a
7 conservator in the following order of priority:
8 (1) A conservator, other than a temporary or emergency conservator,
9 currently acting for the respondent in another jurisdiction;
10 (2) a person nominated as conservator by the respondent, including
11 the respondent's most recent nomination made in a power of attorney for
12 finances;
13 (3) an agent appointed by the respondent to manage the respondent's
14 property under a power of attorney for finances;
15 (4) a spouse of the respondent;
16 (5) a family member or other individual who has shown special care
17 and concern for the respondent; and
18 (6) a person nominated as conservator by the spouse, adult child or
19 other close family member of the respondent.
20 (b) If two or more persons have equal priority under subsection (a),
21 the court shall select as conservator the person the court considers best
22 qualified. In determining the best qualified person, the court shall consider
23 the person's relationship with the respondent, the person's skills, the
24 expressed wishes of the respondent, the extent to which the person and the
25 respondent have similar values and preferences and the likelihood the
26 person will be able to perform the duties of a conservator successfully.
27 (c) The court, acting in the best interest of the respondent, may
28 decline to appoint as conservator a person having priority under subsection
29 (a) and appoint a person having a lower priority or no priority.
30 (d) The following persons shall not be appointed as conservator
31 unless the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that the person is
32 the best qualified person available for appointment and the appointment is
33 in the best interest of the respondent:
34 (1) A person that provides paid services to the respondent, or an
35 individual who is employed by a person that provides paid services to the
36 respondent, or is the spouse, parent or child of an individual who provides
37 or is employed to provide paid services to the respondent;
38 (2) an owner, operator or employee of any entity at which the
39 respondent is receiving care; and
40 (3) a person who provides care or other services, or is an employee of
41 an agency, partnership or corporation that provides care or other services
42 to persons with needs similar to those of the respondent.
43 New Sec. 93. (a) A court order appointing a conservator for a minor
HB 2359 71
1 must include findings to support appointment of a conservator.
2 (b) A court order appointing a conservator for an adult must:
3 (1) Include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence has
4 established that the identified needs of the respondent cannot be met by a
5 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive
6 alternative, including use of appropriate supportive services, technological
7 assistance or supported decision making; and
8 (2) include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence
9 established the respondent was given proper notice of the hearing on the
10 petition.
11 (c) A court order establishing a full conservatorship for an adult must
12 state the basis for granting a full conservatorship and include specific
13 findings to support the conclusion that a limited conservatorship would not
14 meet the functional needs of the adult.
15 (d) A court order establishing a limited conservatorship must state the
16 specific property placed under the control of the conservator and the
17 powers granted to the conservator.
18 (e) A court order appointing a conservator must include the date of a
19 review hearing to be set 90 days after the order of appointment is entered.
20 At that hearing, the court shall review the conservator's plan filed pursuant
21 to section 103, and amendments thereto, and the inventory filed pursuant
22 to section 104, and amendments thereto.
23 (f) The court, as part of an order establishing a conservatorship, shall
24 identify any person that subsequently is entitled to:
25 (1) Notice of the rights of the individual subject to conservatorship
26 under section 94(b), and amendments thereto;
27 (2) notice of a sale or other disposition of, encumbrance of an interest
28 in, or surrender of a lease to any real or personal property of the
29 individual;
30 (3) notice that the conservator will be unavailable to perform the
31 conservator's duties for more than one month;
32 (4) a copy of the conservator's plan under section 103, and
33 amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under section 105, and
34 amendments thereto;
35 (5) access to court records relating to the conservatorship;
36 (6) notice of a transaction involving a substantial conflict between the
37 conservator's fiduciary duties and personal interests;
38 (7) notice of the death or significant change in the condition of the
39 individual;
40 (8) notice that a petition has been filed to limit or modify the powers
41 of the conservator or that the court has limited or modified the powers of
42 the conservator; and
43 (9) notice that a petition has been filed to remove the conservator or
HB 2359 72
1 that the court has removed the conservator.
2 (g) If an individual subject to conservatorship is an adult, the spouse
3 and adult children of the adult subject to conservatorship are entitled under
4 subsection (e) to notice unless the court determines notice would be
5 contrary to the preferences or prior directions of the adult subject to
6 conservatorship or not in the best interest of the adult.
7 (h) If an individual subject to conservatorship is a minor, each parent
8 and adult sibling of the minor is entitled under subsection (e) to notice
9 unless the court determines notice would not be in the best interest of the
10 minor.
11 New Sec. 94. (a) Not later than 14 days after the appointment, a
12 conservator appointed under section 93, and amendments thereto, shall
13 give to the individual subject to conservatorship and to all other persons
14 given notice under section 85, and amendments thereto, a copy of the
15 order of appointment.
16 (b) Not later than 30 days after appointment of a conservator under
17 section 93, and amendments thereto, the court or the court's designee shall
18 give to the individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator, and any
19 other person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and amendments
20 thereto, a statement of the rights of the individual subject to
21 conservatorship and procedures to seek relief if the individual is denied
22 those rights. The statement must be in plain language, in at least 16-point
23 font, and to the extent feasible, in a language in which the individual
24 subject to conservatorship is proficient. The statement must notify the
25 individual subject to conservatorship of the right to:
26 (1) Seek termination or modification of the conservatorship, or
27 removal of the conservator, and choose an attorney to represent the
28 individual in these matters;
29 (2) file a grievance against the conservator under section 50, and
30 amendments thereto;
31 (3) participate in decision making to the extent reasonably feasible;
32 (4) receive a copy of the conservator's plan under section 103, and
33 amendments thereto, the conservator's inventory under section 104, and
34 amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under section 105, and
35 amendments thereto; and
36 (5) object to the conservator's inventory, plan or report.
37 (c) If a conservator is appointed for the reasons stated in section 83(b)
38 (1)(B), and amendments thereto, and the individual subject to
39 conservatorship is missing, notice under this section to the individual is
40 not required. If the individual subject to conservatorship is a minor under
41 the age of 12, notice under this section to the minor is not required.
42 (d) Any person required to provide notice under this section shall file
43 proof of service of such notice with the court.

1 New Sec. 95. (a) On its own after a petition has been filed under
2 section 84, and amendments thereto, or on a verified petition by a person
3 interested in an individual's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
4 conservator for the individual if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
5 establish probable cause that:
6 (1) Appointment of an emergency conservator is necessary to prevent
7 imminent, substantial and irreparable harm to the individual's property or
8 financial interests;
9 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
10 circumstances; and
11 (3) a basis for appointment of a conservator under section 83, and
12 amendments thereto, exists.
13 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency conservator may not
14 exceed 30 days and the emergency conservator may exercise only the
15 powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency conservator's
16 authority may be extended up to three times for not more than 30 days per
17 extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions for
18 appointment of an emergency conservator under subsection (a) continue.
19 (c) Immediately on filing of a petition for an emergency conservator,
20 the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the respondent in the
21 proceeding. Except as otherwise provided in subsection (d), reasonable
22 notice of the date, time and place of a hearing on the petition must be
23 given to the respondent, the respondent's attorney and any other person the
24 court determines.
25 (d) The court may appoint an emergency conservator without notice
26 to the respondent and any attorney for the respondent only if the court
27 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the respondent's property or
28 financial interests will be substantially and irreparably harmed before a
29 hearing with notice on the appointment can be held. If the court appoints
30 an emergency conservator without giving notice under subsection (c), the
31 court must give notice of the appointment not later than 48 hours after the
32 appointment to:
33 (1) The respondent;
34 (2) the respondent's attorney; and
35 (3) any other person the court determines.
36 (e) Not later than five days after the appointment, the court shall hold
37 a hearing on the appropriateness of the appointment.
38 (f) Appointment of an emergency conservator under this section is
39 not a determination that a basis exists for appointment of a conservator
40 under section 83, and amendments thereto.
41 (g) The court may remove an emergency conservator appointed under
42 this section at any time. The emergency conservator shall make any report
43 the court requires.

1 New Sec. 96. An individual subject to conservatorship or a person
2 interested in the welfare of the individual may petition for an order:
3 (a) Modifying bond requirements;
4 (b) requiring an accounting for the administration of the
5 conservatorship estate;
6 (c) directing distribution;
7 (d) removing the conservator and appointing a temporary or
8 successor conservator;
9 (e) modifying the type of appointment or powers granted to the
10 conservator, if the extent of protection or management previously granted
11 is excessive or insufficient to meet the individual's needs, including
12 because the individual's abilities or supports have changed;
13 (f) rejecting or modifying the conservator's plan under section 103,
14 and amendments thereto, the conservator's inventory under section 104,
15 and amendments thereto, or the conservator's report under section 105, and
16 amendments thereto; or
17 (g) granting other appropriate relief.
18 New Sec. 97. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
19 court shall require a conservator to furnish a bond with a surety, or require
20 an alternative asset-protection arrangement, conditioned on faithful
21 discharge of all duties of the conservator. The court may waive the
22 requirement only if the court finds that a bond or other asset-protection
23 arrangement is not necessary to protect the interests of the individual
24 subject to conservatorship. Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c),
25 the court may not waive the requirement if the conservator is in the
26 business of serving as a conservator and is being paid for the conservator's
27 service.
28 (b) Unless the court directs otherwise, the bond required under this
29 section must be in the amount of the aggregate capital value of the
30 conservatorship estate, plus one year's estimated income, less the value of
31 property deposited under an arrangement requiring a court order for its
32 removal, and less the value of real property. The court, in place of surety
33 on a bond, may accept collateral for the performance of the bond,
34 including a pledge of securities or a mortgage of real property.
35 (c) A regulated financial-service institution qualified to do trust
36 business in this state is not required to give a bond under this section.
37 (d) If the conservator appointed is under contract with the Kansas
38 guardianship program, the Kansas department for children and families
39 shall act as surety on the bond.
40 New Sec. 98. (a) The following rules apply to the bond required
41 under section 97, and amendments thereto:
42 (1) Except as otherwise provided by the bond, the surety and the
43 conservator are jointly and severally liable.
HB 2359 75
1 (2) By executing a bond provided by a conservator, the surety
2 submits to the personal jurisdiction of the court that issued letters of office
3 to the conservator in a proceeding relating to the duties of the conservator
4 in which the surety is named as a party. Notice of the proceeding must be

22 New Sec. 99. (a) A conservator is a fiduciary and has duties of
23 prudence, loyalty, reasonable care and diligence to the individual subject to
24 conservatorship.
25 (b) A conservator shall promote the self-determination of the
26 individual subject to conservatorship and, to the extent feasible, encourage
27 the individual to participate in decisions, act on the individual's own
28 behalf, and develop or regain the capacity to manage the individual's
29 personal affairs. A conservator shall strive to assure that the personal, civil
30 and human rights of the individual subject to conservatorship are
31 protected.
32 (c) In making a decision for an individual subject to conservatorship,
33 the conservator shall make the decision that the conservator reasonably
34 believes the individual would make if able, unless doing so would fail to
35 preserve the resources needed to maintain the individual's well-being and
36 lifestyle or otherwise unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or
37 personal or financial interests of the individual. To determine the decision
38 the individual would make if able, the conservator shall consider the
39 individual's prior or current directions, preferences, opinions, values and
40 actions, to the extent actually known or reasonably ascertainable by the
41 conservator.
42 (d) If a conservator cannot make a decision under subsection (c)
43 because the conservator does not know and cannot reasonably determine
HB 2359 76
1 the decision the individual subject to conservatorship probably would
2 make if able, or the conservator reasonably believes the decision the
3 individual would make would fail to preserve resources needed to
4 maintain the individual's well-being and lifestyle or otherwise
5 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
6 interests of the individual, the conservator shall act in accordance with the
7 best interest of the individual. In determining the best interest of the
8 individual, the conservator shall consider:
9 (1) Information received from professionals and persons that
10 demonstrate sufficient interest in the welfare of the individual;
11 (2) other information the conservator believes the individual would
12 have considered if the individual were able to act; and
13 (3) other factors a reasonable person in the circumstances of the
14 individual would consider, including consequences for others.
15 (e) Except when inconsistent with the conservator's duties under
16 subsections (a) through (d), a conservator shall invest and manage the
17 conservatorship estate as a prudent investor would, by considering:
18 (1) The circumstances of the individual subject to conservatorship
19 and the conservatorship estate;
20 (2) general economic conditions;
21 (3) the possible effect of inflation or deflation;
22 (4) the expected tax consequences of an investment decision or
23 strategy;
24 (5) the role of each investment or course of action in relation to the
25 conservatorship estate as a whole;
26 (6) the expected total return from income and appreciation of capital;
27 (7) the need for liquidity, regularity of income and preservation or
28 appreciation of capital; and
29 (8) the special relationship or value, if any, of specific property to the
30 individual subject to conservatorship.
31 (f) The propriety of a conservator's investment and management of
32 the conservatorship estate is determined in light of the facts and
33 circumstances existing when the conservator decides or acts and not by
34 hindsight.
35 (g) A conservator shall make a reasonable effort to verify facts
36 relevant to the investment and management of the conservatorship estate.
37 (h) A conservator that has special skills or expertise, or is named
38 conservator in reliance on the conservator's representation of special skills
39 or expertise, has a duty to use the special skills or expertise in carrying out
40 the conservator's duties.
41 (i) In investing, selecting specific property for distribution, and
42 invoking a power of revocation or withdrawal for the use or benefit of the
43 individual subject to conservatorship, a conservator shall consider any
HB 2359 77
1 estate plan of the individual known or reasonably ascertainable to the
2 conservator and may examine the will or other donative, nominative or
3 appointive instrument of the individual.
4 (j) A conservator shall maintain insurance on the insurable real and
5 personal property of the individual subject to conservatorship, unless the
6 conservatorship estate lacks sufficient funds to pay for insurance or the
7 court finds:
8 (1) The property lacks sufficient equity; or
9 (2) insuring the property would unreasonably dissipate the
10 conservatorship estate or otherwise not be in the best interest of the
11 individual.
12 (k) A conservator has access to and authority over a digital asset of
13 the individual subject to conservatorship to the extent provided by the
14 revised uniform fiduciary access to digital assets act or court order.
15 (l) A conservator for an adult shall notify the court immediately if the
16 condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable of exercising
17 rights previously removed.

3 New Sec. 103. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment, and
4 whenever there is a significant change in circumstances or the conservator
5 seeks to deviate significantly from the existing conservator's plan, a
6 conservator shall file with the court a plan for protecting, managing,
7 expending and distributing the assets of the conservatorship estate. The
8 plan must be based on the needs of the individual subject to
9 conservatorship and take into account the best interest of the individual as
10 well as the individual's preferences, values and prior directions, to the
11 extent known to or reasonably ascertainable by the conservator. The
12 conservator shall include in the plan:
13 (1) A budget containing projected expenses and resources, including
14 an estimate of the total amount of fees the conservator anticipates charging
15 per year and a statement or list of the amount the conservator proposes to
16 charge for each service the conservator anticipates providing to the
17 individual;
18 (2) how the conservator will involve the individual in decisions about
19 management of the conservatorship estate;
20 (3) any step the conservator plans to take to develop or restore the
21 ability of the individual to manage the conservatorship estate; and
22 (4) an estimate of the duration of the conservatorship.
23 (b) A conservator shall give notice of the filing of the conservator's
24 plan under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to the
25 individual subject to conservatorship, any attorney representing the
26 individual subject to conservatorship, a person entitled to notice under
27 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any
28 other person the court determines. The notice must include a statement of
29 the right to object to the plan and must be given at the time of the filing.
30 (c) An individual subject to conservatorship and any person entitled
31 under subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the conservator's plan
32 may object to the plan in writing not later than 21 days after the filing.
33 (d) The court shall review the conservator's plan filed under
34 subsection (a) and determine whether to approve the plan or require a new
35 plan. In deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall consider an
36 objection under subsection (c) and whether the plan is consistent with the
37 conservator's duties and powers. The court shall review an initial
38 conservator's plan at the review hearing scheduled under section 93(e), and
39 amendments thereto. For subsequent conservator's plans, the court has
40 discretion whether to set the matter for hearing but may not approve the
41 plan until 30 days after the filing.
42 (e) After a conservator's plan under this section is approved by the
43 court, the conservator shall provide a copy of the plan to the individual
HB 2359 83
1 subject to conservatorship, any attorney representing the individual subject
2 to conservatorship, a person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and
3 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
4 determines.
5 New Sec. 104. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment, a
6 conservator shall prepare and file with the appointing court a detailed

9 far as information permits. The inventory shall include all of the property
10 and assets of the conservatorship estate, including any sources of regular
11 income to the estate, and information about how property is titled and any

23 determines.
24 New Sec. 105. (a) A conservator shall file with the court a report in a
