17 New Sec. 106. (a) The interest of an individual subject to
18 conservatorship in property included in the conservatorship estate is not
19 transferrable or assignable by the individual and is not subject to levy,
20 garnishment, or similar process for claims against the individual unless
21 allowed under section 110, and amendments thereto.
22 (b) If an individual subject to conservatorship enters into a contract
23 after having the right to enter the contract removed by the court, the
24 contract is void against the individual and the individual's property but is
25 enforceable against the person that contracted with the individual.
26 (c) A person other than the conservator that deals with an individual
27 subject to conservatorship with respect to property included in the
28 conservatorship estate is entitled to protection provided by law of this state
29 other than this act.
30 New Sec. 107. A transaction involving a conservatorship estate which
31 is affected by a substantial conflict between the conservator's fiduciary
32 duties and personal interests is voidable unless the transaction is
33 authorized by court order after notice to persons entitled to notice under
34 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order. A
35 transaction affected by a substantial conflict includes a sale, encumbrance
36 or other transaction involving the conservatorship estate entered into by
37 the conservator, an individual with whom the conservator resides, the
38 spouse, descendant, sibling, agent or attorney of the conservator, or a
39 corporation or other enterprise in which the conservator has a substantial
40 beneficial interest.
41 New Sec. 108. (a) A person that assists or deals with a conservator in
42 good faith and for value in any transaction, other than a transaction
43 requiring a court order under section 102, and amendments thereto, is
HB 2359 86
1 protected as though the conservator properly exercised any power in
2 question. Knowledge alone by a person that the person is dealing with a
3 conservator does not require the person to inquire into the existence of
4 authority of the conservator or the propriety of the conservator's exercise
5 of authority, but restrictions on authority stated in letters of office, or
6 otherwise provided by law, are effective as to the person. A person that
7 pays or delivers property to a conservator is not responsible for proper
8 application of the property.
9 (b) Protection under subsection (a) extends to a procedural
10 irregularity or jurisdictional defect in the proceeding leading to the
11 issuance of letters of office and does not substitute for protection for a
12 person that assists or deals with a conservator provided by comparable
13 provisions in law of this state other than this act relating to a commercial
14 transaction or simplifying a transfer of securities by a fiduciary.
15 New Sec. 109. (a) If an individual subject to conservatorship dies, the
16 conservator shall deliver to the district court any will of the individual that
17 is in the conservator's possession and inform the personal representative
18 named in the will if feasible. The conservator shall give notice of the
19 delivery of the will under this section to any person entitled to notice under
20 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
21 (b) On the death of an individual subject to conservatorship, the
22 conservator shall conclude the administration of the conservatorship estate
23 as provided in section 113, and amendments thereto.
24 New Sec. 110. (a) A conservator may pay a claim against the
25 conservatorship estate or the individual subject to conservatorship arising
26 before or during the conservatorship, on presentation and allowance in
27 accordance with the priorities under subsection (d). A claimant may
28 present a claim by:
29 (1) Sending or delivering to the conservator a statement in a record of
30 the claim, indicating its basis, the name and address of the claimant and
31 the amount claimed; or
32 (2) filing the claim with the court, in a form acceptable to the court,
33 and sending or delivering a copy of the claim to the conservator.
34 (b) A claim under subsection (a) is presented on receipt by the
35 conservator of the statement of the claim or the filing with the court of the
36 claim, whichever occurs first. A presented claim is allowed, if it is not
37 disallowed in whole or in part, by the conservator in a record sent or
38 delivered to the claimant not later than 60 days after its presentation.
39 Before payment, the conservator may change an allowance of the claim to
40 a disallowance in whole or in part, but not after allowance under a court
41 order or order directing payment of the claim. Presentation of a claim tolls
42 until 30 days after disallowance of the claim the running of a statute of
43 limitations that has not expired relating to the claim.
HB 2359 87
1 (c) A claimant whose claim under subsection (a) has not been paid
2 may petition the court to determine the claim at any time before it is barred
3 by a statute of limitations, and the court may order its allowance, payment
4 or security by encumbering property included in the conservatorship
5 estate. If a proceeding is pending against the individual subject to
6 conservatorship at the time of appointment of the conservator or is
7 initiated thereafter, the moving party shall give the conservator notice of
8 the proceeding if it could result in creating a claim against the
9 conservatorship estate.
10 (d) If a conservatorship estate is likely to be exhausted before all
11 existing claims are paid, the conservator shall distribute the estate in
12 money or in kind in payment of claims in the following order:
13 (1) Costs and expenses of administration;
14 (2) a claim of the federal or state government having priority under
15 law other than this act;
16 (3) a claim incurred by the conservator for support, care, education,
17 health or welfare previously provided to the individual subject to
18 conservatorship or an individual who is in fact dependent on the individual
19 subject to conservatorship;
20 (4) a claim arising before the conservatorship; and
21 (5) all other claims.
22 (e) Preference may not be given in the payment of a claim under
23 subsection (d) over another claim of the same class. A claim due and
24 payable may not be preferred over a claim not due unless:
25 (1) Doing so would leave the conservatorship estate without
26 sufficient funds to pay the basic living and healthcare expenses of the
27 individual subject to conservatorship; and
28 (2) the court authorizes the preference under section 102(a)(8), and
29 amendments thereto.
30 (f) If assets of a conservatorship estate are adequate to meet all
31 existing claims, the court, acting in the best interest of the individual
32 subject to conservatorship, may order the conservator to grant a security
33 interest in the conservatorship estate for payment of a claim at a future
34 date.
35 New Sec. 111. (a) Except as otherwise agreed by a conservator, the
36 conservator is not personally liable on a contract properly entered into in a
37 fiduciary capacity in the course of administration of the conservatorship
38 estate unless the conservator fails to reveal the conservator's representative
39 capacity in the contract or before entering into the contract.
40 (b) A conservator is personally liable for an obligation arising from
41 control of property of the conservatorship estate or an act or omission
42 occurring in the course of administration of the conservatorship estate only
43 if the conservator is personally at fault.
HB 2359 88
1 (c) A claim based on a contract entered into by a conservator in a
2 fiduciary capacity, an obligation arising from control of property included
3 in the conservatorship estate, or a tort committed in the course of
4 administration of the conservatorship estate may be asserted against the
5 conservatorship estate in a proceeding against the conservator in a
6 fiduciary capacity, whether or not the conservator is personally liable for
7 the claim.
8 (d) A question of liability between a conservatorship estate and the
9 conservator personally may be determined in a proceeding for accounting,
10 surcharge, or indemnification or another appropriate proceeding or action.
11 New Sec. 112. (a) The court may remove a conservator for failure to
12 perform the conservator's duties or other good cause and appoint a
13 successor conservator to assume the duties of the conservator.
14 (b) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether to remove a
15 conservator and appoint a successor on:
16 (1) Petition of the individual subject to conservatorship, conservator
17 or person interested in the welfare of the individual which contains
18 allegations that, if true, would support a reasonable belief that removal of
19 the conservator and appointment of a successor may be appropriate, but
20 the court may decline to hold a hearing if a petition based on the same or
21 substantially similar facts was filed during the preceding six months;
22 (2) communication from the individual subject to conservatorship,
23 conservator or person interested in the welfare of the individual which
24 supports a reasonable belief that removal of the conservator and
25 appointment of a successor may be appropriate;
26 (3) determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
27 interest of the individual subject to conservatorship; or
28 (4) determination by the court that the conservator's reports and
29 accountings are delinquent or deficient as filed.
30 (c) Notice of a petition under subsection (b)(1) or any hearing under
31 this section must be given to the individual subject to conservatorship, the
32 conservator, a person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and
33 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
34 determines.
35 (d) If the individual subject to conservatorship is not represented by
36 an attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the same conditions
37 as in section 88, and amendments thereto. The court shall award
38 reasonable attorney fees to the attorney as provided in section 42, and
39 amendments thereto.
40 (e) In selecting a successor conservator, the court shall follow the
41 priorities under section 92, and amendments thereto.
42 (f) Not later than 30 days after appointing a successor conservator,
43 the court or court's designee shall give notice of the appointment to the
HB 2359 89
1 individual subject to conservatorship and any person entitled to notice
2 under section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
3 New Sec. 113. (a) A conservatorship for a minor terminates on the
4 earliest of:
5 (1) A court order terminating the conservatorship;
6 (2) the minor becoming an adult except as provided in section 114,
7 and amendments thereto;
8 (3) emancipation of the minor; or
9 (4) death of the minor.
10 (b) A conservatorship for an adult terminates on order of the court or
11 when the adult dies.
12 (c) An individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator, or a
13 person interested in the welfare of the individual may petition for:
14 (1) Termination of the conservatorship on the ground that a basis for
15 appointment under section 83, and amendments thereto, does not exist or
16 termination would be in the best interest of the individual or for other good
17 cause; or
18 (2) modification of the conservatorship on the ground that the extent
19 of protection or assistance granted is not appropriate or for other good
20 cause.
21 (d) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether termination
22 or modification of a conservatorship is appropriate on:
23 (1) Petition under subsection (c) which contains allegations that, if
24 true, would support a reasonable belief that termination or modification of
25 the conservatorship may be appropriate, but the court may decline to hold
26 a hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts was
27 filed within the preceding six months;
28 (2) a communication from the individual subject to conservatorship,
29 conservator or person interested in the welfare of the individual which
30 supports a reasonable belief that termination or modification of the
31 conservatorship may be appropriate, including because the functional
32 needs of the individual or supports or services available to the individual
33 have changed;
34 (3) a report from a guardian or conservator which indicates that
35 termination or modification may be appropriate because the functional
36 needs or supports or services available to the individual have changed or a
37 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive
38 alternative is available; or
39 (4) a determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
40 interest of the individual.
41 (e) Notice of a petition under subsection (c) or of a hearing under this
42 section must be given to the individual subject to conservatorship, the
43 conservator, a person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and
HB 2359 90
1 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
2 determines.
3 (f) After the hearing, the court shall order termination unless it is
4 proven that a basis for appointment of a conservator under section 83, and
5 amendments thereto, continues to exist.
6 (g) The court shall modify the powers granted to a conservator if the
7 powers are excessive or inadequate due to a change in the abilities or
8 limitations of the individual subject to conservatorship, the individual's
9 supports or other circumstances.
10 (h) Unless the court otherwise orders for good cause, before
11 terminating a conservatorship, the court shall follow the same procedures
12 to safeguard the rights of the individual subject to conservatorship which
13 apply to a petition for conservatorship.
14 (i) An individual subject to conservatorship who seeks to terminate or
15 modify the terms of the conservatorship has the right to retain an attorney
16 to represent the individual in this matter. If the individual is not
17 represented by an attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the
18 same conditions as in section 88, and amendments thereto. The court shall
19 award reasonable attorney fees to the attorney as provided in section 42,
20 and amendments thereto.
21 (j) On termination of a conservatorship other than by reason of the
22 death of the individual subject to conservatorship, property of the
23 conservatorship estate passes to the individual. The order of termination
24 must direct the conservator to file a final report and petition for discharge
25 on approval by the court of the final report.
26 (k) On termination of a conservatorship by reason of the death of the
27 individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator promptly shall file a
28 final report and petition for discharge on approval by the court of the final
29 report. On approval of the final report, the conservator shall proceed
30 expeditiously to distribute the conservatorship estate to the individual's
31 estate or as otherwise ordered by the court. The conservator may take
32 reasonable measures necessary to preserve the conservatorship estate until
33 distribution can be made.
34 (l) The court shall issue a final order of discharge on the approval by
35 the court of the final report and satisfaction by the conservator of any other
36 condition the court imposed on the conservator's discharge.
37 (m) Not later than 30 days after entering an order under this section,
38 the court or the court's designee shall give notice of the order to the adult
39 subject to conservatorship and any person entitled to notice under section
40 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
41 New Sec. 114. (a) A conservatorship for a minor may be extended
42 beyond the minor's 18th birthday if the minor consents or the court finds by
43 clear and convincing evidence that substantial harm to the minor's interests
HB 2359 91
1 is otherwise likely. A conservatorship may be extended under this section
2 until the minor reaches the age of 21 and may be extended for two
3 additional two-year periods upon the same finding by the court or upon
4 consent of the minor. Consent to the extension of a conservatorship may be
5 withdrawn at any time.
6 (b) Any request to extend a minor conservatorship under this section
7 must be accompanied by:
8 (1) A description of the funds or assets of the minor's estate which the
9 conservator proposes to distribute to the minor over an extended period
10 following the minor's 18th birthday;
11 (2) the factual basis upon which the conservator alleges the need for
12 such an extended distribution plan; and
13 (3) a proposed conservator's plan that describes how the distribution
14 will occur.
15 (c) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent the minor as
16 provided in section 88, and amendments thereto.
17 (d) After a hearing, the court may extend a conservatorship for a
18 minor and grant to the conservator the authority to establish an extended
19 distribution plan if the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
20 (1) Substantial harm to the minor's interests is likely if the
21 conservatorship is not extended; and
22 (2) the plan approved by the court adequately provides for meeting
23 the expected needs of the minor from the minor's 18th birthday until the
24 final distribution of the funds or assets which the court authorizes to be set
25 aside or transferred from the estate are paid over to the minor, including
26 provisions for accelerated distribution in extraordinary circumstances,
27 which may require court approval.
28 (e) If the court orders a conservatorship for a minor to be extended
29 under this section, the court shall order the conservator to report any
30 expenditure or transfer of funds or assets from the minor's estate for the
31 purposes of effectuating an extended distribution plan within the
32 conservator's next accounting.
33 (f) The court may extend the conservatorship with regard to specific
34 funds or assets of the minor's estate, even though other funds or assets of
35 the minor's estate are paid over to the minor upon the minor's becoming 18
36 years of age.
37 (g) The minor shall be without the power, voluntarily or involuntarily,
38 to sell, mortgage, pledge, hypothecate, assign, alienate, anticipate, transfer
39 or convey any interest in the principal or the income from any funds or
40 assets of the minor's estate set aside or transferred to effectuate a plan for
41 extended distribution until such is actually paid to the minor.
42 New Sec. 115. (a) Unless a person required to transfer funds or other
43 property to a minor knows that a conservator for the minor has been
HB 2359 92
1 appointed or a proceeding is pending for conservatorship, the person may
2 transfer an amount or value not exceeding $25,000 in a 12-month period
3 to:
4 (1) A person that has care or custody of the minor and with whom the
5 minor resides;
6 (2) a guardian for the minor;
7 (3) a custodian under the uniform transfers to minors act; or
8 (4) a financial institution as a deposit in an interest-bearing account or
9 certificate solely in the name of the minor and shall give notice to the
10 minor of the deposit.
11 (b) A person that transfers funds or other property under this section
12 is not responsible for its proper application.
13 (c) A person that receives funds or other property for a minor under
14 subsection (a)(1) or (2) may apply it only to the support, care, education,
15 health or welfare of the minor, and may not derive a personal financial
16 benefit from it, except for reimbursement for necessary expenses. Funds
17 not applied for these purposes must be preserved for the future support,
18 care, education, health or welfare of the minor, and the balance, if any,
19 transferred to the minor when the minor becomes an adult or otherwise is
20 emancipated.
21 (d) Any accumulated balance under this section shall be subject to
22 other provisions of this act.
23 New Sec. 116. The parent of a minor has the right and responsibility
24 to hold in trust and manage for the minor's benefit all of the personal and
25 real property vested in such minor when the total of such property does not
26 exceed $25,000 in value, unless a guardian or conservator has been
27 appointed for the minor.
28 New Sec. 117. (a) Any court having either control over or possession

30 vested in a minor, shall have the discretion to authorize, without the
31 appointment of a conservator or the giving of bond, and notwithstanding

34 union, savings and loan association or any other investment account that
35 the court may authorize, payable either to a conservator, if one shall be
36 appointed for the minor, or to the minor upon attaining 18 years of age.

43 the court shall order that person to hold in trust and manage the minor's
HB 2359 93
1 estate for the minor's benefit.
2 New Sec. 118. Any court having either control over or possession of

12 New Sec. 119. (a) On receiving a petition for a guardianship for an
13 adult, a court may order a protective arrangement instead of guardianship
14 as a less restrictive alternative to guardianship.
15 (b) On receiving a petition for a conservatorship for an individual, a
16 court may order a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship as a
17 less restrictive alternative to conservatorship.
18 (c) A person interested in an adult's welfare, including the adult or a
19 conservator for the adult, may petition under sections 119 through 130,
20 and amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of
21 guardianship.
22 (d) The following persons may petition under sections 119 through
23 130, and amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of
24 conservatorship:
25 (1) The individual for whom the protective arrangement is sought;
26 (2) a person interested in the property, financial affairs or welfare of
27 the individual, including a person that would be affected adversely by lack
28 of effective management of property or financial affairs of the individual;
29 and
30 (3) the guardian for the individual.
31 New Sec. 120. (a) After the hearing on a petition under section 65,
32 and amendments thereto, for a guardianship or under section 119(b), and
33 amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship,
34 the court may issue an order under subsection (b) for a protective
35 arrangement instead of guardianship if the court finds by clear and
36 convincing evidence that:
37 (1) The respondent lacks the ability to meet essential requirements for
38 physical health, safety or self-care because the respondent is unable to
39 receive and evaluate information or make or communicate decisions, even
40 with appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
41 decision making; and
42 (2) the respondent's identified needs cannot be met by a less
43 restrictive alternative.
HB 2359 94
1 (b) If the court makes the findings under subsection (a), the court,
2 instead of appointing a guardian, may:
3 (1) Authorize or direct a transaction necessary to meet the
4 respondent's need for health, safety or care, including:
5 (A) A particular medical treatment or refusal of a particular medical
6 treatment;
7 (B) a move to a specified place of dwelling; or
8 (C) visitation between the respondent and another person;
9 (2) order supervised visitation with, or restrict access to the
10 respondent by, a specified person whose access places the respondent at
11 serious risk of physical, psychological or financial harm; and
12 (3) order other arrangements on a limited basis that are appropriate.

8 New Sec. 123. (a) On filing of a petition under section 119, and
9 amendments thereto, the court shall set a date, time and place for a hearing
10 on the petition.
11 (b) A copy of a petition under section 119, and amendments thereto,
12 and notice of a hearing on the petition must be served personally on the
13 respondent. The notice must inform the respondent of the respondent's
14 rights at the hearing, including the right to an attorney and to attend the
15 hearing. The notice must include a description of the nature, purpose and
16 consequences of granting the petition. The court may not grant the petition
17 if notice substantially complying with this subsection is not served on the
18 respondent. The court may order any of the following persons to serve the
19 notice upon the respondent:
20 (1) The petitioner or the attorney for the petitioner;
21 (2) the attorney appointed by the court to represent the respondent;
22 (3) any law enforcement officer; or
23 (4) any other person whom the court finds to be a proper person to
24 serve this notice.

29 respondent's welfare the court determines. Failure to give notice under this
30 subsection does not preclude the court from granting the petition.

32 sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, notice of a hearing on

15 (3) if the petitioner seeks an order related to the dwelling of the
16 respondent, visit the respondent's present dwelling and any dwelling in
17 which it is reasonably believed the respondent will live if the order is
18 granted;
19 (4) if a protective arrangement instead of guardianship is sought,
20 obtain information from any physician or other provider known to have
21 treated, advised or assessed the respondent's relevant physical or mental
22 condition, to the extent that such information has not already been
23 provided to the court;
24 (5) if a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is sought,
25 review financial records of the respondent, if relevant to the court liaison's
26 recommendation under subsection (e)(2); and
27 (6) investigate the allegations in the petition and any other matter
28 relating to the petition as directed by the court, including, but not limited
29 to, the respondent's family relationships, past conduct, the nature and
30 extent of any property or income of the respondent, whether the
31 respondent is likely to injure self or others and other matters as the court
32 may specify.
33 (e) A court liaison under this section promptly shall file a report with
34 the court at least 10 days prior to the hearing on the petition or other
35 hearing as directed by the court. Unless otherwise ordered by the court,
36 such report must include:
37 (1) To the extent relevant to the order sought, a summary of self-care,
38 independent-living tasks and financial-management tasks the respondent:
39 (A) Can manage without assistance or with existing supports;
40 (B) could manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive
41 services, technological assistance or supported decision making; and
42 (C) cannot manage;
43 (2) a recommendation regarding the appropriateness of the protective
HB 2359 100
1 arrangement sought and whether a less restrictive alternative for meeting
2 the respondent's needs is available;
3 (3) if the petition seeks to change the physical location of the
4 dwelling of the respondent, a statement whether the proposed dwelling
5 meets the respondent's needs and whether the respondent has expressed a
6 preference as to the respondent's dwelling;
7 (4) a statement whether the respondent is able to attend a hearing at
8 the location court proceedings typically are held;
9 (5) a statement whether the respondent is able to participate in a
10 hearing and which identifies any technology or other form of support that
11 would enhance the respondent's ability to participate; and
12 (6) any other matter the court directs.
13 (f) The costs of an investigation by a court liaison shall be assessed as
14 provided for in section 42, and amendments thereto.
15 New Sec. 125. (a) Unless the respondent in a proceeding under
16 sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, is represented by an
17 attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the respondent,
18 regardless of the respondent's ability to pay. The court shall give
19 preference in the appointment of an attorney to an attorney whom the
20 respondent has requested or to any attorney who has represented the
21 respondent in other matters if the court has knowledge of that prior
22 representation.
23 (b) An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding under
24 sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, shall:
25 (1) Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes;
26 (2) advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably
27 ascertainable; and
28 (3) if the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable,
29 advocate for the result that is the least restrictive alternative in type,
30 duration and scope, consistent with the respondent's interests.
31 (c) The court may appoint an attorney to represent a parent of a minor
32 who is the subject of a proceeding under sections 119 through 130, and
33 amendments thereto, if:
34 (1) The parent objects to the entry of an order for a protective
35 arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship;
36 (2) the court determines that counsel is needed to ensure that consent
37 to the entry of an order for a protective arrangement is informed; or
38 (3) the court otherwise determines the parent needs representation.
39 (d) An attorney representing the respondent shall interview the
40 respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to
41 understand:
42 (1) Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature,
43 purpose and effect of the proceeding, and the respondent's rights at the
HB 2359 101
1 hearing on the petition;
2 (2) determine the respondent's views about the order sought by the
3 petitioner; and
4 (3) inform the respondent that all costs and expenses of the
5 proceeding, including respondent's attorney fees, may be paid from the
6 respondent's assets.
7 New Sec. 126. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
8 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
9 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a protective
10 arrangement, the court shall order an examination and evaluation of the
11 respondent to be conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric
12 hospital, community mental health center, or community developmental
13 disability organization, or by a licensed physician, psychiatrist,
14 psychologist, physician assistant, nurse practitioner, social worker or other
15 professional appointed by the court who is qualified to evaluate the
16 respondent's alleged cognitive and functional abilities and limitations and
17 will not be advantaged or disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition
18 or otherwise have a conflict of interest.
19 (b) Unless otherwise specified by the court, the report of the
20 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:
21 (1) The respondent's name, age and date of birth;
22 (2) a description of the respondent's physical and mental condition;
23 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
24 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
25 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
26 (4) a summary of self-care and independent-living tasks the
27 respondent can manage without assistance or with existing supports, could
28 manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive services,
29 technological assistance or supported decision making, and cannot
30 manage;
31 (5) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
32 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;
33 (6) a list and description of any prior assessments, evaluations or
34 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
35 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;
36 (7) the date and location where this examination and evaluation
37 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals
38 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
39 qualifications;
40 (8) a statement by the professional that the professional has
41 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
42 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results
43 of that examination and evaluation, and the professional's opinion with
HB 2359 102
1 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
2 guardian and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance and
3 participation at the hearing on the petition; and
4 (9) the signature of the professional who prepared the report.
5 (c) The professional shall file with the court, at least five days prior to
6 the date of the trial, such professional's written report concerning the
7 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made
8 available by the court to counsel for all parties.
9 (d) In lieu of entering an order for an examination and evaluation as
10 provided for in this section, the court may determine that the report
11 accompanying the petition is in compliance with the requirements of this
12 section and that no further examination or evaluation should be required,
13 unless the respondent, or such person's attorney, requests such an
14 examination and evaluation in writing. Any such request shall be filed with
15 the court, and a copy thereof delivered to the petitioner, at least four days
16 prior to the date of the trial. Accompanying the request shall be a statement
17 of the reasons why an examination and evaluation is requested and the
18 name and address of a qualified professional or facility willing and able to
19 conduct this examination and evaluation. If the court orders a further
20 examination and evaluation, the court may continue the trial and fix a new
21 date, time and place of the trial at a time not to exceed 30 days from the
22 date of the filing of the request.
23 New Sec. 127. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
24 hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, may not
25 proceed unless the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably
26 feasible for the respondent to attend a hearing at the location where court
27 proceedings typically are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to
28 hold the hearing at an alternative location convenient to the respondent or
29 allow the respondent to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual
30 technology.
31 (b) A hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
32 thereto, may proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court
33 finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
34 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
35 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
36 of failing to do so;
37 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
38 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services and
39 technological assistance; or
40 (3) the respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and
41 attendance would be harmful to the minor.
42 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under sections 119
43 through 130, and amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the
HB 2359 103
1 respondent's choosing, assistive technology or an interpreter or translator,
2 or a combination of these supports. If assistance would facilitate the
3 respondent's participation in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to
4 the respondent, the court shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.
5 (d) The respondent has a right to retain an attorney to represent the
6 respondent at a hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
7 thereto.
8 (e) At a hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
9 thereto, the respondent may:
10 (1) Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents;
11 (2) examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and
12 the court liaison; and
13 (3) otherwise participate in the hearing.
14 (f) A hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
15 thereto, must be closed on request of the respondent and a showing of
16 good cause.
17 (g) Any person may request to participate in a hearing under sections
18 119 through 130, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the
19 request, with or without a hearing, on determining that the best interest of
20 the respondent will be served. The court may impose appropriate
21 conditions on the person's participation.
22 New Sec. 128. The court shall give notice of an order under sections
23 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, to the individual who is subject
24 to the protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship, a
25 person whose access to the individual is restricted by the order and any
26 other person the court determines.
27 New Sec. 129. (a) The existence of a proceeding for or the existence
28 of a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship is a
29 matter of public record unless the court seals the record after:
30 (1) The respondent, the individual subject to the protective
31 arrangement, or the parent of a minor subject to the protective arrangement
32 requests the record be sealed; and
33 (2) either:
34 (A) The proceeding is dismissed;
35 (B) the protective arrangement is no longer in effect; or
36 (C) an act authorized by the order granting the protective arrangement
37 has been completed.
38 (b) (1) An order of protective arrangement is a matter of public record
39 unless sealed by the court. All other court records of the proceeding
40 relating to the protective arrangement are not a matter of public record
41 except as further provided.
42 (2) The following persons may access court records of the proceeding
43 and resulting protective arrangement:
HB 2359 104
1 (A) A respondent;
2 (B) an individual subject to a protective arrangement instead of
3 guardianship or conservatorship;
4 (C) an attorney designated by the respondent or individual;
5 (D) a parent of a minor subject to a protective arrangement; and
6 (E) a licensed attorney, abstractor, or title insurance agent.
7 (3) A person not otherwise entitled to access to court records under
8 this subsection for good cause may request permission from the court for
9 access. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest of the
10 respondent or individual subject to the protective arrangement or furthers
11 the public interest and does not endanger the welfare or financial interests
12 of the respondent or individual.
13 (c) A report of a court liaison or professional evaluation generated in
14 the course of a proceeding under sections 119 through 130, and
15 amendments thereto, must be sealed on filing but is available to:
16 (1) The court;
17 (2) the individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation,
18 without limitation as to use;
19 (3) the petitioner, court liaison and petitioner's and respondent's
20 attorneys, for purposes of the proceeding;
21 (4) unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a
22 power of attorney for finances in which the respondent is the principal;
23 (5) if the order is for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship
24 and unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a power of
25 attorney for healthcare in which the respondent is identified as the
26 principal; and
27 (6) any other person if it is in the public interest or for a purpose the
28 court orders for good cause.
29 New Sec. 130. The court may appoint a facilitator to assist in
30 implementing a protective arrangement under sections 119 through 130,
31 and amendments thereto. The facilitator has the authority conferred by the
32 order of appointment and serves until discharged by court order.

34 develop a statement of rights form, petition forms and report and
35 accounting forms.
36 New Sec. 132. In applying and construing this uniform act,
37 consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law
38 with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.

42 U.S.C. § 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices

16 not be liable in any civil or criminal action for failure to obtain consent of
17 a parent.
18 (6) Nothing in this section shall be construed to mean that any person
19 shall be relieved of legal responsibility to provide care and support for a
20 child.
21 (b) Care and treatment requiring court action. If it is brought to the
22 court's attention, while the court is exercising jurisdiction over the person
23 of a child under this code, that the child may be a mentally ill person as
24 defined in K.S.A. 59-2946, and amendments thereto, or a person with an
25 alcohol or substance abuse problem as defined in K.S.A. 59-29b46, and
26 amendments thereto, the court may:
27 (1) Direct or authorize the county or district attorney or the person
28 supplying the information to file the petition provided for in K.S.A. 59-
29 2957, and amendments thereto, and proceed to hear and determine the
30 issues raised by the application as provided in the care and treatment act
31 for mentally ill persons or the petition provided for in K.S.A. 59-29b57,
32 and amendments thereto, and proceed to hear and determine the issues
33 raised by the application as provided in the care and treatment act for
34 persons with an alcohol or substance abuse problem; or
35 (2) authorize that the child seek voluntary admission to a treatment
36 facility as provided in K.S.A. 59-2949, and amendments thereto, or K.S.A.
37 59-29b49, and amendments thereto.
38 The application to determine whether the child is a mentally ill person
39 or a person with an alcohol or substance abuse problem may be filed in the
40 same proceedings as the petition alleging the child to be a child in need of
41 care, or may be brought in separate proceedings. In either event, the court
42 may enter an order staying any further proceedings under this code until
43 all proceedings have been concluded under the care and treatment act for
HB 2359 112
1 mentally ill persons or the care and treatment act for persons with an
2 alcohol or substance abuse problem.

9 Sec. 144. K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-656 is hereby amended to read as
10 follows: 58-656. (a) An attorney in fact who elects to act under a power of
11 attorney is under a duty to act in the interest of the principal and to avoid
12 conflicts of interest that impair the ability of the attorney in fact so to act.
13 A person who is appointed an attorney in fact under a power of attorney
14 who undertakes to exercise the authority conferred in the power of
15 attorney, has a fiduciary obligation to exercise the powers conferred in the
16 best interests of the principal, and to avoid self-dealing and conflicts of
17 interest, as in the case of a trustee with respect to the trustee's beneficiary
18 or beneficiaries. The attorney in fact shall keep a record of receipts,
19 disbursements and transactions made on behalf of the principal and shall
20 not comingle funds or assets of the principal with the funds or assets of the
21 attorney in fact. In the absence of explicit authorization, the attorney in
22 fact shall exercise a high degree of care in maintaining, without
23 modification, any estate plan which the principal may have in place,
24 including, but not limited to, arrangements made by the principal for
25 disposition of assets at death through beneficiary designations, ownership
26 by joint tenancy or tenancy by the entirety, trust arrangements or by will or
27 codicil. Unless otherwise provided in the power of attorney or in a separate
28 agreement between the principal and attorney in fact, an attorney in fact
29 who elects to act shall exercise the authority granted in a power of attorney
30 with that degree of care that would be observed by a prudent person
31 dealing with the property and conducting the affairs of another, except that
32 all investments made on or after July 1, 2003, shall be in accordance with
33 the provisions of the Kansas uniform prudent investor act, K.S.A. 58-
34 24a01 et seq., and amendments thereto. If the attorney in fact has special
35 skills or was appointed attorney in fact on the basis of representations of
36 special skills or expertise, the attorney in fact has a duty to use those skills
37 in the principal's behalf.
38 (b) On matters undertaken or to be undertaken in the principal's
39 behalf and to the extent reasonably possible under the circumstances, an
40 attorney in fact has a duty to keep in regular contact with the principal, to
41 communicate with the principal and to obtain and follow the instructions
42 of the principal.
43 (c) If, following execution of a durable power of attorney, a court of
HB 2359 118
1 the principal's domicile appoints a conservator, guardian of the estate or
2 other fiduciary charged with the management of all of the principal's
3 property or all of the principal's property except specified exclusions, the
4 attorney in fact is accountable to the fiduciary as well as to the principal.
5 The fiduciary has the same power to revoke or amend the durable power of
6 attorney that the principal would have had if the principal were not an
7 adult with an impairment in need of a guardian or conservator or both as
8 defined by subsection (a) of K.S.A. 59-3051 section 25, and amendments
9 thereto.
10 (d) A principal may nominate by a power of attorney, a guardian or
11 conservator, or both, for consideration by the court. If a petition to appoint
12 a guardian or conservator, or both, is filed, the court shall make the
13 appointment in accordance with the principal's most recent nomination in
14 the power of attorney, so long as the individual nominated is a fit and
15 proper person.
16 (e) An attorney in fact shall exercise authority granted by the
17 principal in accordance with the instrument setting forth the power of
18 attorney, any modification made therein by the principal or the principal's
19 legal representative or a court, and the oral and written instructions of the
20 principal, or the written instructions of the principal's legal representative
21 or a court.
22 (f) An attorney in fact may be instructed in a power of attorney that
23 the authority granted shall not be exercised until, or shall terminate on, the
24 happening of a future event, condition or contingency, as determined in a
25 manner prescribed in the instrument.
26 (g) On the death of the principal, the attorney in fact shall follow the
27 instructions of the court, if any, having jurisdiction over the estate of the
28 principal, or any part thereof, and shall communicate with and be
29 accountable to the principal's personal representative, or if none, the
30 principal's successors. The attorney in fact shall promptly deliver to and
31 put in the possession and control of the principal's personal representative
32 or successors, any property of the principal and copies of any records of
33 the attorney in fact relating to transactions undertaken in the principal's
34 behalf that are deemed by the personal representative or the court to be
35 necessary or helpful in the administration of the decedent's estate.
36 (h) If an attorney in fact has a property or contract interest in the
37 subject of the power of attorney or the authority of the attorney in fact is
38 otherwise coupled with an interest in a person other than the principal, this
39 section does not impose any duties on the attorney in fact that would
40 conflict or be inconsistent with that interest.

1 sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto.
2 (f) In addition to any other remedies available under law, if after

8 the authority granted by the durable power of attorney be suspended or

21 identifying the immediate relatives of the principal and any other persons

25 the court, but no such temporary order shall be effective for more than 30

27 persons identified as herein provided in this subsection.

43 uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other protective arrangements
HB 2359 121
1 act, sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto; and
2 (3) relieve the attorney in fact of any obligation to exercise authority
3 for a disabled principal under a durable power of attorney.
4 (i) Unless previously barred by adjudication, consent or limitation,
5 any cause of action against an attorney in fact or successor for breach of
6 duty to the principal shall be barred as to any principal who has received
7 an account or other statement fully disclosing the matter unless a
8 proceeding to assert the cause of action is commenced within two years
9 after receipt of the account or statement by the principal or, if the principal
10 is a disabled person, by a guardian or conservator of the disabled person's
11 estate. If a disabled person has no guardian or conservator of the disabled
12 person's estate at the time an account or statement is presented, then the
13 cause of action shall not be barred until one year after the removal of the
14 principal's disability or incapacity, one year after the appointment of a
15 conservator for the principal or one year after the death of the principal.
16 The cause of action thus barred does not include any action to recover
17 from an attorney in fact or successor for fraud, misrepresentation or
18 concealment related to the settlement of any transaction involving the

4 (a) "Discharge" means the final and complete release from treatment,
5 by either the head of a treatment facility acting pursuant to K.S.A. 59-
6 2950, and amendments thereto, or by an order of a court issued pursuant to
7 K.S.A. 59-2973, and amendments thereto.
8 (b) "Head of a treatment facility" means the administrative director of
9 a treatment facility or such person's designee.
10 (c) "Law enforcement officer" means the same as defined in K.S.A.
11 22-2202, and amendments thereto.
12 (d) (1) "Mental health center" means any community mental health
13 center as defined in K.S.A. 39-2002, and amendments thereto, or a mental
14 health clinic organized as a not-for-profit or a for-profit corporation
15 pursuant to K.S.A. 17-1701 through 17-1775, and amendments thereto, or
16 K.S.A. 17-6001 through 17-6010, and amendments thereto, and licensed in
17 accordance with the provisions of K.S.A. 39-2001 et seq., and
18 amendments thereto.
19 (2) "Participating mental health center" means a mental health center
20 that has entered into a contract with the secretary for aging and disability
21 services pursuant to the provisions of K.S.A. 39-1601 through 39-1612,
22 and amendments thereto.
23 (e) "Mentally ill person" means any person who is suffering from a
24 mental disorder that is manifested by a clinically significant behavioral or
25 psychological syndrome or pattern and associated with either a painful
26 symptom or an impairment in one or more important areas of functioning,
27 and involving substantial behavioral, psychological or biological
28 dysfunction, to the extent that the person is in need of treatment.
29 (f) (1) "Mentally ill person subject to involuntary commitment for
30 care and treatment" means a mentally ill person, as defined in subsection
31 (e), who also lacks capacity to make an informed decision concerning
32 treatment, is likely to cause harm to self or others, and whose diagnosis is
33 not solely one of the following mental disorders: Alcohol or chemical
34 substance abuse; antisocial personality disorder; intellectual disability;
35 organic personality syndrome; or an organic mental disorder.
36 (2) "Lacks capacity to make an informed decision concerning
37 treatment" means that the person, by reason of the person's mental
38 disorder, is unable, despite conscientious efforts at explanation, to
39 understand basically the nature and effects of hospitalization or treatment
40 or is unable to engage in a rational decision-making process regarding
41 hospitalization or treatment, as evidenced by an inability to weigh the
42 possible risks and benefits.
43 (3) "Likely to cause harm to self or others" means that the person, by
HB 2359 135
1 reason of the person's mental disorder: (A) Is likely, in the reasonably
2 foreseeable future, to cause substantial physical injury or physical abuse to
3 self or others or substantial damage to another's property, as evidenced by
4 behavior threatening, attempting or causing such injury, abuse or damage;
5 except that if the harm threatened, attempted or caused is only harm to the
6 property of another, the harm must be of such a value and extent that the
7 state's interest in protecting the property from such harm outweighs the
8 person's interest in personal liberty; or (B) is substantially unable, except
9 for reason of indigency, to provide for any of the person's basic needs,
10 such as food, clothing, shelter, health or safety, causing a substantial
11 deterioration of the person's ability to function on the person's own.
12 No person who is being treated by prayer in the practice of the religion
13 of any church that teaches reliance on spiritual means alone through prayer
14 for healing shall be determined to be a mentally ill person subject to
15 involuntary commitment for care and treatment under this act unless
16 substantial evidence is produced upon which the district court finds that
17 the proposed patient is likely in the reasonably foreseeable future to cause
18 substantial physical injury or physical abuse to self or others or substantial
19 damage to another's property, as evidenced by behavior threatening,
20 attempting or causing such injury, abuse or damage; except that if the harm
21 threatened, attempted or caused is only harm to the property of another, the
22 harm must be of such a value and extent that the state's interest in
23 protecting the property from such harm outweighs the person's interest in
24 personal liberty.
25 (g) "Patient" means a person who is a voluntary patient, a proposed
26 patient or an involuntary patient.
27 (1) "Voluntary patient" means a person who is receiving treatment at
28 a treatment facility pursuant to K.S.A. 59-2949, and amendments thereto.
29 (2) "Proposed patient" means a person for whom a petition pursuant
30 to K.S.A. 59-2952 or 59-2957, and amendments thereto, has been filed.
31 (3) "Involuntary patient" means a person who is receiving treatment
32 under order of a court or a person admitted and detained by a treatment
33 facility pursuant to an application filed pursuant to K.S.A. 59-2954(b) or
34 (c), and amendments thereto.
35 (h) "Physician" means a person licensed to practice medicine and
36 surgery as provided for in the Kansas healing arts act or a person who is
37 employed by a state psychiatric hospital or by an agency of the United
38 States and who is authorized by law to practice medicine and surgery
39 within that hospital or agency.
40 (i) "Psychologist" means a licensed psychologist, as defined by
41 K.S.A. 74-5302, and amendments thereto.
42 (j) "Qualified mental health professional" means a physician or
43 psychologist who is employed by a participating mental health center or
HB 2359 136
1 who is providing services as a physician or psychologist under a contract
2 with a participating mental health center, a licensed master's level
3 psychologist, a licensed clinical psychotherapist, a licensed marriage and
4 family therapist, a licensed clinical marriage and family therapist, a
5 licensed professional counselor, a licensed clinical professional counselor,
6 a licensed specialist social worker or a licensed master social worker or a
7 registered nurse who has a specialty in psychiatric nursing, who is
8 employed by a participating mental health center and who is acting under
9 the direction of a physician or psychologist who is employed by, or under
10 contract with, a participating mental health center.
11 (1) "Direction" means monitoring and oversight including regular,
12 periodic evaluation of services.
13 (2) "Licensed master social worker" means a person licensed as a
14 master social worker by the behavioral sciences regulatory board under
15 K.S.A. 65-6301 through 65-6318, and amendments thereto.
16 (3) "Licensed specialist social worker" means a person licensed in a
17 social work practice specialty by the behavioral sciences regulatory board
18 under K.S.A. 65-6301 through 65-6318, and amendments thereto.
19 (4) "Licensed master's level psychologist" means a person licensed as
20 a licensed master's level psychologist by the behavioral sciences regulatory
21 board under K.S.A. 74-5361 through 74-5373, and amendments thereto.
22 (5) "Registered nurse" means a person licensed as a registered
23 professional nurse by the board of nursing under K.S.A. 65-1113 through
24 65-1164, and amendments thereto.
25 (k) "Secretary" means the secretary for aging and disability services.
26 (l) "State psychiatric hospital" means Larned state hospital,
27 Osawatomie state hospital or Rainbow mental health facility.
28 (m) "Treatment" means any service intended to promote the mental
29 health of the patient and rendered by a qualified professional, licensed or
30 certified by the state to provide such service as an independent practitioner
31 or under the supervision of such practitioner.
32 (n) "Treatment facility" means any mental health center or clinic,
33 psychiatric unit of a medical care facility, state psychiatric hospital,
34 psychologist, physician or other institution or person authorized or
35 licensed by law to provide either inpatient or outpatient treatment to any
36 patient.
37 (o) The terms defined in K.S.A. 59-3051 section 25, and amendments
38 thereto, shall have the meanings provided by that section.

35 Sec. 166. K.S.A. 77-201 is hereby amended to read as follows: 77-
36 201. In the construction of the statutes of this state the following rules
37 shall be observed, unless the construction would be inconsistent with the
38 manifest intent of the legislature or repugnant to the context of the statute:
39 First. The repeal of a statute does not revive a statute previously
40 repealed, nor does the repeal affect any right which accrued, any duty
41 imposed, any penalty incurred or any proceeding commenced, under or by
42 virtue of the statute repealed. The provisions of any statute, so far as they
43 are the same as those of any prior statute, shall be construed as a
HB 2359 144
1 continuation of the prior provisions and not as a new enactment.
2 Second. Words and phrases shall be construed according to the context
3 and the approved usage of the language, but technical words and phrases,
4 and other words and phrases that have acquired a peculiar and appropriate
5 meaning in law, shall be construed according to their peculiar and
6 appropriate meanings.
7 Third. Words importing the singular number only may be extended to
8 several persons or things, and words importing the plural number only
9 may be applied to one person or thing. Words importing the masculine
10 gender only may be extended to females.
11 Fourth. Words giving a joint authority to three or more public officers
12 or other persons shall be construed as given that authority to a majority of
13 them, unless it is otherwise expressed in the act giving the authority.
14 Fifth. "Highway" and "road" include public bridges and may be
15 construed to be equivalent to "county way," "county road," "common
16 road," "state road" and "territorial road."
17 Sixth. "Incompetent person" includes disabled persons and
18 incapacitated persons as defined herein in this section.
19 Seventh. "Issue," as applied to the descent of estates, includes all the
20 lawful lineal descendants of the ancestor.
21 Eighth. "Land," "real estate" and "real property" include lands,
22 tenements and hereditaments, and all rights to them and interest in them,
23 equitable as well as legal.
24 Ninth. "Personal property" includes money, goods, chattels, evidences
25 of debt and things in action, and digital assets as defined in the revised
26 uniform fiduciary access to digital assets act, K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-4801
27 through 58-4819, and amendments thereto.
28 Tenth. "Property" includes personal and real property.
29 Eleventh. "Month" means a calendar month, unless otherwise
30 expressed. "Year" alone, and also the abbreviation "A.D.," is equivalent to
31 the expression "year of our Lord."
32 Twelfth. "Oath" includes an affirmation in all cases where an
33 affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in similar cases "swear"
34 includes affirm.
35 Thirteenth. "Person" may be extended to bodies politic and corporate.
36 Fourteenth. If the seal of a court or public office or officer is required
37 by law to be affixed to any paper, "seal" includes an impression of the seal
38 upon the paper alone, as well as upon wax or a wafer affixed to the paper.
39 "Seal" also includes both a rubber stamp seal used with permanent ink and
40 the word "seal" printed on court documents produced by computer
41 systems, so that the seal may be legibly reproduced by photographic
42 process.
43 Fifteenth. "State," when applied to the different parts of the United
HB 2359 145
1 States, includes the District of Columbia and the territories. "United
2 States" may include that district and those territories.
3 Sixteenth. "Town" may mean a civil township, unless a different
4 meaning is plainly intended.
5 Seventeenth. "Will" includes codicils.
6 Eighteenth. "Written" and "in writing" may include printing, engraving,
7 lithography and any other mode of representing words and letters,
8 excepting those cases where the written signature or the mark of any
9 person is required by law.
10 Nineteenth. "Sheriff" may be extended to any person performing the
11 duties of the sheriff, either generally or in special cases.
12 Twentieth. "Deed" is applied to an instrument conveying lands but does
13 not imply a sealed instrument. "Bond" and "indenture" do not necessarily
14 imply a seal but in other respects mean the same kind of instruments as
15 above. "Undertaking" means a promise or security in any form where
16 required by law.
17 Twenty-first. "Executor" includes an administrator where the subject
18 matter applies to an administrator.
19 Twenty-second. Roman numerals and Arabic figures are to be taken as a
20 part of the English language.
21 Twenty-third. "Residence" means the place which is adopted by a
22 person as the person's place of habitation and to which, whenever the
23 person is absent, the person has the intention of returning. When a person
24 eats at one place and sleeps at another, the place where the person sleeps
25 shall be considered the person's residence.
26 Twenty-fourth. "Usual place of residence" and "usual place of abode,"
27 when applied to the service of any process or notice, means the place
28 usually occupied by a person. If a person has no family, or does not have
29 family with the person, the person's office or place of business or, if the
30 person has no place of business, the room or place where the person
31 usually sleeps shall be construed to be the person's place of residence or
32 abode.
33 Twenty-fifth. "Householder" means a person who is 18 or more years of
34 age and who owns or occupies a house as a place of residence and not as a
35 boarder or lodger.
36 Twenty-sixth. "General election" refers to the election required to be
37 held on the Tuesday following the first Monday in November of each
38 even-numbered year.
39 Twenty-seventh. "Under legal disability" includes persons who are
40 within the period of minority, or who are incapacitated, incompetent or
41 imprisoned.
42 Twenty-eighth. When a person is required to be disinterested or
43 indifferent in acting on any question or matter affecting other parties,
HB 2359 146
1 relationship within the degree of second cousin, inclusive, shall disqualify
2 the person from acting, except by consent of parties.
3 Twenty-ninth. "Head of a family" shall include any person who has
4 charge of children, relatives or others living with the person.
5 Thirtieth. "Mentally ill person" means a mentally ill person as defined
6 in K.S.A. 59-2946, and amendments thereto.
7 Thirty-first. "Incapacitated person" means an individual whose ability
8 to receive and evaluate relevant information, or to effectively
9 communicate decisions, or both, even with the use of assistive
10 technologies or other supports, is impaired to the degree that the person
11 lacks the capacity to manage the person's estate, or to meet essential needs
12 for the person's physical health, safety or welfare, as defined in K.S.A. 59-
13 3051 section 25, and amendments thereto, whether or not a guardian or a
14 conservator has been appointed for that person.
15 Thirty-second. "Guardian" means an individual or a nonprofit
16 corporation certified in accordance with K.S.A. 59-3070 section 35, and
17 amendments thereto, which has been appointed by a court to act on behalf
18 of a ward and possessed of some or all of the powers and duties set out in
19 K.S.A. 59-3075 sections 76 through 78, and amendments thereto.
20 "Guardian" does not mean natural guardian unless specified.
21 Thirty-third. "Natural guardian" means both the biological or adoptive
22 mother and father of a minor if neither parent has been found to be an
23 adult with an impairment in need of a guardian or has had parental rights
24 terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction. If either parent of a minor
25 is deceased, or has been found to be an adult with an impairment in need
26 of a guardian, as provided for in K.S.A. 59-3050 through 59-3095 the
27 Kansas uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other protective
28 arrangements act, sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto, or
29 has had parental rights terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction,
30 then the other parent shall be the natural guardian, unless also deceased, or
31 found to be an adult with an impairment in need of a guardian, or has had
32 parental rights terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction, in which
33 case no person shall qualify as the natural guardian.
34 Thirty-fourth. "Conservator" means an individual or corporation
35 appointed by the court to act on behalf of a conservatee and possessed of
36 some or all of the powers and duties set out in K.S.A. 59-3078 sections 99
37 through 102, and amendments thereto.
38 Thirty-fifth. "Minor" means any person defined by K.S.A. 38-101, and
39 amendments thereto, as being within the period of minority.
40 Thirty-sixth. "Proposed ward" means a person for whom a petition for
41 the appointment of a guardian pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3058, 59-3059, 59-
42 3060 or 59-3061 sections 17, 18, 28, 49, 52 or 65, and amendments
43 thereto, has been filed.
HB 2359 147
1 Thirty-seventh. "Proposed conservatee" means a person for whom a
2 petition for the appointment of a conservator pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3058,
3 59-3059, 59-3060 or 59-3061 sections 17, 18, 28, 49, 52 or 65, and
4 amendments thereto, has been filed.
5 Thirty-eighth. "Ward" means a person who has a guardian.
6 Thirty-ninth. "Conservatee" means a person who has a conservator.
7 Fortieth. "Manufactured home" means a structure which:
8 (1) Is transportable in one or more sections which, in the traveling
9 mode, is 8 body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length,
10 or, when erected on site, is 320 or more square feet, and which is built on a
11 permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling, with or without
12 permanent foundation, when connected to the required utilities, and
13 includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning and electrical systems
14 contained therein; and
15 (2) is subject to the federal manufactured home construction and
16 safety standards established pursuant to 42 U.S.C. § 5403.
17 Forty-first. "Mobile home" means a structure which:
18 (1) Is transportable in one or more sections which, in the traveling
19 mode, is 8 body feet or more in width and 36 body feet or more in length
20 and is built on a permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling,
21 with or without a permanent foundation, when connected to the required
22 utilities, and includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning and electrical
23 systems contained therein; and
24 (2) is not subject to the federal manufactured home construction and
25 safety standards established pursuant to 42 U.S.C. § 5403.
26 Forty-second. "Disabled person" includes incapacitated persons and
27 incompetent persons as defined herein in this section.

Session of 2025
HOUSE BILL No. 2359
By Committee on Judiciary
Requested by Nancy Strouse on behalf of the Kansas Judicial Council.
2-7
1 AN ACT concerning guardians and conservators; enacting the uniform
2 adult guardianship and protective proceedings jurisdiction act and the
3 uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other protective
4 arrangements act; amending K.S.A. 9-1215, 17-2263, 17-2264, 21-
5 5417, 38-2217, 44-513a, 44-1601, 58-662, 58-24a15, 59-1701, 59-
6 2949, 59-2951, 59-2960, 59-29b49, 59-29b51, 73-507, 76-729, 76-
7 12b04 and 77-201 and K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-656, 58-4802, 58-4814,
8 58a-103, 59-2401a, 59-2946, 59-2948, 59-29b46, 59-29b48, 59-29b60,
9 59-29c03 and 75-652 and repealing the existing sections; also repealing
10 K.S.A. 59-2701, 59-2702, 59-2703, 59-2704, 59-2705, 59-2706, 59-
11 2707, 59-2708, 59-3050, 59-3054, 59-3057, 59-3063, 59-3064, 59-
