19
20 Be it enacted by the Legislature of the State of Kansas:
21 New Section 1. Sections 1 through 23, and amendments thereto, may
22 be cited as the uniform adult guardianship and protective proceedings
23 jurisdiction act (2007).
24 New Sec. 2. As used in this act:
25 (a) "Adult" means an individual who has attained 18 years of age or
26 an emancipated individual under 18 years of age.
27 (b) "Conservator" means a person appointed by the court to
28 administer the property of an adult, including a person appointed under
29 section 93, and amendments thereto.
30 (c) "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court to make
31 decisions regarding the person of an adult, including a person appointed
32 under section 72, and amendments thereto.
33 (d) "Guardianship order" means an order appointing a guardian.
34 (e) "Guardianship proceeding" means a judicial proceeding in which
35 an order for the appointment of a guardian is sought or has been issued.

HB 2359 2
1 (f) "Incapacitated person" means an adult for whom a guardian has
2 been appointed.
3 (g) "Party" means the respondent, petitioner, guardian, conservator or
4 any other person allowed by the court to participate in a guardianship or
5 protective proceeding.
6 (h) "Person," except in the term "incapacitated person" or "protected
7 person," means an individual, corporation, business trust, estate, trust,
8 partnership, limited liability company, association, joint venture, public
9 corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency or
10 instrumentality, or any other legal or commercial entity.
11 (i) "Protected person" means an adult for whom a protective order has
12 been issued.
13 (j) "Protective order" means an order appointing a conservator or
14 other order related to management of an adult's property.
15 (k) "Protective proceeding" means a judicial proceeding in which a
16 protective order is sought or has been issued.
17 (l) "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible
18 medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is
19 retrievable in perceivable form.
20 (m) "Respondent" means an adult for whom a protective order or the
21 appointment of a guardian is sought.
22 (n) "State" means a state of the United States, the District of
23 Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, a federally
24 recognized Indian tribe or any territory or insular possession subject to the
25 jurisdiction of the United States.
26 New Sec. 3. A court of this state may treat a foreign country as if it
27 were a state for the purpose of applying sections 1 through 17 and sections
28 21 through 23, and amendments thereto.
29 New Sec. 4. (a) A court of this state may communicate with a court in
30 another state concerning a proceeding arising under this act. The court may
31 allow the parties to participate in the communication. Except as otherwise
32 provided in subsection (b), the court shall make a record of the
33 communication. The record may be limited to the fact that the
34 communication occurred.
35 (b) Courts may communicate concerning schedules, calendars, court
36 records and other administrative matters without making a record.
37 New Sec. 5. (a) In a guardianship or protective proceeding in this
38 state, a court of this state may request the appropriate court of another state
39 to do any of the following:
40 (1) Hold an evidentiary hearing;
41 (2) order a person in that state to produce evidence or give testimony
42 pursuant to procedures of that state;
43 (3) order that an evaluation or assessment be made of the respondent;

HB 2359 3
1 (4) order any appropriate investigation of a person involved in a
2 proceeding;
3 (5) forward to the court of this state a certified copy of the transcript
4 or other record of a hearing under paragraph (1) or any other proceeding,
5 any evidence otherwise produced under paragraph (2) and any evaluation
6 or assessment prepared in compliance with an order under paragraph (3) or
7 (4);
8 (6) issue any order necessary to assure the appearance in the
9 proceeding of a person whose presence is necessary for the court to make a
10 determination, including the respondent or the incapacitated or protected
11 person; and
12 (7) issue an order authorizing the release of medical, financial,
13 criminal or other relevant information in that state, including protected
14 health information as defined in 45 C.F.R 160.103.
15 (b) If a court of another state in which a guardianship or protective
16 proceeding is pending requests assistance of the kind provided in
17 subsection (a), a court of this state has jurisdiction for the limited purpose
18 of granting the request or making reasonable efforts to comply with the
19 request.
20 New Sec. 6. (a) In a guardianship or protective proceeding, in
21 addition to other procedures that may be available, testimony of a witness
22 who is located in another state may be offered by deposition or other
23 means allowable in this state for testimony taken in another state. The
24 court on its own motion may order that the testimony of a witness be taken
25 in another state and may prescribe the manner in which and the terms upon
26 which the testimony is to be taken.
27 (b) In a guardianship or protective proceeding, a court in this state
28 may permit a witness located in another state to be deposed or to testify by
29 telephone or audiovisual or other electronic means. A court of this state
30 shall cooperate with the court of the other state in designating an
31 appropriate location for the deposition or testimony.
32 New Sec. 7. (a) As used in sections 7 through 15, and amendments
33 thereto:
34 (1) "Emergency" means a circumstance that likely will result in
35 substantial harm to a respondent's health, safety or welfare, and for which
36 the appointment of a guardian is necessary because no other person has
37 authority and is willing to act on the respondent's behalf;
38 (2) "home state" means the state in which the respondent was
39 physically present, including any period of temporary absence, for at least
40 six consecutive months immediately before the filing of a petition for a
41 protective order or the appointment of a guardian, or if none, the state in
42 which the respondent was physically present, including any period of
43 temporary absence, for at least six consecutive months ending within the

HB 2359 4
1 six months prior to the filing of the petition; and
2 (3) "significant-connection state" means a state, other than the home
3 state, with which a respondent has a significant connection other than mere
4 physical presence and in which substantial evidence concerning the
5 respondent is available.
6 (b) In determining under sections 9 and 16(e), and amendments
7 thereto, whether a respondent has a significant connection with a particular
8 state, the court shall consider:
9 (1) The location of the respondent's family and other persons required
10 to be notified of the guardianship or protective proceeding;
11 (2) the length of time the respondent at any time was physically
12 present in the state and the duration of any absence;
13 (3) the location of the respondent's property; and
14 (4) the extent to which the respondent has ties to the state such as
15 voting registration, state or local tax return filing, vehicle registration,
16 driver's license, social relationship and receipt of services.
17 New Sec. 8. Sections 7 through 15, and amendments thereto,
18 provides the exclusive jurisdictional basis for a court of this state to
19 appoint a guardian or issue a protective order for an adult.
20 New Sec. 9. A court of this state has jurisdiction to appoint a guardian
21 or issue a protective order for a respondent if:
22 (a) This state is the respondent's home state;
23 (b) on the date the petition is filed, this state is a significant-
24 connection state and:
25 (1) The respondent does not have a home state or a court of the
26 respondent's home state has declined to exercise jurisdiction because this
27 state is a more appropriate forum; or
28 (2) the respondent has a home state, a petition for an appointment or
29 order is not pending in a court of that state or another significant-
30 connection state, and, before the court makes the appointment or issues the
31 order:
32 (A) A petition for an appointment or order is not filed in the
33 respondent's home state;
34 (B) an objection to the court's jurisdiction is not filed by a person
35 required to be notified of the proceeding; and
36 (C) the court in this state concludes that it is an appropriate forum
37 under the factors set forth in section 12, and amendments thereto;
38 (c) this state does not have jurisdiction under either subsection (a) or
39 (b), the respondent's home state and all significant-connection states have
40 declined to exercise jurisdiction because this state is the more appropriate
41 forum and jurisdiction in this state is consistent with the constitutions of
42 this state and the United States; or
43 (d) the requirements for special jurisdiction under section 10, and

HB 2359 5
1 amendments thereto, are met.
2 New Sec. 10. (a) A court of this state lacking jurisdiction under
3 section 9(a), (b) or (c), and amendments thereto, has special jurisdiction to
4 do any of the following:
5 (1) Appoint a guardian in an emergency for a term not exceeding 90
6 days for a respondent who is physically present in this state;
7 (2) issue a protective order with respect to real or tangible personal
8 property located in this state;
9 (3) appoint a guardian or conservator for an incapacitated or protected
10 person for whom a provisional order to transfer the proceeding from
11 another state has been issued under procedures similar to section 16, and
12 amendments thereto.
13 (b) If a petition for the appointment of a guardian in an emergency is
14 brought in this state and this state was not the respondent's home state on
15 the date the petition was filed, the court shall dismiss the proceeding at the
16 request of the court of the home state, if any, whether dismissal is
17 requested before or after the emergency appointment.
18 New Sec. 11. Except as otherwise provided in section 10, and
19 amendments thereto, a court that has appointed a guardian or issued a
20 protective order consistent with this act has exclusive and continuing
21 jurisdiction over the proceeding until it is terminated by the court or the
22 appointment or order expires by its own terms.
23 New Sec. 12. (a) A court of this state having jurisdiction under
24 section 9, and amendments thereto, to appoint a guardian or issue a
25 protective order may decline to exercise its jurisdiction if it determines at
26 any time that a court of another state is a more appropriate forum.
27 (b) If a court of this state declines to exercise its jurisdiction under
28 subsection (a), it shall either dismiss or stay the proceeding. The court may
29 impose any condition the court considers just and proper, including the
30 condition that a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a
31 protective order be filed promptly in another state.
32 (c) In determining whether it is an appropriate forum, the court shall
33 consider all relevant factors, including:
34 (1) Any expressed preference of the respondent;
35 (2) whether abuse, neglect or exploitation of the respondent has
36 occurred or is likely to occur and which state could best protect the
37 respondent from the abuse, neglect or exploitation;
38 (3) the length of time the respondent was physically present in or was
39 a legal resident of this or another state;
40 (4) the distance of the respondent from the court in each state;
41 (5) the financial circumstances of the respondent's estate;
42 (6) the nature and location of the evidence;
43 (7) the ability of the court in each state to decide the issue

HB 2359 6
1 expeditiously and the procedures necessary to present evidence;
2 (8) the familiarity of the court of each state with the facts and issues
3 in the proceeding; and
4 (9) if an appointment were made, the court's ability to monitor the
5 conduct of the guardian or conservator.
6 New Sec. 13. (a) If at any time a court of this state determines that it
7 acquired jurisdiction to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order
8 because of unjustifiable conduct, the court may:
9 (1) Decline to exercise jurisdiction;
10 (2) exercise jurisdiction for the limited purpose of fashioning an
11 appropriate remedy to ensure the health, safety and welfare of the
12 respondent or the protection of the respondent's property or prevent a
13 repetition of the unjustifiable conduct, including staying the proceeding
14 until a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a
15 protective order is filed in a court of another state having jurisdiction; or
16 (3) continue to exercise jurisdiction after considering:
17 (A) The extent to which the respondent and all persons required to be
18 notified of the proceedings have acquiesced in the exercise of the court's
19 jurisdiction;
20 (B) whether it is a more appropriate forum than the court of any other
21 state under the factors set forth in section 12(c), and amendments thereto;
22 and
23 (C) whether the court of any other state would have jurisdiction under
24 factual circumstances in substantial conformity with the jurisdictional
25 standards of section 9, and amendments thereto.
26 (b) If a court of this state determines that it acquired jurisdiction to
27 appoint a guardian or issue a protective order because a party seeking to
28 invoke its jurisdiction engaged in unjustifiable conduct, it may assess
29 against that party necessary and reasonable expenses, including attorney
30 fees, investigative fees, court costs, communication expenses, witness fees
31 and expenses and travel expenses. The court may not assess fees, costs or
32 expenses of any kind against this state or a governmental subdivision,
33 agency or instrumentality of this state unless authorized by law other than
34 this act.
35 New Sec. 14. If a petition for the appointment of a guardian or
36 issuance of a protective order is brought in this state and this state was not
37 the respondent's home state on the date the petition was filed, in addition
38 to complying with the notice requirements of this state, notice of the
39 petition must be given to those persons who would be entitled to notice of
40 the petition if a proceeding were brought in the respondent's home state.
41 The notice must be given in the same manner as notice is required to be
42 given in this state.
43 New Sec. 15. Except for a petition for the appointment of a guardian

HB 2359 7
1 in an emergency or issuance of a protective order limited to property
2 located in this state under section 10(a)(1) or (2), and amendments thereto,
3 if a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a protective
4 order is filed in this state and in another state and neither petition has been
5 dismissed or withdrawn, the following rules apply:
6 (a) If the court in this state has jurisdiction under section 9, and
7 amendments thereto, it may proceed with the case unless a court in another
8 state acquires jurisdiction under provisions similar to section 9, and
9 amendments thereto, before the appointment or issuance of the order.
10 (b) If the court in this state does not have jurisdiction under section 9,
11 and amendments thereto, whether at the time the petition is filed or at any
12 time before the appointment or issuance of the order, the court shall stay
13 the proceeding and communicate with the court in the other state. If the
14 court in the other state has jurisdiction, the court in this state shall dismiss
15 the petition unless the court in the other state determines that the court in
16 this state is a more appropriate forum.
17 New Sec. 16. (a) A guardian or conservator appointed in this state
18 may petition the court to transfer the guardianship or conservatorship to
19 another state.
20 (b) Notice of a petition under subsection (a) must be given to the
21 persons that would be entitled to notice of a petition in this state for the
22 appointment of a guardian or conservator.
23 (c) On the court's own motion or on request of the guardian or
24 conservator, the incapacitated or protected person, or other person required
25 to be notified of the petition, the court shall hold a hearing on a petition
26 filed pursuant to subsection (a).
27 (d) The court shall issue an order provisionally granting a petition to
28 transfer a guardianship and shall direct the guardian to petition for
29 guardianship in the other state if the court is satisfied that the guardianship
30 will be accepted by the court in the other state and the court finds that:
31 (1) The incapacitated person is physically present in or is reasonably
32 expected to move permanently to the other state;
33 (2) an objection to the transfer has not been made or, if an objection
34 has been made, the objector has not established that the transfer would be
35 contrary to the interests of the incapacitated person; and
36 (3) plans for care and services for the incapacitated person in the
37 other state are reasonable and sufficient.
38 (e) The court shall issue a provisional order granting a petition to
39 transfer a conservatorship and shall direct the conservator to petition for
40 conservatorship in the other state if the court is satisfied that the
41 conservatorship will be accepted by the court of the other state and the
42 court finds that:
43 (1) The protected person is physically present in or is reasonably

HB 2359 8
1 expected to move permanently to the other state, or the protected person
2 has a significant connection to the other state considering the factors in
3 section 7(b), and amendments thereto;
4 (2) an objection to the transfer has not been made or, if an objection
5 has been made, the objector has not established that the transfer would be
6 contrary to the interests of the protected person; and
7 (3) adequate arrangements will be made for management of the
8 protected person's property.
9 (f) The court shall issue a final order confirming the transfer and
10 terminating the guardianship or conservatorship upon its receipt of:
11 (1) A provisional order accepting the proceeding from the court to
12 which the proceeding is to be transferred which is issued under provisions
13 similar to section 17, and amendments thereto; and
14 (2) the documents required to terminate a guardianship or
15 conservatorship in this state.
16 New Sec. 17. (a) To confirm transfer of a guardianship or
17 conservatorship transferred to this state under provisions similar to section
18 16, and amendments thereto, the guardian or conservator must petition the
19 court in this state to accept the guardianship or conservatorship. The
20 petition must include a certified copy of the other state's provisional order
21 of transfer.
22 (b) Notice of a petition under subsection (a) must be given to those
23 persons that would be entitled to notice if the petition were a petition for
24 the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a protective order in both the
25 transferring state and this state. The notice must be given in the same
26 manner as notice is required to be given in this state.
27 (c) On the court's own motion or on request of the guardian or
28 conservator, the incapacitated or protected person, or other person required
29 to be notified of the proceeding, the court shall hold a hearing on a petition
30 filed pursuant to subsection (a).
31 (d) The court shall issue an order provisionally granting a petition
32 filed under subsection (a) unless:
33 (1) An objection is made and the objector establishes that transfer of
34 the proceeding would be contrary to the interests of the incapacitated or
35 protected person; or
36 (2) the guardian or conservator is ineligible for appointment in this
37 state.
38 (e) The court shall issue a final order accepting the proceeding and
39 appointing the guardian or conservator as guardian or conservator in this
40 state upon its receipt from the court from which the proceeding is being
41 transferred of a final order issued under provisions similar to section 16,
42 and amendments thereto, transferring the proceeding to this state.
43 (f) Not later than 90 days after issuance of a final order accepting

HB 2359 9
1 transfer of a guardianship or conservatorship, the court shall determine
2 whether the guardianship or conservatorship needs to be modified to
3 conform to the law of this state.
4 (g) In granting a petition under this section, the court shall recognize
5 a guardianship or conservatorship order from the other state, including the
6 determination of the incapacitated or protected person's incapacity and the
7 appointment of the guardian or conservator.
8 (h) The denial by a court of this state of a petition to accept a
9 guardianship or conservatorship transferred from another state does not
10 affect the ability of the guardian or conservator to seek appointment as
11 guardian or conservator in this state under sections 24 through 135, and
12 amendments thereto, if the court has jurisdiction to make an appointment
13 other than by reason of the provisional order of transfer.
14 New Sec. 18. If a guardian has been appointed in another state and a
15 petition for the appointment of a guardian is not pending in this state, the
16 guardian appointed in the other state, after giving notice to the appointing
17 court of an intent to register, may register the guardianship order in this
18 state by filing as a foreign judgment in a court, in any appropriate county
19 of this state, certified copies of the order and letters of office.
20 New Sec. 19. If a conservator has been appointed in another state and
21 a petition for a protective order is not pending in this state, the conservator
22 appointed in the other state, after giving notice to the appointing court of
23 an intent to register, may register the protective order in this state by filing
24 as a foreign judgment in a court of this state, in any county in which
25 property belonging to the protected person is located, certified copies of
26 the order and letters of office and of any bond.
27 New Sec. 20. (a) Upon registration of a guardianship or protective
28 order from another state, the guardian or conservator may exercise in this
29 state all powers authorized in the order of appointment except as
30 prohibited under the laws of this state, including maintaining actions and
31 proceedings in this state and, if the guardian or conservator is not a
32 resident of this state, subject to any conditions imposed upon nonresident
33 parties.
34 (b) A court of this state may grant any relief available under this act
35 and other law of this state to enforce a registered order.
36 New Sec. 21. In applying and construing this uniform act,
37 consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law
38 with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.
39 New Sec. 22. This act modifies, limits or supersedes the electronic
40 signatures in global and national commerce act, 15 U.S.C. § 7001 et seq.,
41 but does not modify, limit or supersede section 101(c) of that act, 15
42 U.S.C. § 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices
43 described in section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. § 7003(b).

HB 2359 10
1 New Sec. 23. (a) This act applies to guardianship and protective
2 proceedings begun on or after January 1, 2026.
3 (b) Sections 1 through 6 and 16 through 22, and amendments thereto,
4 apply to proceedings begun before January 1, 2026, regardless of whether
5 a guardianship or protective order has been issued.
6 New Sec. 24. Sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto, may
7 be cited as the Kansas uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other
8 protective arrangements act.
9 New Sec. 25. As used in this act:
10 (a) "Adult" means an individual at least 18 years of age or an
11 emancipated individual under 18 years of age.
12 (b) "Adult subject to conservatorship" means an adult for whom a
13 conservator has been appointed under this act.
14 (c) "Adult subject to guardianship" means an adult for whom a
15 guardian has been appointed under this act.
16 (d) "Claim" includes a claim against an individual or conservatorship
17 estate, whether arising in contract, tort or otherwise.
18 (e) "Conservator" means a person appointed by a court to make
19 decisions with respect to the property or financial affairs of an individual
20 subject to conservatorship. "Conservator" includes a co-conservator.
21 (f) "Conservatorship estate" means the property subject to
22 conservatorship under this act.
23 (g) "Full conservatorship" means a conservatorship that grants the
24 conservator all powers available under this act.
25 (h) "Full guardianship" means a guardianship that grants the guardian
26 all powers available under this act.
27 (i) "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court to make
28 decisions with respect to the personal affairs of an individual. "Guardian"
29 includes a co-guardian but does not include a guardian ad litem.
30 (j) "Guardian ad litem" means a person appointed to inform the court
31 about, and to represent, the needs and best interest of an individual.
32 (k) "Individual subject to conservatorship" means an adult or minor
33 for whom a conservator has been appointed under this act.
34 (l) "Individual subject to guardianship" means an adult or minor for
35 whom a guardian has been appointed under this act.
36 (m) "Less restrictive alternative" means an approach to meeting an
37 individual's needs which restricts fewer rights of the individual than would
38 the appointment of a guardian or conservator. "Less restrictive alternative"
39 includes supported decision making, appropriate technological assistance,
40 appointment of a representative payee and appointment of an agent by the
41 individual, including appointment under a power of attorney for healthcare
42 or power of attorney for finances.
43 (n) "Letters of office" means a record issued by a court certifying a

HB 2359 11
1 guardian's or conservator's authority to act.
2 (o) "Limited conservatorship" means a conservatorship that grants the
3 conservator less than all powers available under this act, grants powers
4 over only certain property or otherwise restricts the powers of the
5 conservator.
6 (p) "Limited guardianship" means a guardianship that grants the
7 guardian less than all powers available under this act or otherwise restricts
8 the powers of the guardian.
9 (q) "Minor" means an unemancipated individual under 18 years of
10 age.
11 (r) "Minor subject to conservatorship" means a minor for whom a
12 conservator has been appointed under this act.
13 (s) "Minor subject to guardianship" means a minor for whom a
14 guardian has been appointed under this act.
15 (t) "Parent" does not include an individual whose parental rights have
16 been terminated.
17 (u) "Person" means an individual, estate, business or nonprofit entity,
18 public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency or
19 instrumentality or other legal entity.
20 (v) "Property" includes tangible and intangible property.
21 (w) "Protective arrangement instead of conservatorship" means a
22 court order entered under section 121, and amendments thereto.
23 (x) "Protective arrangement instead of guardianship" means a court
24 order entered under section 120, and amendments thereto.
25 (y) "Record," used as a noun, means information that is inscribed on a
26 tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is
27 retrievable in perceivable form.
28 (z) "Respondent" means an individual for whom appointment of a
29 guardian or conservator or a protective arrangement instead of
30 guardianship or conservatorship is sought.
31 (aa) "Sign" means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a
32 record:
33 (1) To execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or
34 (2) to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic
35 symbol, sound or process.
36 (bb) "Standby guardian" means a person appointed by the court under
37 section 57, and amendments thereto.
38 (cc) "State" means a state of the United States, the District of
39 Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands or any territory or
40 insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States. "State"
41 includes a federally recognized Indian tribe.
42 (dd) "Supported decision making" means assistance from one or more
43 persons of an individual's choosing in understanding the nature and

HB 2359 12
1 consequences of potential personal and financial decisions, which enables
2 the individual to make the decisions, and in communicating a decision
3 once made if consistent with the individual's wishes.
4 New Sec. 26. Unless displaced by a particular provision of this act,
5 the principles of law and equity supplement its provisions.
6 New Sec. 27. (a) Except to the extent jurisdiction is precluded by the
7 uniform child custody jurisdiction and enforcement act, K.S.A. 23-37,101
8 through 23-37,405, and amendments thereto, the district court has
9 jurisdiction over a guardianship for a minor domiciled or present in this
10 state. The court has jurisdiction over a conservatorship or protective
11 arrangement instead of conservatorship for a minor domiciled or having
12 property in this state.
13 (b) The district court has jurisdiction over a guardianship,
14 conservatorship or protective arrangement under section 120 or 121, and
15 amendments thereto, for an adult as provided in the uniform adult
16 guardianship and protective proceedings jurisdiction act, sections 1
17 through 23, and amendments thereto.
18 (c) After notice is given in a proceeding for a guardianship,
19 conservatorship or protective arrangement under section 120 or 121, and
20 amendments thereto, and until termination of the proceeding, the court in
21 which the petition is filed has:
22 (1) Exclusive jurisdiction to determine the need for the guardianship,
23 conservatorship or protective arrangement;
24 (2) exclusive jurisdiction to determine how property of the
25 respondent must be managed, expended or distributed to or for the use of
26 the respondent, an individual who is dependent in fact on the respondent or
27 other claimant;
28 (3) nonexclusive jurisdiction to determine the validity of a claim
29 against the respondent or property of the respondent or a question of title
30 concerning the property; and
31 (4) if a guardian or conservator is appointed, exclusive jurisdiction
32 over issues related to administration of the guardianship or
33 conservatorship.
34 (d) A court that appoints a guardian or conservator, or authorizes a
35 protective arrangement under section 120 or 121, and amendments thereto,
36 has exclusive and continuing jurisdiction over the proceeding until the
37 court terminates the proceeding or the appointment or protective
38 arrangement expires by its terms.
39 New Sec. 28. (a) This section does not apply to a guardianship or
40 conservatorship for an adult that is subject to the transfer provisions of
41 section 16 or 17, and amendments thereto.
42 (b) After appointment of a guardian or conservator, the court that
43 made the appointment may transfer the proceeding to a court in another

HB 2359 13
1 county in this state or another state if transfer is in the best interest of the
2 individual subject to the guardianship or conservatorship.
3 (c) If a proceeding for a guardianship or conservatorship is pending in
4 another state or a foreign country and a petition for guardianship or
5 conservatorship for the same individual is filed in a court in this state, the
6 court shall notify the court in the other state or foreign country and, after
7 consultation with that court, assume or decline jurisdiction, whichever is in
8 the best interest of the respondent.
9 (d) A guardian or conservator appointed in another state or country
10 may petition the court for appointment as a guardian or conservator in this
11 state for the same individual if jurisdiction in this state is or will be
12 established. The appointment may be made on proof of appointment in the
13 other state or foreign country and presentation of a certified copy of the
14 part of the court record in the other state or country specified by the court
15 in this state.
16 (e) Notice of hearing on a petition under subsection (d), together with
17 a copy of the petition, must be given to the respondent, if the respondent is
18 at least 12 years of age at the time of the hearing, and to the persons that
19 would be entitled to notice if the procedures for appointment of a guardian
20 or conservator under this act were applicable. The court shall make the
21 appointment unless it determines the appointment would not be in the best
22 interest of the respondent.
23 (f) Not later than 14 days after appointment under subsection (e), the
24 guardian or conservator shall give a copy of the order of appointment to
25 the individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship, if the individual
26 is at least 12 years of age, and to all persons given notice of the hearing on
27 the petition.
28 New Sec. 29. (a) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a
29 guardianship proceeding for a minor is in:
30 (1) The county in which the minor resides or is present at the time the
31 proceeding commences; or
32 (2) the county in which another proceeding concerning the custody or
33 parental rights of the minor is pending.
34 (b) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a guardianship
35 proceeding or protective arrangement instead of guardianship for an adult
36 is in:
37 (1) The county in which the respondent resides;
38 (2) if the respondent has been admitted to an institution by court
39 order, the county in which the court is located; or
40 (3) if the proceeding is for appointment of an emergency guardian for
41 an adult, the county in which the respondent is present.
42 (c) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a conservatorship
43 proceeding or protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is in:

HB 2359 14
1 (1) The county in which the respondent resides, whether or not a
2 guardian has been appointed in another county or other jurisdiction; or
3 (2) if the respondent does not reside in this state, in any county in
4 which property of the respondent is located.
5 (d) If proceedings under this act are brought in more than one county,
6 the court of the county in which the first proceeding is brought has the
7 exclusive right to proceed unless the court determines that venue is
8 properly in another court or the interest of justice otherwise requires
9 transfer of the proceeding.
10 (e) If proceedings under this act are brought in a county other than as
11 provided in subsections (a), (b) or (c), the court may determine that venue
12 is proper if it is in the best interest of the respondent and in the interest of
13 justice for the proceedings to take place in that county.
14 New Sec. 30. (a) The petitioner and the respondent shall each be
15 afforded an opportunity to appear at the trial, to testify and to present and
16 cross-examine witnesses. If the trial has been consolidated with a trial
17 being held pursuant to either the care and treatment act for mentally ill
18 persons or the care and treatment act for persons with an alcohol or
19 substance abuse problem, persons not necessary for the conduct of the
20 proceedings may be excluded as provided for in those acts. The trial shall
21 be conducted in as informal a manner as may be consistent with orderly
22 procedure. The court shall have the authority to receive all relevant and
23 material evidence which may be offered, including the testimony or
24 written report, findings or recommendations of any professional or other
25 person who has examined or evaluated the respondent and the testimony
26 and written findings and recommendations of any court liaison appointed
27 pursuant to section 67, and amendments thereto. Such evidence shall not
28 be privileged for the purpose of this trial.
29 (b) If proceedings for a guardianship, conservatorship or protective
30 arrangement under section 120 or 121, and amendments thereto, for the
31 same individual are commenced or pending in the same court, the
32 proceedings may be consolidated.
33 (c) A respondent may demand a jury trial in a proceeding under this
34 act on the issue of whether a basis exists for appointment of a guardian or
35 conservator.
36 New Sec. 31. (a) The court shall issue letters of office to a guardian
37 on filing by the guardian of:
38 (1) An acceptance of appointment;
39 (2) an oath or affirmation as required by K.S.A. 59-1702, and
40 amendments thereto;
41 (3) evidence of completion of a basic instructional program
42 concerning the duties and responsibilities of a guardian; and
43 (4) a personal information sheet containing any personal identifying

HB 2359 15
1 information about the guardian required by the court. Such information
2 shall not be disclosed to the public.
3 (b) The court shall issue letters of office to a conservator on filing by
4 the conservator of:
5 (1) An acceptance of appointment;
6 (2) an oath or affirmation as required by K.S.A. 59-1702, and
7 amendments thereto;
8 (3) any required bond or compliance with any other asset-protection
9 arrangement required by the court;
10 (4) evidence of completion of a basic instructional program
11 concerning the duties and responsibilities of a conservator; and
12 (5) a personal information sheet containing any personal identifying
13 information about the conservator required by the court. Such information
14 shall not be disclosed to the public.
15 (c) Limitations on the powers of a guardian or conservator or on the
16 property subject to conservatorship must be stated on the letters of office.
17 If the court appoints co-guardians or co-conservators, the letters of office
18 must specify whether such co-guardians or co-conservators may act
19 independently, whether they must act jointly, or under what circumstances
20 or with regard to what matters they may act independently or must act
21 jointly.
22 (d) The court at any time may limit the powers conferred on a
23 guardian or conservator. The court shall issue new letters of office to
24 reflect the limitation. The court shall give notice of the limitation to the
25 guardian or conservator, individual subject to guardianship or
26 conservatorship, each parent of a minor subject to guardianship or
27 conservatorship and any other person the court determines.
28 (e) The judicial council shall prepare a basic instructional program
29 concerning the duties and responsibilities of a guardian and a conservator.
30 The court shall have the authority to require any guardian or conservator
31 appointed prior to January 1, 2026, to complete the basic instructional
32 program and provide evidence thereof to the court.
33 New Sec. 32. (a) On acceptance of appointment, a guardian or
34 conservator submits to personal jurisdiction of the court in this state in any
35 proceeding relating to the guardianship or conservatorship.
36 (b) Every guardian or conservator that resides outside the state of
37 Kansas shall appoint a resident agent by executing an appointment of
38 resident agent that specifically identifies the person or entity that will act
39 as the resident agent. A resident agent may be either:
40 (1) An individual resident in this state; or
41 (2) a corporation, limited partnership, limited liability partnership,
42 limited liability company or business trust that has its principal place of
43 business in this state.

HB 2359 16
1 (c) Every resident agent for a guardian or conservator shall:
2 (1) Maintain contact with and remain aware of the current address

4 (2) accept service of process and other communications directed to
5 the guardian or conservator; and
6 (3) forward to the guardian or conservator documents sent by the

13 (e) For purposes of this section, the terms guardian and conservator

17 New Sec. 33. (a) The court at any time may appoint a co-guardian or

25 New Sec. 34. (a) The court at any time may appoint a successor
26 guardian or successor conservator to serve immediately or when a
27 designated event occurs, including the absence, impairment, resignation or
28 death of the guardian or conservator.
29 (b) A person entitled under section 52 or 65, and amendments thereto,
30 to petition the court to appoint a guardian may petition the court to appoint
31 a successor guardian. A person entitled under section 84, and amendments
32 thereto, to petition the court to appoint a conservator may petition the court
33 to appoint a successor conservator.
34 (c) A successor guardian or successor conservator appointed to serve
35 when a designated event occurs may act as guardian or conservator when:
36 (1) The event occurs; and
37 (2) the successor complies with section 31(a) or (b), and amendments
38 thereto, respectively.
39 (d) A successor guardian or successor conservator has the
40 predecessor's powers unless otherwise provided by the court.
41 New Sec. 35. (a) Any corporation organized under the Kansas general
42 corporation code may act as guardian for an individual found to be in need
43 of a guardian under the Kansas uniform guardianship, conservatorship and

HB 2359 17
1 other protective arrangements act, sections 24 through 135, and
2 amendments thereto, if the corporation has been certified by the secretary
3 for children and families as a suitable agency to perform the duties of a
4 guardian.
5 (b) The secretary for children and families shall establish criteria for
6 determining whether a corporation should be certified as a suitable agency
7 to perform the duties of a guardian. The criteria shall be designed for the
8 protection of the ward and shall include, but not be limited to, the
9 following:
10 (1) Whether the corporation is capable of performing the duties of a
11 guardian;
12 (2) whether the staff of the corporation is accessible and available to
13 wards and to other persons concerned about their well-being and is
14 adequate in number to properly perform the duties and responsibilities of a
15 guardian;
16 (3) whether the corporation is a stable organization which is likely to
17 continue in existence for some time; and
18 (4) whether the corporation will agree to submit such reports and
19 answer such questions as the secretary may require in monitoring
20 corporate guardianships.
21 (c) Application for certification under this section shall be made to
22 the secretary for children and families in such manner as the secretary may
23 direct. The secretary for children and families may suspend or revoke
24 certification of a corporation under this section, after notice and hearing,
25 upon a finding that such corporation has failed to comply with the criteria
26 established by rules and regulations under subsection (b). Such corporation
27 shall not be appointed as a guardian during the period of time the
28 certificate is suspended or revoked.
29 (d) No corporation shall be eligible for appointment as provided for
30 in sections 55 and 71, and amendments thereto, as the guardian of any
31 person if such corporation provides care, treatment or housing to that
32 person or is the owner, part owner or operator of any adult care home,
33 lodging establishment or institution utilized for the care, treatment or
34 housing of that person.
35 (e) The secretary for children and families may adopt rules and
36 regulations necessary to administer the provisions of this section.
37 New Sec. 36. (a) Appointment of a guardian or conservator
38 terminates on the death or removal of the guardian or conservator, or when
39 the court under subsection (b) approves a resignation of the guardian or
40 conservator.
41 (b) A guardian or conservator must petition the court for approval to
42 resign. The petition may include a request that the court appoint a
43 successor. Notice of the petition must be given to the person subject to

HB 2359 18
1 guardianship or conservatorship and any other person the court
2 determines. Resignation of a guardian or conservator is effective on the
3 date the resignation is approved by the court.
4 (c) Death, removal or resignation of a guardian or conservator does
5 not affect liability for a previous act or the obligation to account for:
6 (1) An action taken on behalf of the individual subject to
7 guardianship or conservatorship; or
8 (2) the individual's funds or other property.
9 New Sec. 37. (a) Except as otherwise provided in sections 53, 57, 66,
10 85 and 123, and amendments thereto, if notice of a hearing under this act
11 is required, the movant shall give notice of the date, time and place of the
12 hearing to the person to be notified unless otherwise ordered by the court
13 for good cause. Except as otherwise provided in this act, notice must be
14 given in compliance with K.S.A. 59-2208, and amendments thereto, at
15 least 14 days before the hearing.
16 (b) Proof of notice of a hearing under this act must be made before or
17 at the hearing and filed in the proceeding.
18 (c) Notice of a hearing under this act must be in at least 16-point font,
19 in plain language, and, to the extent feasible, in a language in which the

21 New Sec. 38. A respondent, individual subject to guardianship,
22 individual subject to conservatorship or individual subject to a protective
23 arrangement under section 120 or 121, and amendments thereto, may not
24 waive notice under this act. Any other person may waive notice in a record
25 signed by the person or person's attorney and filed in the proceeding.
26 New Sec. 39. The court at any time may appoint a guardian ad litem
27 for an individual if the court determines the individual's interest otherwise
28 would not be adequately represented. If no conflict of interest exists, a
29 guardian ad litem may be appointed to represent multiple individuals or
30 interests. The guardian ad litem may not be the same individual as the
31 attorney representing the respondent. The court shall state the duties of the
32 guardian ad litem and the reasons for the appointment in the order of
33 appointment.

35 under this act if the person is:
36 (1) Not otherwise entitled to notice; and

38 guardianship or conservatorship or individual subject to a protective
39 arrangement under section 120 or 121, and amendments thereto.
40 (b) A request under subsection (a) must include a statement showing
41 the interest of the person making the request and the address of the person

1 give notice of the approval to the guardian or conservator, if one has been

4 New Sec. 41. (a) Before accepting appointment as a guardian or
5 conservator, a person shall disclose to the court whether the person:
6 (1) Is or has been a debtor in a bankruptcy, insolvency or receivership
7 proceeding;
8 (2) has been convicted of:
9 (A) A felony;
10 (B) a crime involving dishonesty, neglect, violence or use of physical
11 force; or
12 (C) other crime relevant to the functions the individual would assume
13 as guardian or conservator;
14 (3) has committed an act of physical, mental or emotional abuse or
15 neglect or sexual abuse as validated by the Kansas department for children
16 and families pursuant to K.S.A. 38-2226, and amendments thereto; or
17 (4) has been found to have committed an act of abuse, neglect or
18 exploitation of an adult as contained in the register of reports under K.S.A.
19 39-1434, and amendments thereto.
20 (b) A guardian or conservator that engages or anticipates engaging a
21 service provider the guardian or conservator knows has been convicted of
22 a felony, a crime involving dishonesty, neglect, violence or use of physical
23 force, or other crime relevant to the functions the service provider is being
24 engaged to perform promptly shall disclose that knowledge to the court in
25 writing.
26 (c) If a conservator engages or anticipates engaging a service provider
27 under section 47, and amendments thereto, to manage finances of the
28 individual subject to conservatorship and knows the service provider is or
29 has been a debtor in a bankruptcy, insolvency or receivership proceeding,
30 the conservator promptly shall disclose that knowledge to the court in
31 writing.
32 New Sec. 42. (a) Unless otherwise compensated or reimbursed, an

38 subject to guardianship or conservatorship or for whom a protective
39 arrangement under section 120 or 121, and amendments thereto, was

42 (c) The court must approve compensation and expenses payable
43 under this section before payment. Approval is not required before a

HB 2359 20
1 service is provided or an expense is incurred. The costs may be taxed to
2 the property of the respondent or individual subject to guardianship or

29 department for children and families as to the residence of the respondent
30 or person subject to guardianship or conservatorship shall be applicable
31 only to the assessment of costs. Any county of residence which pays from

39 New Sec. 43. (a) Subject to court approval, a guardian is entitled to
40 reasonable compensation for services as guardian and to reimbursement
41 for room, board, clothing and other appropriate expenses advanced for the
42 benefit of the individual subject to guardianship.
43 (b) Subject to court approval, a conservator is entitled to reasonable

HB 2359 21
1 compensation for services and reimbursement for appropriate expenses
2 from the property of the individual subject to conservatorship.
3 (c) In determining reasonable compensation for a guardian or
4 conservator, the court, or a conservator in determining reasonable
5 compensation for a guardian as provided in subsection (a), shall consider:
6 (1) The necessity and quality of the services provided;
7 (2) the experience, training, professional standing and skills of the
8 guardian or conservator;
9 (3) the difficulty of the services performed, including the degree of
10 skill and care required;
11 (4) the conditions and circumstances under which a service was
12 performed, including whether the service was provided outside regular
13 business hours or under dangerous or extraordinary conditions;
14 (5) the effect of the services on the individual subject to guardianship
15 or conservatorship;
16 (6) the extent to which the services provided were or were not
17 consistent with the guardian's plan under section 79, and amendments
18 thereto, or conservator's plan under section 103, and amendments thereto;
19 and
20 (7) the fees customarily paid to a person that performs a like service
21 in the community.
22 (d) A guardian or conservator need not use personal funds of the
23 guardian or conservator for the expenses of the individual subject to
24 guardianship or conservatorship.
25 (e) If an individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship seeks
26 to modify or terminate the guardianship or conservatorship or remove the
27 guardian or conservator, the court may order compensation to the guardian
28 or conservator for time spent opposing modification, termination or
29 removal only to the extent the court determines the opposition was
30 reasonably necessary to protect the interest of the individual subject to
31 guardianship or conservatorship.
32 (f) Nothing in this section shall prohibit a guardian or a conservator
33 associated with the Kansas guardianship program from receiving a stipend
34 from that program.
35 New Sec. 44. A guardian or conservator is not personally liable to
36 another person solely because of the guardianship or conservatorship for
37 an act or omission of the individual subject to guardianship or
38 conservatorship.

1 conservatorship.
2 (c) On notice and hearing on a petition under subsection (a), the court
3 may give an instruction and issue an appropriate order.
4 New Sec. 46. (a) A person must recognize the authority of a guardian
5 or conservator to act on behalf of an individual subject to guardianship or
6 conservatorship unless:
7 (1) The person has actual knowledge or a reasonable belief that the
8 letters of office of the guardian or conservator are invalid or the
9 conservator or guardian is exceeding or improperly exercising authority
10 granted by the court;
11 (2) the person has actual knowledge that the individual subject to
12 guardianship or conservatorship is subject to physical or financial abuse,
13 neglect, exploitation or abandonment by the guardian or conservator or a
14 person acting for or with the guardian or conservator; or
15 (3) the person makes, or has actual knowledge that another person
16 has made, a report under K.S.A. 39-1402 or 39-1431, and amendments
17 thereto, stating a good-faith belief that the individual subject to
18 guardianship or conservatorship is subject to physical or financial abuse,
19 neglect, exploitation or abandonment by the guardian or conservator or a
20 person acting for or with the guardian or conservator.
21 (b) A person that refuses to accept the authority of a guardian or
22 conservator must, within 10 days of the refusal, report the refusal and the
23 reason for refusal to the court. Upon receiving the report, the clerk of the
24 district court shall forward the report to the presiding judge who shall
25 consider whether further action is appropriate. A report of a refusal under
26 this section shall be treated in the same manner as a grievance under
27 section 50, and amendments thereto.
28 (c) A guardian or conservator may petition the court to require a third
29 party to accept a decision made by the guardian or conservator on behalf
30 of the individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship.
31 New Sec. 47. (a) A guardian or conservator may retain a third person
32 to provide any service to an individual subject to guardianship or
33 conservatorship if retaining such third person, hereinafter referred to as a
34 service provider, is consistent with the guardian's or conservator's fiduciary
35 duties and the guardian's plan under section 79, and amendments thereto,
36 or conservator's plan under section 103, and amendments thereto.
37 (b) In retaining a service provider under subsection (a), the guardian
38 or conservator shall exercise reasonable care, skill and caution in:
39 (1) Selecting the service provider;
40 (2) establishing the scope and terms of the service provider's work in
41 accordance with the guardian's plan under section 79, and amendments
42 thereto, or the conservator's plan under section 103, and amendments
43 thereto;

HB 2359 23
1 (3) monitoring the service provider's performance and compliance
2 with the scope and terms of work; and
3 (4) redressing an act or omission of the service provider which would
4 constitute a breach of the guardian's or conservator's duties if done by the
5 guardian or conservator.
6 (c) In providing services under this section, a service provider shall
7 exercise reasonable care to comply with the scope and terms of the work
8 and use reasonable care in the performance of the work.
9 (d) A service provider who agrees to provide services under
10 subsection (a) submits to the personal jurisdiction of the courts of this state
11 in an action involving the service provider's performance.
12 (e) A guardian or conservator that retains and monitors a service
13 provider in compliance with this section is not liable for the decision, act
14 or omission of the service provider.
15 New Sec. 48. (a) The court may appoint a temporary substitute
16 guardian for an individual subject to guardianship for a period not
17 exceeding six months if:
18 (1) A proceeding to remove a guardian for the individual is pending;
19 or
20 (2) the court finds a guardian is not effectively performing the
21 guardian's duties and the welfare of the individual requires immediate
22 action.
23 (b) The court may appoint a temporary substitute conservator for an
24 individual subject to conservatorship for a period not exceeding six
25 months if:
26 (1) A proceeding to remove a conservator for the individual is
27 pending; or
28 (2) the court finds that a conservator for the individual is not
29 effectively performing the conservator's duties and the welfare of the
30 individual or the conservatorship estate requires immediate action.
31 (c) Except as otherwise ordered by the court, a temporary substitute
32 guardian or temporary substitute conservator appointed under this section
33 has the powers stated in the order of appointment of the guardian or
34 conservator. The authority of the existing guardian or conservator is
35 suspended for as long as the temporary substitute guardian or conservator
36 has authority.
37 (d) (1) The court shall give notice of appointment of a temporary
38 substitute guardian or temporary substitute conservator, not later than five
39 days after the appointment, to:
40 (A) The individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship;
41 (B) the affected guardian or conservator; and
42 (C) in the case of a minor, each parent of the minor and any person
43 currently having care or custody of the minor.

HB 2359 24
1 (2) If the individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship is not
2 represented by an attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the
3 same conditions as in sections 54 and 68, and amendments thereto. The
4 court shall set the matter for hearing if any person entitled to notice so
5 requests.
6 (e) The court may remove a temporary substitute guardian or
7 temporary substitute conservator at any time. The temporary substitute
8 guardian or temporary substitute conservator shall make any report the
9 court requires.
10 New Sec. 49. (a) If a guardian has been appointed in another state for
11 an individual, and a petition for guardianship for the individual is not
12 pending in this state, the guardian appointed in the other state, after giving
13 notice to the appointing court, may register the guardianship order in this
14 state by filing as a foreign judgment, in a court of an appropriate county of
15 this state, certified copies of the order and letters of office.
16 (b) If a conservator has been appointed in another state for an
17 individual, and a petition for conservatorship for the individual is not
18 pending in this state, the conservator appointed for the individual in the
19 other state, after giving notice to the appointing court, may register the
20 conservatorship in this state by filing as a foreign judgment, in a court of a
21 county in which property belonging to the individual subject to
22 conservatorship is located, certified copies of the order of conservatorship,
23 letters of office and any bond or other asset-protection arrangement
24 required by the court.
25 (c) On registration under this section of a guardianship or
26 conservatorship order from another state, the guardian or conservator may
27 exercise in this state all powers authorized in the order except as
28 prohibited by this act and law of this state other than this act. If the
29 guardian or conservator is not a resident of this state, the guardian or
30 conservator may maintain an action or proceeding in this state subject to
31 any condition imposed by this state on an action or proceeding by a
32 nonresident party.
33 (d) The court may grant any relief available under this act and law of
34 this state other than this act to enforce an order registered under this
35 section. However, absent a transfer pursuant to section 28, and
36 amendments thereto, jurisdiction remains with the court that established
37 the guardianship or conservatorship.
38 New Sec. 50. (a) An individual who is subject to guardianship or
39 conservatorship, or person interested in the welfare of an individual
40 subject to guardianship or conservatorship, who reasonably believes the
41 guardian or conservator is breaching the guardian's or conservator's
42 fiduciary duty or otherwise acting in a manner inconsistent with this act
43 may file a grievance in a record with the court. The clerk of the district

HB 2359 25
1 court shall forward the grievance to the presiding judge.
2 (b) Subject to subsection (c), after receiving a grievance under
3 subsection (a), the court:
4 (1) Shall review the grievance and, if necessary to determine the
5 appropriate response, court records related to the guardianship or
6 conservatorship;
7 (2) shall schedule a hearing if the individual subject to guardianship
8 or conservatorship is an adult and the grievance supports a reasonable
9 belief that:
10 (A) Removal of the guardian and appointment of a successor may be
11 appropriate under section 81, and amendments thereto;
12 (B) termination or modification of the guardianship may be
13 appropriate under section 82, and amendments thereto;
14 (C) removal of the conservator and appointment of a successor may
15 be appropriate under section 112, and amendments thereto; or
16 (D) termination or modification of the conservatorship may be
17 appropriate under section 113, and amendments thereto; and
18 (3) may take any action supported by the evidence, including:
19 (A) Ordering the guardian or conservator to provide the court a
20 report, accounting, inventory, updated plan or other information;
21 (B) appointing a guardian ad litem;
22 (C) appointing an attorney for the individual subject to guardianship
23 or conservatorship; or
24 (D) holding a hearing.
25 (c) The court may decline to act under subsection (b) if a similar
26 grievance was filed within the six months preceding the filing of the
27 current grievance and the court followed the procedures of subsection (b)
28 in considering the earlier grievance.
29 New Sec. 51. (a) A person becomes a guardian for a minor only on
30 appointment by the court.
31 (b) After a hearing under section 53, and amendments thereto, the
32 court may appoint a guardian for a minor who does not have a guardian if
33 the court finds the appointment is in the minor's best interest and:
34 (1) Each parent of the minor, after being fully informed of the nature
35 and consequences of guardianship, consents;
36 (2) all parental rights have been terminated;
37 (3) there is clear and convincing evidence that the parents of the
38 minor are unwilling, unable or unfit to exercise the powers the court is
39 granting the guardian; or
40 (4) there is clear and convincing evidence that highly unusual or
41 extraordinary circumstances exist that cause the court to appoint the
42 guardian over the objection of a parent of the minor.
43 New Sec. 52. (a) A person interested in the welfare of a minor,

HB 2359 26
1 including the minor, may file a verified petition for appointment of a
2 guardian for the minor.
3 (b) A petition under subsection (a) must state the petitioner's name,
4 principal residence, current street address if different, relationship to the

36 New Sec. 53. (a) When a petition is filed under section 52, and

39 (1) Serve notice of the date, time and place of the hearing, together

39 New Sec. 54. (a) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent a

41 amendments thereto, if:
42 (1) Requested by the minor and the minor is 12 years of age or older;
43 (2) recommended by a guardian ad litem; or

HB 2359 28
1 (3) the court determines the minor needs representation.
2 (b) An attorney appointed under subsection (a) shall:
3 (1) Make a reasonable effort to ascertain the minor's wishes;
4 (2) advocate for the minor's wishes to the extent reasonably
5 ascertainable; and
6 (3) if the minor's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable, advocate
7 for the minor's best interest.

15 New Sec. 55. (a) The court may require a minor who is the subject of
16 a hearing under section 53, and amendments thereto, to attend and
17 participate in the hearing. If the court orders the minor to attend the
18 hearing but later rescinds that order, the court shall enter in the record of
19 the proceedings the facts upon which the court found that the presence of
20 the minor should be excused.
21 (b) Unless excused by the court for good cause, the person proposed
22 to be appointed as guardian for a minor shall attend a hearing under
23 section 53, and amendments thereto.
24 (c) The minor who is the subject of a hearing under section 53, and
25 amendments thereto, has the right to attend the hearing. Each parent of a
26 minor who is the subject of a hearing under section 53, and amendments
27 thereto, has the right to attend the hearing.
28 (d) A person may request permission to participate in a hearing under
29 section 53, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the request, with
30 or without hearing, on determining that it is in the best interest of the
31 minor who is the subject of the hearing. The court may impose appropriate
32 conditions on the person's participation.
33 New Sec. 56. (a) After a hearing under section 53, and amendments
34 thereto, the court may appoint a guardian for a minor, if appointment is
35 proper under section 51, and amendments thereto, dismiss the proceeding
36 or take other appropriate action.
37 (b) In appointing a guardian under subsection (a), the following rules
38 apply:
39 (1) The court shall appoint a person nominated as guardian by a
40 parent of the minor in a will or other record unless the court finds the
41 appointment is contrary to the best interest of the minor.
42 (2) If multiple parents have nominated different persons to serve as
43 guardian, the court shall appoint the nominee whose appointment is in the

HB 2359 29
1 best interest of the minor, unless the court finds that appointment of none
2 of the nominees is in the best interest of the minor.
3 (3) If a guardian is not appointed under paragraph (1) or (2), the court
4 shall appoint the person nominated by the minor if the minor is 12 years of
5 age or older unless the court finds that appointment is contrary to the best
6 interest of the minor, in which case, the court shall appoint as guardian a
7 person whose appointment is in the best interest of the minor.
8 (c) An order granting a guardianship for a minor must state that each
9 parent of the minor is entitled to notice that:
10 (1) The guardian has changed the residence or school of the minor
11 subject to guardianship;
12 (2) the court has modified or limited the powers of the guardian; or
13 (3) the court has removed the guardian.
14 (d) An order granting a guardianship for a minor must identify any
15 person, in addition to a parent of the minor, who is entitled to notice of the
16 events listed in subsection (c).
17 (e) The appointment of a guardian under this section shall not be
18 construed to relieve a parent of any obligation imposed by law for the
19 support, maintenance, care, treatment, habilitation or education of that
20 parent's minor child.
21 New Sec. 57. (a) A standby guardian appointed under this section
22 may act as guardian, with all duties and powers of a guardian under
23 sections 59 and 60, and amendments thereto, when no parent of the minor
24 is willing or able to exercise the duties and powers granted to the guardian.
25 (b) A parent of a minor, in a signed record, may nominate a person to
26 be appointed by the court as standby guardian for the minor. The parent, in
27 a signed record, may revoke or amend the nomination at any time before
28 the court appoints a standby guardian.
29 (c) The court may appoint a standby guardian for a minor on:
30 (1) Petition by a parent of the minor or a person nominated under
31 subsection (b); and
32 (2) finding that no parent of the minor likely will be able or willing to
33 care for or make decisions with respect to the minor not later than two
34 years after the appointment.
35 (d) A petition under subsection (c)(1) must include the same
36 information required under section 52, and amendments thereto, for the
37 appointment of a guardian for a minor.
38 (e) On filing a petition under subsection (c)(1), the petitioner shall:
39 (1) Serve a copy of the petition personally on:

42 (B) each parent of the minor;
43 (C) the person nominated as the standby guardian; and

1 (D) any other person the court determines; and

33 (1) The court shall appoint the person nominated under subsection (b)

37 standby guardian, the court shall appoint the nominee whose appointment
38 is in the best interest of the minor, unless the court finds that appointment
39 of none of the nominees is in the best interest of the minor.

43 (1) The standby guardian assumes the duties and powers of the

1 guardian;
2 (2) the standby guardian changes the residence or school of the
