20 New Sec. 58. (a) On its own, or on verified petition by a person
21 interested in a minor's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
22 guardian for the minor if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
23 establish probable cause that:
24 (1) Appointment of an emergency guardian is necessary to prevent
25 imminent and substantial harm to the minor's health, safety or welfare; and
26 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
27 circumstances.
28 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency guardian for a minor
29 may not exceed 30 days, and the emergency guardian may exercise only
30 the powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency
31 guardian's authority may be extended up to three times for not more than
32 30 days per extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions
33 for appointment of an emergency guardian in subsection (a) continue.
34 (c) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (d), reasonable notice
35 of the date, time and place of a hearing on a petition for appointment of an
36 emergency guardian for a minor must be given to:
37 (1) The minor, if the minor is 12 years of age or older;
38 (2) any attorney appointed under section 54, and amendments thereto;
39 (3) each parent of the minor;
40 (4) any person, other than a parent, having care or custody of the
41 minor; and
42 (5) any other person the court determines.
43 (d) The court may appoint an emergency guardian for a minor

HB 2359 32
1 without notice under subsection (c) and without a hearing only if the court
2 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the minor's health, safety or
3 welfare will be substantially harmed before a hearing with notice on the
4 appointment can be held. If the court appoints an emergency guardian
5 without notice to an unrepresented minor or the attorney for a represented
6 minor, notice of the appointment must be given not later than 48 hours
7 after the appointment to the individuals listed in subsection (c). Not later
8 than seven days after the appointment, the court shall hold a hearing on the
9 appropriateness of the appointment.
10 (e) Appointment of an emergency guardian under this section, with or
11 without notice, is not a determination that a basis exists for appointment of
12 a guardian under section 51, and amendments thereto.
13 (f) The emergency guardian shall make any report the court requires.
14 (g) The court may remove an emergency guardian appointed under
15 this section at any time.
16 New Sec. 59. (a) A guardian for a minor is a fiduciary. Except as
17 otherwise limited by the court, a guardian for a minor has the duties and
18 responsibilities of a parent regarding the minor's support, care, education,
19 health, safety and welfare. A guardian shall act in the minor's best interest
20 and exercise reasonable care, diligence and prudence.
21 (b) A guardian for a minor shall:
22 (1) Be personally acquainted with the minor and maintain sufficient
23 contact with the minor to know the minor's abilities, limitations, needs,
24 opportunities and physical and mental health;
25 (2) take reasonable care of the minor's personal effects and bring a
26 proceeding for a conservatorship, or protective arrangement instead of
27 conservatorship, if necessary to protect other property of the minor;
28 (3) if authorized by the court under section 61, and amendments
29 thereto, expend funds of the minor which have been received by the
30 guardian for the minor's current needs for support, care, education, health,
31 safety and welfare;
32 (4) conserve any funds of the minor not expended under paragraph
33 (3) for the minor's future needs, but if a conservator is appointed for the
34 minor, pay the funds at least quarterly to the conservator to be conserved
35 for the minor's future needs;
36 (5) report the condition of the minor and account for funds and other
37 property of the minor in the guardian's possession or subject to the
38 guardian's control, as required by court rule or ordered by the court on
39 application of a person interested in the minor's welfare;
40 (6) inform the court of any change in the minor's dwelling or address;
41 and
42 (7) in determining what is in the minor's best interest, take into
43 account the minor's preferences to the extent actually known or reasonably

HB 2359 33
1 ascertainable by the guardian.
2 New Sec. 60. (a) Except as otherwise limited by court order, a
3 guardian of a minor has the powers a parent otherwise would have
4 regarding the minor's support, care, education, health, safety and welfare.
5 (b) Except as otherwise limited by court order, a guardian for a minor
6 may:
7 (1) If authorized by the court under section 61, and amendments
8 thereto, apply for and receive funds and benefits otherwise payable for the
9 support of the minor to the minor's parent, guardian or custodian under a
10 statutory system of benefits or insurance or any private contract, devise,
11 trust, conservatorship or custodianship;
12 (2) unless inconsistent with a court order entitled to recognition in
13 this state, take custody of the minor and establish the minor's place of
14 dwelling and, on authorization of the court, establish or move the minor's
15 dwelling outside this state;
16 (3) if the minor is not subject to conservatorship, commence a
17 proceeding, including an administrative proceeding, or take other
18 appropriate action to compel a person to support the minor or make a
19 payment for the benefit of the minor; and
20 (4) consent to health or other care, treatment or service for the minor.
21 (c) The court may authorize a guardian for a minor to consent to the
22 adoption of the minor if the minor does not have a parent.
23 (d) A guardian for a minor may consent to the marriage of the minor
24 if authorized by the court, and the guardianship shall terminate upon such
25 marriage.
26 New Sec. 61. A guardian for a minor may not exercise any control or
27 authority over the minor's estate, unless specifically authorized by the
28 court. Any guardian who is granted such authority must prepare an
29 inventory and provide notice of the inventory as provided in section 104,
30 and amendments thereto. The court may assign such authority to the
31 guardian and may waive the requirement of the posting of a bond, only if:
32 (a) Initially, the combined value of any funds and assets owned by the
33 minor equals $25,000 or less;
34 (b) either the court requires the guardian to report to the court the
35 commencement of the exercising of such authority, or requires the
36 guardian to obtain court authorization to commence the exercise of such
37 authority, as the court shall specify; and
38 (c) the court also requires the guardian, whenever the combined value
39 of such funds and property exceeds $25,000, to:
40 (1) File a guardian's plan as provided for in section 63, and
41 amendments thereto, that contains elements similar to those that would be
42 contained in a conservator's plan as provided for in section 103, and
43 amendments thereto;

HB 2359 34
1 (2) petition the court for appointment of a conservator; or
2 (3) notify the court as the court shall specify that the value of the
3 minor's estate has equaled or exceeded $25,000, if the court has earlier
4 appointed a conservator but did not issue letters of conservatorship
5 pending such notification.
6 New Sec. 62. (a) Guardianship under this act for a minor terminates:
7 (1) On the minor's death, adoption, emancipation or attainment of
8 majority; or
9 (2) when the court finds that the standard in section 51, and
10 amendments thereto, for appointment of a guardian is not satisfied, unless
11 the court finds that:
12 (A) Termination of the guardianship would be harmful to the minor;
13 and
14 (B) the minor's interest in the continuation of the guardianship
15 outweighs the interest of any parent of the minor in restoration of the
16 parent's right to make decisions for the minor.
17 (b) A minor subject to guardianship or a person interested in the
18 welfare of the minor may petition the court to terminate the guardianship,
19 modify the guardianship, remove the guardian and appoint a successor
20 guardian or remove a standby guardian and appoint a different standby
21 guardian.
22 (c) A petitioner under subsection (b) shall give notice of the hearing
23 on the petition to the minor, if the minor is 12 years of age or older and is
24 not the petitioner, the guardian, each parent of the minor and any other
25 person the court determines.
26 (d) The court shall follow the priorities in section 56(b), and
27 amendments thereto, when selecting a successor guardian for a minor.
28 (e) Not later than 30 days after appointment of a successor guardian
29 for a minor, the court shall give notice of the appointment to the minor
30 subject to guardianship, if the minor is 12 years of age or older, each
31 parent of the minor and any other person the court determines.
32 (f) When terminating a guardianship for a minor under this section,
33 the court may issue an order providing for transitional arrangements that
34 will assist the minor with a transition of custody and is in the best interest
35 of the minor.
36 (g) A removed guardian for a minor shall cooperate with a successor
37 guardian to facilitate transition of the guardian's responsibilities and
38 protect the best interest of the minor.
39 (h) Not later than 30 days after entering an order under this section,
40 the court or the court's designee shall give notice of the order to the minor
41 subject to guardianship and any person entitled to notice under section 56,
42 and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
43 New Sec. 63. (a) At any time, the court may require the guardian of a

HB 2359 35
1 minor, or the guardian of a minor may choose, to develop and file with the
2 court a plan of care for the minor. Any such plan must be based on the
3 needs of the minor and take into account the best interest of the minor as
4 well as the minor's preferences, to the extent known to or reasonably
5 ascertainable by the guardian. The guardian may include in the plan:
6 (1) Where the minor will reside and attend school;
7 (2) whether the parents of the minor will have contact or visitation
8 with the minor;
9 (3) whether the parents of the minor will have access to medical,
10 educational or other records of the minor;
11 (4) whether the parents of the minor will retain any rights to decision
12 making regarding the minor's healthcare, education or other matters;
13 (5) any other provisions the guardian deems appropriate; and
14 (6) any other provisions the court requires.
15 (b) The guardian for a minor shall give notice of the filing of the
16 guardian's plan under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to
17 the minor if the minor is 12 years of age or older, any attorney representing
18 the minor in the guardianship proceeding or any other proceeding
19 concerning the care or custody of the minor identified in the petition, each
20 parent of the minor, a person entitled to notice under section 56(d), and
21 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
22 determines. The notice shall include a statement of the right to object to
23 the plan and shall be given at the time of the filing.
24 (c) The minor, a parent of the minor and any person entitled under
25 subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the guardian's plan may
26 object to the plan in writing not later than 21 days after the filing.
27 (d) The court shall review the guardian's plan filed under subsection
28 (a) and determine whether to approve the plan, modify the plan or require
29 a new plan. In deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall
30 consider an objection under subsection (c) and whether the plan is
31 consistent with the guardian's duties and powers under sections 59 and 60,
32 and amendments thereto. The court may not approve the plan until 30 days
33 after the filing.
34 (e) After the guardian's plan filed under this section is approved by
35 the court, the guardian shall provide a copy of the plan to the minor if the
36 minor is 12 years of age or older, to any attorney representing the minor in
37 the guardianship proceeding or any other proceeding concerning the care
38 or custody of the minor identified in the petition, to each parent of the
39 minor, to any person entitled to notice under section 56(d), and
40 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
41 determines.
42 New Sec. 64. (a) On petition and after notice and hearing, the court
43 may:

HB 2359 36
1 (1) Appoint a guardian for an adult if the court finds by clear and
2 convincing evidence that:
3 (A) The respondent lacks the ability to meet essential requirements
4 for physical health, safety or self-care because the respondent is unable to
5 receive and evaluate information or make or communicate decisions, even
6 with appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
7 decision making; and
8 (B) the respondent's identified needs cannot be met by a protective
9 arrangement instead of guardianship or other less restrictive alternative; or
10 (2) with appropriate findings, treat the petition as one for a
11 conservatorship under sections 83 through 118, and amendments thereto,
12 or a protective arrangement under sections 119 through 130, and
13 amendments thereto, issue any appropriate order or dismiss the
14 proceeding.
15 (b) The court shall grant a guardian appointed under subsection (a)
16 only those powers necessitated by the demonstrated needs and limitations
17 of the respondent and issue orders that will encourage development of the
18 respondent's maximum self-determination and independence. The court
19 may not establish a full guardianship if a limited guardianship, protective
20 arrangement instead of guardianship or other less restrictive alternatives
21 would meet the needs of the respondent.

2 New Sec. 67. (a) On receipt of a petition under section 65, and
3 amendments thereto, for appointment of a guardian for an adult, the court
4 may appoint a court liaison. The court liaison must be an individual with
5 training or experience in the type of abilities, limitations and needs alleged
6 in the petition.
7 (b) (1) A court liaison appointed under subsection (a) shall interview

11 proceeding, including the potential loss of rights as a result of the
12 proceeding; and

14 the petitioner, including views about a proposed guardian, the guardian's
15 proposed powers and duties and the scope and duration of the proposed
16 guardianship.
17 (2) These explanations and discussions are not intended to be a
18 substitute for the attorney appointed to represent the respondent to inform
19 the respondent of the respondent's rights and the nature and purpose of the
20 proceeding.
21 (c) The court liaison appointed under subsection (a) may be assigned
22 any or all of the following duties, in the discretion of the presiding judge:
23 (1) Interview the petitioner and proposed guardian, if any;

26 made;
27 (3) obtain information from any physician or other provider known to
28 have treated, advised or assessed the respondent's relevant physical or
29 mental condition, to the extent that such information has not already been
30 provided to the court; and

32 relating to the petition as directed by the court, including, but not limited
33 to, the respondent's family relationships, past conduct, the nature and
34 extent of any property or income of the respondent, whether the
35 respondent is likely to injure self or others and other matters as the court
36 may specify.

24 New Sec. 68. (a) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent the
25 respondent, regardless of the respondent's ability to pay. The court shall
26 give preference in the appointment of an attorney to any attorney who has
27 represented the respondent in other matters if the court has knowledge of
28 that prior representation or to an attorney whom the respondent has
29 requested. Any appointment made by the court shall terminate after the
30 guardian's plan has been approved and after any appeal from the
31 appointment of a guardian, unless the court continues the appointment by
32 further order. Thereafter, an attorney may be appointed by the court if
33 requested, in writing, by the adult subject to guardianship, the guardian, or
34 upon the court's own motion.
35 (b) An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding for
36 appointment of a guardian for an adult shall:
37 (1) Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes;
38 (2) advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably
39 ascertainable; and
40 (3) if the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable,
41 advocate for the result that is the least restrictive in type, duration and
42 scope, consistent with the respondent's interests.
43 (c) An attorney representing the respondent shall interview the

1 respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to

9 guardianship; and

11 proceeding, including respondent's attorney fees, may be paid from the
12 respondent's assets.
13 New Sec. 69. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
14 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
15 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a guardian, the court
16 shall order an examination and evaluation of the respondent to be
17 conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric hospital, community
18 mental health center, community developmental disability organization or
19 by a licensed physician, psychiatrist, psychologist, physician assistant,
20 nurse practitioner, social worker or other professional appointed by the
21 court who is qualified to evaluate the respondent's alleged cognitive and
22 functional abilities and limitations and will not be advantaged or
23 disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition or otherwise have a
24 conflict of interest.
25 (b) Unless otherwise specified by the court, the report of the
26 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:
27 (1) The respondent's name, age and date of birth;
28 (2) a description of the respondent's physical and mental condition;
29 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
30 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
31 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
32 (4) a summary of self-care and independent-living tasks the
33 respondent can manage without assistance or with existing supports, could
34 manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive services,
35 technological assistance or supported decision making, and cannot
36 manage;
37 (5) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
38 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;
39 (6) a list and description of any prior assessments, evaluations or
40 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
41 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;
42 (7) the date and location where this examination and evaluation
43 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals

HB 2359 42
1 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
2 qualifications;
3 (8) a statement by the professional that the professional has
4 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
5 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results
6 of that examination and evaluation, and the professional's opinion with
7 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
8 guardian and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance and
9 participation at the hearing on the petition; and
10 (9) the signature of the professional who prepared the report.
11 (c) The professional shall file with the court, at least five days prior to
12 the date of the trial, such professional's written report concerning the
13 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made
14 available by the court to counsel for all parties.
15 (d) In lieu of entering an order for an examination and evaluation as
16 provided for in this section, the court may determine that the report
17 accompanying the petition is in compliance with the requirements of this
18 section and that no further examination or evaluation should be required,
19 unless the respondent, or such person's attorney, requests such an
20 examination and evaluation in writing. Any such request shall be filed with
21 the court, and a copy thereof delivered to the petitioner, at least four days
22 prior to the date of the trial. Accompanying the request shall be a statement
23 of the reasons why an examination and evaluation is requested and the
24 name and address of a qualified professional or facility willing and able to
25 conduct this examination and evaluation. If the court orders a further
26 examination and evaluation, the court may continue the trial and fix a new
27 date, time and place of the trial at a time not to exceed 30 days from the
28 date of the filing of the request.
29 New Sec. 70. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
30 hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto, may not proceed unless
31 the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably feasible for the
32 respondent to attend a hearing at the location court proceedings typically
33 are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to hold the hearing at an
34 alternative location convenient to the respondent or allow the respondent
35 to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual technology.
36 (b) A hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto, may
37 proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court finds by clear
38 and convincing evidence that:
39 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
40 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
41 of failing to do so; or
42 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
43 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services and

HB 2359 43
1 technological assistance.
2 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under section 66, and
3 amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the respondent's choosing,
4 assistive technology or an interpreter or translator, or a combination of
5 these supports. If assistance would facilitate the respondent's participation
6 in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to the respondent, the court
7 shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.
8 (d) The respondent has a right to retain an attorney to represent the
9 respondent at a hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto.
10 (e) At a hearing held under section 66, and amendments thereto, the
11 respondent may:
12 (1) Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents;
13 (2) examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and
14 the court liaison; and
15 (3) otherwise participate in the hearing.
16 (f) Unless excused by the court for good cause, a proposed guardian
17 shall attend a hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto.
18 (g) A hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto, must be
19 closed on request of the respondent and a showing of good cause.
20 (h) Any person may request to participate in a hearing under section
21 66, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the request, with or
22 without a hearing, on determining that the best interest of the respondent
23 will be served. The court may impose appropriate conditions on the
24 person's participation.
25 New Sec. 71. (a) The existence of a proceeding for or the existence of
26 a guardianship for an adult is a matter of public record unless the court
27 seals the record after:
28 (1) The respondent or individual subject to guardianship requests the
29 record be sealed; and
30 (2) either:
31 (A) The petition for guardianship is dismissed; or
32 (B) the guardianship is terminated.
33 (b) (1) The following court records are a matter of public record
34 unless sealed by the court:
35 (A) Letters of guardianship;
36 (B) orders suspending or removing a guardian; and
37 (C) orders terminating a guardianship.
38 (2) All other court records of a guardianship proceeding are not a
39 matter of public record except as further provided.
40 (3) The following persons are entitled to access court records of the
41 proceeding and resulting guardianship, including the guardian's plan under
42 section 79, and amendments thereto, and report under section 80, and
43 amendments thereto:

HB 2359 44
1 (A) An adult subject to a proceeding for a guardianship, whether or
2 not a guardian is appointed;
3 (B) an attorney designated by the adult;
4 (C) a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and amendments
5 thereto, or a subsequent order; and
6 (D) a licensed attorney, abstractor or title insurance agent.
7 (4) A person not otherwise entitled to access court records under this
8 subsection for good cause may request permission from the court for
9 access to court records of the guardianship, including the guardian's report
10 and plan. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest of the
11 respondent or adult subject to guardianship or furthers the public interest
12 and does not endanger the welfare or financial interests of the adult.
13 (c) A report under section 67, and amendments thereto, of a court
14 liaison or a professional evaluation under section 69, and amendments
15 thereto, is confidential and must be sealed on filing, but is available to:
16 (1) The court;
17 (2) the individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation,

20 attorneys, for purposes of the proceeding;
21 (4) unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a
22 power of attorney for healthcare or power of attorney for finances in which
23 the respondent is the principal; and
24 (5) any other person if it is in the public interest or for a purpose the
25 court orders for good cause.
26 New Sec. 72. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
27 court in appointing a guardian for an adult shall consider persons qualified
28 to be guardian in the following order of priority:
29 (1) A guardian, other than a temporary or emergency guardian,
30 currently acting for the respondent in another jurisdiction;
31 (2) a person nominated as guardian by the respondent, including the
32 respondent's most recent nomination made in a power of attorney;
33 (3) an agent appointed by the respondent under a power of attorney
34 for healthcare;
35 (4) a spouse of the respondent;
36 (5) a family member or other individual who has shown special care
37 and concern for the respondent; and
38 (6) a person nominated as guardian by the spouse, adult child or other
39 close family member of the respondent.
40 (b) If two or more persons have equal priority under subsection (a),
41 the court shall select as guardian the person the court considers best
42 qualified. In determining the best qualified person, the court shall consider
43 the person's relationship with the respondent, the person's skills, the

HB 2359 45
1 expressed wishes of the respondent, the extent to which the person and the
2 respondent have similar values and preferences and the likelihood the
3 person will be able to perform the duties of a guardian successfully.
4 (c) The court, acting in the best interest of the respondent, may
5 decline to appoint as guardian a person having priority under subsection
6 (a) and appoint a person having a lower priority or no priority.
7 (d) In determining whether the appointment of a proposed guardian is
8 in the best interest of the respondent, the court shall consider the number
9 of other cases in which the proposed guardian, other than a corporation, is
10 currently serving as guardian, particularly if that number is more than 15.
11 (e) The following persons shall not be appointed as guardian unless
12 the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that the person is the best
13 qualified person available for appointment and the appointment is in the
14 best interest of the respondent:
15 (1) A person that provides paid services to the respondent, or an
16 individual who is employed by a person that provides paid services to the
17 respondent, or is the spouse, parent or child of an individual who provides
18 or is employed to provide paid services to the respondent;
19 (2) an owner, operator or employee of any entity at which the
20 respondent is receiving care; and
21 (3) a person who provides care or other services, or is an employee of
22 an agency, partnership or corporation that provides care or other services
23 to persons with needs similar to those of the respondent.
24 New Sec. 73. (a) A court order appointing a guardian for an adult
25 must:
26 (1) Include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence
27 established that the identified needs of the respondent cannot be met by a
28 protective arrangement instead of guardianship or other less restrictive
29 alternative, including use of appropriate supportive services, technological
30 assistance or supported decision making; and
31 (2) include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence
32 established the respondent was given proper notice of the hearing on the
33 petition.
34 (b) A court order establishing a full guardianship for an adult must
35 state the basis for granting a full guardianship and include specific findings
36 that support the conclusion that a limited guardianship would not meet the
37 functional needs of the adult subject to guardianship.
38 (c) A court order establishing a limited guardianship for an adult must
39 state the specific powers granted to the guardian.
40 (d) A court order appointing a guardian for an adult must include the
41 date of a review hearing to be set 90 days after the order of appointment is
42 entered. At that hearing, the court shall review the guardian's plan filed
43 pursuant to section 79, and amendments thereto.

24 New Sec. 74. (a) Not later than 14 days after the appointment, a
25 guardian appointed under section 72, and amendments thereto, shall give
26 the adult subject to guardianship and all other persons given notice under
27 section 66, and amendments thereto, a copy of the order of appointment.
28 (b) Not later than 30 days after appointment of a guardian under
29 section 72, and amendments thereto, the court or the court's designee shall
30 give to the adult subject to guardianship, the guardian and any other person
31 entitled to notice under section 72(e), and amendments thereto, or a
32 subsequent order a statement of the rights of the adult subject to
33 guardianship and procedures to seek relief if the adult is denied those
34 rights. The statement must be in at least 16-point font, in plain language
35 and, to the extent feasible, in a language in which the adult subject to
36 guardianship is proficient. The statement must notify the adult subject to
37 guardianship of the right to:
38 (1) Seek termination or modification of the guardianship, or removal
39 of the guardian, and choose an attorney to represent the adult in these
40 matters;
41 (2) file a grievance against the guardian under section 50, and
42 amendments thereto;
43 (3) be involved in decisions affecting the adult, including decisions

HB 2359 47
1 about the adult's care, dwelling, activities or social interactions, to the
2 extent reasonably feasible, and that the adult retains the right to vote and
3 the right to marry;
4 (4) be involved in healthcare decision making to the extent
5 reasonably feasible and supported in understanding the risks and benefits
6 of healthcare options to the extent reasonably feasible;
7 (5) be notified at least 14 days before a change in the adult's primary
8 dwelling or permanent move to a nursing home, mental health facility or
9 other facility that places restrictions on the individual's ability to leave or
10 have visitors unless the change or move is proposed in the guardian's plan
11 under section 79, and amendments thereto, or authorized by the court by
12 specific order;
13 (6) object to a change or move described in paragraph (5) and the
14 process for objecting;
15 (7) communicate, visit or interact with others, including receiving
16 visitors, and making or receiving telephone calls, personal mail or
17 electronic communications, including through social media, unless:
18 (A) The guardian has been authorized by the court by specific order
19 to restrict communications, visits or interactions;
20 (B) a protective order or protective arrangement instead of
21 guardianship is in effect that limits contact between the adult and a person;
22 or
23 (C) the guardian has good cause to believe restriction is necessary
24 because interaction with a specified person poses a risk of significant
25 physical, psychological or financial harm to the adult, and the restriction
26 is:
27 (i) For a period of not more than seven business days if the person
28 has a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult; or
29 (ii) for a period of not more than 60 days if the person does not have
30 a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult;
31 (8) receive a copy of the guardian's plan under section 79, and
32 amendments thereto, and the guardian's report under section 80, and
33 amendments thereto; and
34 (9) object to the guardian's plan or report.
35 (c) Any person required to provide notice under this section shall file
36 proof of service of such notice with the court.
37 New Sec. 75. (a) On its own after a petition has been filed under
38 section 65, and amendments thereto, or on verified petition by a person
39 interested in an adult's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
40 guardian for the adult if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
41 establish probable cause that:
42 (1) Appointment of an emergency guardian is necessary to prevent
43 imminent and substantial harm to the adult's physical health, safety or

HB 2359 48
1 welfare;
2 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
3 circumstances; and
4 (3) a basis for appointment of a guardian under section 64, and
5 amendments thereto, exists.
6 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency guardian for an adult
7 may not exceed 30 days, and the emergency guardian may exercise only
8 the powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency
9 guardian's authority may be extended up to three times for not more than
10 30 days per extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions
11 for appointment of an emergency guardian in subsection (a) continue.
12 (c) Immediately upon filing of a petition for appointment of an
13 emergency guardian for an adult, the court shall appoint an attorney to
14 represent the respondent in the proceeding. Except as otherwise provided
15 in subsection (d), reasonable notice of the date, time, and place of a
16 hearing on the petition must be given to the respondent, the respondent's
17 attorney and any other person the court determines.
18 (d) The court may appoint an emergency guardian for an adult
19 without notice to the adult and any attorney for the adult only if the court
20 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the respondent's physical health,
21 safety or welfare will be substantially harmed before a hearing with notice
22 on the appointment can be held. If the court appoints an emergency
23 guardian without giving notice under subsection (c), the court must:
24 (1) Give notice of the appointment not later than 48 hours after the
25 appointment to:
26 (A) The respondent;
27 (B) the respondent's attorney; and
28 (C) any other person the court determines; and
29 (2) hold a hearing on the appropriateness of the appointment not later
30 than five days after the appointment.
31 (e) Appointment of an emergency guardian under this section is not a
32 determination that a basis exists for appointment of a guardian under
33 section 64, and amendments thereto.
34 (f) The court may remove an emergency guardian appointed under
35 this section at any time. The emergency guardian shall make any report the
36 court requires.
37 New Sec. 76. (a) A guardian for an adult is a fiduciary. A guardian
38 shall strive to assure that the personal, civil and human rights of the
39 individual subject to guardianship are protected. Except as otherwise
40 limited by the court, a guardian for an adult shall make decisions regarding
41 the support, care, education, health and welfare of the adult subject to
42 guardianship to the extent necessitated by the adult's limitations and in
43 accordance with the guardian's plan under section 79, and amendments

HB 2359 49
1 thereto.
2 (b) A guardian for an adult shall promote the self-determination of the
3 adult and, to the extent reasonably feasible, include the adult in decision
4 making, and encourage the adult to participate in decisions, act on the
5 adult's own behalf, and develop or regain the capacity to manage the
6 adult's personal affairs. In furtherance of this duty, the guardian shall:
7 (1) Become or remain personally acquainted with the adult and
8 maintain sufficient contact with the adult, including through regular
9 visitation, to know the adult's abilities, limitations, needs, opportunities
10 and physical and mental health;
11 (2) to the extent reasonably feasible, identify the values and
12 preferences of the adult and involve the adult in decisions affecting the
13 adult, including decisions about the adult's care, dwelling, activities or
14 social interactions; and
15 (3) make reasonable efforts to identify and facilitate supportive
16 relationships and services for the adult.
17 (c) A guardian for an adult at all times shall exercise reasonable care,
18 diligence and prudence when acting on behalf of or making decisions for
19 the adult. In furtherance of this duty, the guardian shall:
20 (1) Take reasonable care of the personal effects and service or support
21 animals of the adult and bring a proceeding for a conservatorship or
22 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship if necessary to protect
23 the adult's property;
24 (2) if authorized by the court under section 78, and amendments
25 thereto, expend funds and other property of the adult received by the
26 guardian for the adult's current needs for support, care, education, health
27 and welfare;
28 (3) conserve any funds and other property of the adult not expended
29 under paragraph (2) for the adult's future needs, but if a conservator has
30 been appointed for the adult, pay the funds and other property at least
31 quarterly to the conservator to be conserved for the adult's future needs;
32 and
33 (4) monitor the quality of services, including long-term care services,
34 provided to the adult.
35 (d) In making a decision for an adult subject to guardianship, the
36 guardian shall make the decision the guardian reasonably believes the
37 adult would make if the adult were able unless doing so would
38 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
39 interests of the adult. To determine the decision the adult subject to
40 guardianship would make if able, the guardian shall consider the adult's
41 previous or current directions, preferences, opinions, cultural practices,
42 religious beliefs, values and actions, to the extent actually known or
43 reasonably ascertainable by the guardian.

HB 2359 50
1 (e) If a guardian for an adult cannot make a decision under subsection
2 (d) because the guardian does not know and cannot reasonably determine
3 the decision the adult probably would make if able, or the guardian
4 reasonably believes the decision the adult would make would
5 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
6 interests of the adult, the guardian shall act in accordance with the best
7 interest of the adult. In determining the best interest of the adult, the
8 guardian shall consider:
9 (1) Information received from professionals and persons that
10 demonstrate sufficient interest in the welfare of the adult;
11 (2) other information the guardian believes the adult would have
12 considered if the adult were able to act; and
13 (3) other factors a reasonable person in the circumstances of the adult
14 would consider, including consequences for others.
15 (f) A guardian for an adult shall notify the court immediately if the
16 condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable of exercising
17 rights previously removed.
18 New Sec. 77. (a) Except as limited by court order, a guardian for an
19 adult may:
20 (1) If authorized by the court under section 78, and amendments
21 thereto, apply for and receive funds and benefits for the support of the
22 adult, unless a conservator is appointed for the adult and the application or
23 receipt is within the powers of the conservator;
24 (2) establish the adult's place of dwelling;
25 (3) consent to health, including mental health, or other care, treatment
26 or service for the adult;
27 (4) if a conservator for the adult has not been appointed, commence a
28 proceeding including an administrative proceeding, or take other
29 appropriate action to compel another person to support the adult or pay
30 funds for the adult's benefit; and
31 (5) receive personally identifiable healthcare information regarding
32 the adult.
33 (b) The court by specific order may authorize a guardian for an adult
34 to consent to the adoption of the adult.
35 (c) The court by specific order may authorize a guardian for an adult
36 to litigate as petitioner or respondent an action for divorce, dissolution or
37 annulment of marriage of the individual subject to guardianship, including
38 negotiation of a settlement thereof.
39 (d) In determining whether to authorize a power under subsection (b)
40 or (c), the court shall consider whether the underlying act would be in
41 accordance with the adult's preferences, values and prior directions and
42 whether the underlying act would be in the adult's best interest.
43 (e) In exercising a guardian's power under subsection (a)(2) to

HB 2359 51
1 establish the adult's place of dwelling, the guardian shall:
2 (1) Select a residential setting the guardian believes the adult would
3 select if the adult were able, in accordance with the decision-making
4 standard in section 76(d) and (e), and amendments thereto. If the guardian
5 does not know and cannot reasonably determine what setting the adult
6 subject to guardianship probably would choose if able, or the guardian
7 reasonably believes the decision the adult would make would
8 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
9 interests of the adult, the guardian shall choose in accordance with section
10 76(e), and amendments thereto, a residential setting that is consistent with
11 the adult's best interest;
12 (2) in selecting among residential settings, give priority to a
13 residential setting in a location that will allow the adult to interact with

15 restrictive manner reasonably feasible unless to do so would be
16 inconsistent with the decision-making standard in section 76(d) and (e),
17 and amendments thereto;
18 (3) not later than 30 days after a change in the dwelling of the adult:
19 (A) Give notice of the change to the court, the adult and any person
20 identified as entitled to the notice in the court order appointing the
21 guardian or a subsequent order; and
22 (B) include in the notice the address and nature of the new dwelling
23 and state whether the adult received advance notice of the change and
24 whether the adult objected to the change;
25 (4) establish or move the permanent place of dwelling of the adult to
26 a nursing home, mental health facility or other facility that places
27 restrictions on the adult's ability to leave or have visitors only if:
28 (A) The establishment or move is in the guardian's plan under section

30 (B) the court authorizes the establishment or move; or
31 (C) the guardian gives notice of the establishment or move at least 14

34 order, and no objection is filed;

37 by specific order; and
38 (6) take action that would result in the sale of or surrender of the lease
39 to the primary dwelling of the adult only if:
40 (A) The action is specifically included in the guardian's plan under
41 section 79, and amendments thereto;
42 (B) the court authorizes the action by specific order; or
43 (C) notice of the action was given at least 14 days before the action to

HB 2359 52
1 the adult and all persons entitled to the notice under section 73(e)(2), and
2 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order and no objection has been
3 filed.
4 (f) In exercising a guardian's power under subsection (a)(3) to make
5 healthcare decisions, the guardian shall:
6 (1) Involve the adult in decision making to the extent reasonably
7 feasible, including, when practicable, by encouraging and supporting the
8 adult in understanding the risks and benefits of healthcare options;
9 (2) act in accordance with any declaration of the adult made pursuant
10 to the provisions of K.S.A. 65-28,101 through 65-28,109, and amendments
11 thereto; and
12 (3) take into account:
13 (A) The risks and benefits of treatment options; and

16 New Sec. 78. (a) A guardian for an adult may not initiate the
17 commitment of the adult to a mental health facility except in accordance
18 with the care and treatment act for mentally ill persons, K.S.A. 59-2945 et
19 seq., and amendments thereto.
20 (b) A guardian for an adult may not restrict the ability of the adult to
21 communicate, visit or interact with others, including receiving visitors and
22 making or receiving telephone calls, personal mail or electronic
23 communications, including through social media, or participating in social
24 activities, unless:
25 (1) Authorized by the court by specific order;
26 (2) a protective order or a protective arrangement instead of
27 guardianship is in effect that limits contact between the adult and a person;
28 or
29 (3) the guardian has good cause to believe restriction is necessary
30 because interaction with a specified person poses a risk of significant
31 physical, psychological or financial harm to the adult and the restriction is:
32 (A) For a period of not more than seven business days if the person
33 has a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult; or
34 (B) for a period of not more than 60 days if the person does not have
35 a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult.
36 (c) A guardian for an adult may not consent, on behalf of the adult, to:
37 (1) Any psychosurgery, removal of any bodily organ or amputation of
38 any limb, unless such surgery, removal or amputation has been approved
39 in advance by the court, except in an emergency and when necessary to
40 preserve the life of the adult or to prevent serious and irreparable
41 impairment to the physical health of the adult;
42 (2) the sterilization of the adult, unless approved by the court
43 following a due process hearing held for the purposes of determining

HB 2359 53
1 whether to approve such, and during which hearing the adult is represented
2 by an attorney appointed by the court;
3 (3) the performance of any experimental biomedical or behavioral
4 procedure on the adult, or for the adult to be a participant in any
5 biomedical or behavioral experiment, without the prior review and
6 approval of such by either an institutional review board as provided for in
7 title 45, part 46 of the code of federal regulations, or if such regulations do
8 not apply, then by a review committee established by the agency,
9 institution or treatment facility at which the procedure or experiment is
10 proposed to occur, composed of members selected for the purposes of
11 determining whether the proposed procedure or experiment:
12 (A) Does not involve any significant risk of harm to the physical or
13 mental health of the adult, or the use of aversive stimulants, and is
14 intended to preserve the life or health of the adult or to assist the adult to
15 develop or regain skills or abilities; or
16 (B) involves a significant risk of harm to the physical or mental
17 health of the adult, or the use of an aversive stimulant, but that the
18 conducting of the proposed procedure or experiment is intended either to
19 preserve the life of the adult, or to significantly improve the quality of life
20 of the adult, or to assist the adult to develop or regain significant skills or
21 abilities, and that the guardian has been fully informed concerning the
22 potential risks and benefits of the proposed procedure or experiment or of
23 any aversive stimulant proposed to be used, and as to how and under what
24 circumstances the aversive stimulant may be used, and has specifically
25 consented to such;
26 (4) the withholding or withdrawal of life-saving or life-sustaining
27 medical care, treatment, services or procedures, except:
28 (A) In accordance with the provisions of any declaration of the adult
29 made pursuant to the provisions of K.S.A. 65-28,101 through 65-28,109,
30 and amendments thereto; or
31 (B) if the adult, prior to the court's appointment of a guardian, has
32 executed a durable power of attorney for healthcare decisions pursuant to
33 K.S.A. 58-625, et seq., and amendments thereto, and that durable power of
34 attorney has not previously been revoked by the adult, and it includes any
35 provision relevant to the withholding or withdrawal of life-saving or life-
36 sustaining medical care, treatment, services or procedures, then the
37 guardian shall have the authority to act as provided for in that power of
38 attorney, even if the guardian has revoked or amended that power of
39 attorney pursuant to the authority of K.S.A. 58-627, and amendments
40 thereto; or
41 (C) in the circumstances where the adult's treating physician certifies
42 in writing to the guardian that the adult is in a persistent vegetative state or
43 is suffering from an illness or other medical condition for which further

HB 2359 54
1 treatment, other than for the relief of pain, would not likely prolong the life
2 of the adult other than by artificial means, nor would be likely to restore to
3 the adult any significant degree of capabilities beyond those the adult
4 currently possesses, and which opinion is concurred in by either a second
5 physician or by any medical ethics or similar committee to which the
6 healthcare provider has access established for the purposes of reviewing
7 such circumstances and the appropriateness of any type of physician's
8 order which would have the effect of withholding or withdrawing life-
9 saving or life-sustaining medical care, treatment, services or procedures.
10 The court shall review the written certification within 72 hours at a due
11 process hearing during which the adult is represented by an attorney
12 appointed by the court. The court may request that the state protection and
13 advocacy agency as provided by K.S.A. 65-5603(a)(10) or K.S.A. 74-

15 U.S.C. 10805 or 29 U.S.C. 794e represent the adult. Upon completion of
16 the hearing, if the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that the
17 adult meets the conditions set forth in this section, the court shall approve
18 the written certification. If the court does not find by clear and convincing
19 evidence that the adult meets the conditions set forth in this section, then
20 the written certification shall not be approved.
21 (d) A guardian for an adult may not exercise any control or authority
22 over the adult's estate, unless specifically authorized by the court. Any
23 guardian who is granted such authority must prepare an inventory and
24 provide notice of the inventory as provided in section 104, and
25 amendments thereto. The court may assign such authority to the guardian
26 and may waive the requirement of the posting of a bond, only if:
27 (1) Initially, the combined value of any funds and assets owned by the
28 adult equals $25,000 or less; and
29 (2) either the court requires the guardian to report to the court the
30 commencement of the exercising of such authority, or requires the
31 guardian to obtain court authorization to commence the exercise of such
32 authority, as the court shall specify; and
33 (3) the court also requires the guardian, whenever the combined value
34 of such funds and property exceeds $25,000, to:
35 (A) File a guardian's plan as provided for in section 79, and
36 amendments thereto, that contains elements similar to those that would be
37 contained in a conservator's plan as provided for in section 103, and
38 amendments thereto;
39 (B) petition the court for appointment of a conservator; or
40 (C) notify the court as the court shall specify that the value of the
41 adult's estate has equaled or exceeded $25,000, if the court has earlier
42 appointed a conservator but did not issue letters of conservatorship
43 pending such notification;

HB 2359 55
1 (e) A guardian for an adult may not access digital assets of the adult
2 except if authorized by the court pursuant to K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-4814,

4 New Sec. 79. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment and when
5 there is a significant change in circumstances, or the guardian seeks to
6 deviate significantly from the existing guardian's plan, a guardian for an
7 adult shall file with the court a plan for the care of the adult. The plan must
8 be based on the needs of the adult and take into account the best interest of
9 the adult as well as the adult's preferences, values and prior directions, to
10 the extent known to or reasonably ascertainable by the guardian. The
11 guardian shall include in the plan:
12 (1) The living arrangement, services and supports the guardian
13 expects to arrange, facilitate or continue for the adult;
14 (2) social and educational activities the guardian expects to facilitate
15 on behalf of the adult;
16 (3) any person with whom the adult has a close personal relationship
17 or relationship involving regular visitation and any plan the guardian has
18 for facilitating visits with the person;
19 (4) the anticipated nature and frequency of the guardian's visits and
20 communication with the adult;
21 (5) goals for the adult, including any goal related to the restoration of
22 the adult's rights, and how the guardian anticipates achieving the goals;
23 (6) whether the adult has an existing plan and, if so, whether the
24 guardian's plan is consistent with the adult's plan; and
25 (7) a statement or list of the amount the guardian proposes to charge
26 for each service the guardian anticipates providing to the adult.
27 (b) A guardian shall give notice of the filing of the guardian's plan
28 under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to the adult subject
29 to guardianship, any attorney representing the adult subject to
30 guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and
31 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
32 determines. The notice must include a statement of the right to object to
33 the plan and must be given at the time of the filing.
34 (c) An adult subject to guardianship and any person entitled under
35 subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the guardian's plan may
36 object to the plan in writing no later than 21 days after the filing.
37 (d) The court shall review the guardian's plan filed under subsection
38 (a) and determine whether to approve the plan or require a new plan. In
39 deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall consider an objection
40 under subsection (c) and whether the plan is consistent with the guardian's
41 duties and powers under sections 76 and 77, and amendments thereto. The
42 court shall review an initial guardian's plan at the review hearing
43 scheduled under section 73(b), and amendments thereto. When reviewing

HB 2359 56
1 subsequent guardian's plans, the court has discretion whether to set the
2 matter for hearing but may not approve the plan until 30 days after the
3 filing.
4 (e) After the guardian's plan filed under this section is approved by
5 the court, the guardian shall provide a copy of the plan to the adult subject
6 to guardianship, any attorney representing the adult subject to
7 guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and
8 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
9 determines.
10 New Sec. 80. (a) A guardian for an adult shall file with the court at
11 least annually and at any other time the court directs a report in a record
12 regarding the condition of the adult and accounting for funds and other
13 property in the guardian's possession or subject to the guardian's control.
14 (b) A report under subsection (a) must state or contain:
15 (1) The mental, physical and social condition of the adult;
16 (2) the living arrangements of the adult during the reporting period;
17 (3) a summary of the supported decision making, technological
18 assistance, medical services, educational and vocational services and other
19 supports and services provided to the adult and the guardian's opinion as to
20 the adequacy of the adult's care;
21 (4) a summary of the guardian's visits with the adult, including the
22 frequency of the visits;
23 (5) action taken on behalf of the adult;
24 (6) the extent to which the adult has participated in decision making;
25 (7) if the adult is living in a mental health facility or living in a
26 facility that provides the adult with healthcare or other personal services,
27 whether the guardian considers the facility's current plan for support, care,
28 treatment or habilitation consistent with the adult's preferences, values,
29 prior directions and best interest;
30 (8) anything of more than de minimis value which the guardian, any
31 individual who resides with the guardian, or the spouse, parent, child or
32 sibling of the guardian has received from an individual providing goods or
33 services to the adult;
34 (9) any circumstance that may constitute a conflict of interest
35 between the guardian and the adult. A conflict of interest occurs where the
36 guardian has some personal, business or agency interest that could be
37 perceived as self-serving or adverse to the position or best interest of the
38 adult, including, but not limited to, being paid for providing caregiver
39 services to the adult;
40 (10) if a guardian has been granted financial authority under section
41 78(c), and amendments thereto, an accounting that lists property included
42 in the adult's estate and the receipts, disbursements, liabilities and
43 distributions during the period for which the report is made;

HB 2359 57
1 (11) a copy of the guardian's most recently approved plan under
2 section 79, and amendments thereto, and a statement whether the guardian
3 has deviated from the plan and, if so, how the guardian has deviated and
4 why;
5 (12) plans for future care and support of the adult;
6 (13) a recommendation as to the need for continued guardianship and
7 any recommended change in the scope of the guardianship, including
8 whether the condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable
9 of exercising rights previously removed; and
10 (14) whether any co-guardian or successor guardian appointed to
11 serve when a designated event occurs is alive and able to serve.
12 (c) A guardian for an adult shall file a special report with the court
13 upon the occurrence of any of the following:
14 (1) A change of address of the guardian;
15 (2) a change of residence or placement of the adult;
16 (3) a significant change in the health or impairment of the adult;
17 (4) the acquisition by the adult of any real property, or the receipt or
18 accumulation of other property or income by the adult or by the guardian
19 on behalf of the adult, which causes the total value of the adult's estate to
20 equal or exceed $25,000;
21 (5) the death of the adult; or
22 (6) a change in the circumstances of the guardian or the adult that
23 may constitute a conflict of interest. A conflict of interest occurs where the
24 guardian has some personal, business or agency interest that could be
25 perceived as self-serving or adverse to the position or best interest of the
26 adult.
27 (d) The court may appoint a court liaison to review a report submitted
28 under this section or a guardian's plan submitted under section 79, and
29 amendments thereto, interview the guardian or adult subject to
30 guardianship or investigate any other matter involving the guardianship.
31 (e) Notice of the filing under this section of a guardian's report or
32 special report, together with a copy of the report, must be given to the
33 adult subject to guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section
34 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other
35 person the court determines. The notice and report must be given not later
36 than 14 days after the filing.
37 (f) The court shall establish procedures for monitoring a report
38 submitted under this section and review each report at least annually to
39 determine whether:
40 (1) The report provides sufficient information to establish the
41 guardian has complied with the guardian's duties;
42 (2) the guardianship should continue; and
43 (3) the guardian's requested fees, if any, should be approved.

HB 2359 58
1 (g) If the court determines that there is reason to believe a guardian
2 for an adult has not complied with the guardian's duties or the

4 (1) Shall notify the adult, the guardian and any other person entitled
5 to notice under section 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent

7 (2) may require additional information from the guardian;

10 (4) consistent with sections 81 and 82, and amendments thereto, may
11 hold a hearing to consider removal of the guardian, termination of the
12 guardianship or a change in the powers granted to the guardian or terms of
13 the guardianship.
14 (h) If the court has reason to believe fees requested by a guardian for

17 (i) A guardian for an adult may petition the court for approval of a
18 report filed under this section. The court after review may approve the

20 the report is accurate as to a matter adequately disclosed in the report.
21 New Sec. 81. (a) The court may remove a guardian for an adult for
22 failure to perform the guardian's duties or for other good cause and appoint
23 a successor guardian to assume the duties of guardian.
24 (b) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether to remove a
25 guardian for an adult and appoint a successor guardian on:
26 (1) Petition of the adult, guardian or person interested in the welfare
27 of the adult, which contains allegations that, if true, would support a
28 reasonable belief that removal of the guardian and appointment of a
29 successor guardian may be appropriate, but the court may decline to hold a
30 hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts was
31 filed during the preceding six months;
32 (2) communication from the adult, guardian or person interested in
33 the welfare of the adult which supports a reasonable belief that removal of
34 the guardian and appointment of a successor guardian may be appropriate;
35 (3) determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
36 interest of the adult; or
37 (4) determination by the court that the guardian's annual reports are
38 delinquent or deficient as filed.
39 (c) Notice of a petition under subsection (b)(1) or a hearing under this
40 section must be given to the adult subject to guardianship, the guardian, a
41 person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a
42 subsequent order, and any other person the court determines.
43 (d) If the adult subject to guardianship is not represented by an

HB 2359 59
1 attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the same conditions as

5 (e) In selecting a successor guardian for an adult, the court shall

11 New Sec. 82. (a) An adult subject to guardianship, the guardian for
12 the adult or a person interested in the welfare of the adult may petition for:
13 (1) Termination of the guardianship on the ground that a basis for
14 appointment under section 64, and amendments thereto, does not exist or
15 termination would be in the best interest of the adult or for other good
16 cause; or
17 (2) modification of the guardianship on the ground that the extent of
18 protection or assistance granted is not appropriate or for other good cause.
19 (b) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether termination
20 or modification of a guardianship for an adult is appropriate on:
21 (1) Petition under subsection (a) which contains allegations that, if
22 true, would support a reasonable belief that termination or modification of
23 the guardianship may be appropriate, but the court may decline to hold a
24 hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts was
25 filed during the preceding six months;
26 (2) communication from the adult, guardian or person interested in
27 the welfare of the adult which supports a reasonable belief that termination
28 or modification of the guardianship may be appropriate, including because
29 the functional needs of the adult or supports or services available to the
30 adult have changed;
31 (3) a report from a guardian or conservator which indicates that
32 termination or modification may be appropriate because the functional
33 needs of the adult or supports or services available to the adult have
34 changed or a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or other less
35 restrictive alternative for meeting the adult's needs is available; or
36 (4) a determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
37 interest of the adult.
38 (c) Notice of a petition under subsection (b)(1) or of a hearing under
39 this section must be given to the adult subject to guardianship, the
40 guardian, a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and amendments
41 thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court determines.
42 (d) After the hearing, the court shall order termination unless it is
43 proven that a basis for appointment of a guardian under section 64, and

HB 2359 60
1 amendments thereto, continues to exist.
2 (e) The court shall modify the powers granted to a guardian for an
3 adult if the powers are excessive or inadequate due to a change in the
4 abilities or limitations of the adult, the adult's supports or other
5 circumstances.
6 (f) Unless the court otherwise orders for good cause, before
7 terminating or modifying a guardianship for an adult, the court shall
8 follow the same procedures to safeguard the rights of the adult which
9 apply to a petition for guardianship.
10 (g) An adult subject to guardianship who seeks to terminate or
11 modify the terms of the guardianship has the right to choose an attorney to
12 represent the adult in the matter. If the adult is not represented by an
13 attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the same conditions as
14 in section 68, and amendments thereto. The court shall award reasonable
15 attorney fees to the attorney for the adult as provided in section 42, and
16 amendments thereto.
17 (h) Not later than 30 days after entering an order under this section,
18 the court or the court's designee shall give notice of the order to the adult
19 subject to guardianship and any person entitled to notice under section
20 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
21 New Sec. 83. (a) On petition and after notice and hearing, the court
22 may appoint a conservator for the property or financial affairs of a minor if
23 the court finds by a preponderance of evidence that the minor owns funds
24 or other property exceeding $25,000 in value derived from court
25 settlements, death transfers or sources other than the minor's employment
26 earnings or accounts established under the uniform transfers to minors act,
27 and either:
28 (1) The minor owns funds or other property requiring management or
29 protection that otherwise cannot be provided;
30 (2) the minor has or may have financial affairs that may be put at
31 unreasonable risk or hindered because of the minor's age; or
32 (3) appointment is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide funds
33 or other property needed for the support, care, education, health or welfare
34 of the minor.
35 (b) On petition and after notice and hearing, the court may appoint a
36 conservator for the property or financial affairs of an adult if the court
37 finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
38 (1) The adult is unable to manage property or financial affairs
39 because:
40 (A) Of a limitation in the adult's ability to receive and evaluate
41 information or make or communicate decisions, even with the use of
42 appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
43 decision making; or

HB 2359 61
1 (B) the adult is missing, detained or unable to return to the United
2 States;
3 (2) appointment is necessary to:
4 (A) Avoid harm to the adult or significant dissipation of the property
5 of the adult; or
6 (B) obtain or provide funds or other property needed for the support,
7 care, education, health or welfare of the adult or of an individual entitled to
8 the adult's support; and
9 (3) the adult's identified needs cannot be met by a protective
10 arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive alternative.
11 (c) The court shall grant a conservator only those powers necessitated
12 by demonstrated limitations and needs of the adult and issue orders that
13 will encourage development of the adult's maximum self-determination
14 and independence. The court may not establish a full conservatorship if a
15 limited conservatorship, protective arrangement instead of conservatorship
16 or other less restrictive alternative would meet the needs of the adult.
17 New Sec. 84. (a) The following may file a verified petition for the
18 appointment of a conservator:
19 (1) The individual for whom the order is sought;
20 (2) a person interested in the estate, financial affairs or welfare of the
21 individual, including a person that would be adversely affected by lack of
22 effective management of property or financial affairs of the individual; or
23 (3) the guardian for the individual.

25 principal residence, current street address if different, relationship to the
26 respondent, interest in the appointment, the name and address of any
27 attorney representing the petitioner and, to the extent known, the
28 following:

30 address if different and, if different, address of the dwelling in which it is
31 proposed the respondent will reside if the petition is granted;

38 nearest in kinship to the respondent who can be found with reasonable
39 diligence; and
40 (C) adult former stepchildren with whom the respondent had an
41 ongoing relationship during the two years immediately before the filing of
42 the petition;
43 (3) the name and current address of each of the following, if

22 New Sec. 85. (a) On filing of a petition under section 84, and
23 amendments thereto, for appointment of a conservator, the court shall set a
24 date, time and place for a hearing on the petition.
25 (b) A copy of a petition under section 84, and amendments thereto,
26 and notice of a hearing on the petition must be served personally on the
27 respondent. If the respondent's whereabouts are unknown or personal
28 service cannot be made, service on the respondent must be made by
29 substituted service, as ordered by the court. The notice must inform the
30 respondent of the respondent's rights at the hearing, including the right to
31 an attorney and to attend the hearing. The notice must include a
32 description of the nature, purpose and consequences of granting the
33 petition. The court may not grant a petition for appointment of a
34 conservator if notice substantially complying with this subsection is not
35 served on the respondent. The court may order any of the following
36 persons to serve the notice upon the respondent:
37 (1) The petitioner or the attorney for the petitioner;
38 (2) the attorney appointed by the court to represent the respondent;
39 (3) any law enforcement officer; or
40 (4) any other person whom the court finds to be a proper person to
41 serve this notice.
42 (c) In a proceeding on a petition under section 84, and amendments
43 thereto, the notice required under subsection (b) must be given to the

HB 2359 64
1 persons required to be listed in the petition under section 84(b)(1) through
2 (3), and amendments thereto, and any other person interested in the
3 respondent's welfare the court determines. Failure to give notice under this
4 subsection does not preclude the court from appointing a conservator.
5 (d) After the appointment of a conservator, notice of a hearing on a
6 petition for any other order under sections 83 through 118, and
7 amendments thereto, together with a copy of the petition, must be given to:
8 (1) The individual subject to conservatorship, if the individual is 12
9 years of age or older and not missing, detained or unable to return to the
10 United States;
11 (2) the conservator; and
12 (3) any other person the court determines.
13 New Sec. 86. While a petition under section 84, and amendments
14 thereto, is pending, after preliminary hearing and without notice to others,
15 the court may issue an order to preserve and apply property of the
16 respondent as required for the support of the respondent or an individual
17 who is in fact dependent on the respondent. The court may appoint an
18 emergency conservator to assist in implementing the order.
19 New Sec. 87. (a) If the respondent in a proceeding to appoint a
20 conservator is a minor, the court may appoint a court liaison to investigate
21 a matter related to the petition or inform the minor or a parent of the minor
22 about the petition or a related matter.
23 (b) If the respondent in a proceeding to appoint a conservator is an
24 adult, the court may appoint a court liaison. The duties and reporting
25 requirements of the court liaison are limited to the relief requested in the
26 petition. The court liaison must be an individual with training or
27 experience in the type of abilities, limitations and needs alleged in the
28 petition.
29 (c) (1) A court liaison appointed under subsection (b) for an adult
30 shall interview the respondent in person and in a manner the respondent is
31 best able to understand:
32 (A) Explain, in general, the petition, and the nature and purpose of
33 the proceeding, including the potential loss of rights as a result of the
34 proceeding; and
35 (B) obtain the respondent's views about the appointment sought by
36 the petitioner, including views about a proposed conservator, the
37 conservator's proposed powers and duties and the scope and duration of
38 the proposed conservatorship.
39 (2) These explanations and discussions are not intended to be a
40 substitute for the attorney appointed to represent the respondent to inform
41 the respondent of the respondent's rights and the nature and purpose of the
42 proceeding.
43 (d) A court liaison appointed under subsection (b) for an adult may be

HB 2359 65
1 assigned any or all of the following duties, in the discretion of the
2 presiding judge:
3 (1) Interview the petitioner and proposed conservator, if any;
4 (2) review financial records of the respondent, if relevant to the court
5 liaison's recommendation under subsection (e)(1);
6 (3) investigate whether the respondent's needs could be met by a
7 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive

10 (4) investigate the allegations in the petition and any other matter

12 to, the respondent's family relationships, past conduct, the nature and
13 extent of any property or income of the respondent, whether the
