40 New Sec. 88. (a) Unless the respondent in a proceeding for
41 appointment of a conservator is represented by an attorney, the court shall
42 appoint an attorney to represent the respondent, regardless of the
43 respondent's ability to pay. The court shall give preference in the

HB 2359 66
1 appointment of an attorney to any attorney who has represented the
2 respondent in other matters if the court has knowledge of that prior
3 representation or to an attorney whom the respondent has requested. Any
4 appointment made by the court shall terminate after the conservator's plan
5 has been approved and after any appeal from the appointment of a
6 conservator, unless the court continues the appointment by further order.
7 Thereafter, an attorney may be appointed by the court if requested, in
8 writing, by the adult subject to conservatorship, the conservator or upon
9 the court's own motion.
10 (b) An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding for
11 appointment of a conservator shall:
12 (1) Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes;
13 (2) advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably
14 ascertainable; and
15 (3) if the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable,
16 advocate for the result that is the least-restrictive in type, duration and
17 scope, consistent with the respondent's interests.
18 (c) An attorney representing the respondent shall interview the
19 respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to
20 understand:
21 (1) Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature,
22 purpose and effect of the proceeding, the respondent's rights at the hearing
23 on the petition and the general powers and duties of a conservator;
24 (2) determine the respondent's views about the appointment sought by
25 the petitioner, including views about a proposed conservator, the
26 conservator's proposed powers and duties and the scope and duration of
27 the proposed conservatorship; and
28 (3) inform the respondent that all costs and expenses of the
29 proceeding, including respondent's attorney fees, may be paid from the
30 respondent's assets.
31 (d) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent a parent of a
32 minor who is the subject of a proceeding under section 84, and
33 amendments thereto, if the court determines the parent needs
34 representation.
35 New Sec. 89. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
36 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
37 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a conservator, the court
38 shall order an examination and evaluation of the respondent to be
39 conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric hospital, community
40 mental health center or community developmental disability organization,
41 or by a licensed physician, psychiatrist, psychologist, physician assistant,
42 nurse practitioner, social worker or other professional appointed by the
43 court who is qualified to evaluate the respondent's alleged cognitive and

HB 2359 67
1 functional abilities and limitations and will not be advantaged or
2 disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition or otherwise have a
3 conflict of interest.
4 (b) Unless otherwise specified by the court, the report of the
5 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:
6 (1) The respondent's name, age and date of birth;
7 (2) a description of the respondent's physical and mental condition;
8 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
9 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
10 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
11 (4) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
12 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;
13 (5) a list and description of any prior assessments, evaluations or
14 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
15 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;
16 (6) the date and location where this examination and evaluation
17 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals
18 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
19 qualifications;
20 (7) a statement by the professional that the professional has
21 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
22 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results
23 of that examination and evaluation, and the professional's opinion with
24 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
25 conservator and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance
26 and participation at the hearing on the petition; and
27 (8) the signature of the professional who prepared the report.
28 (c) The professional shall file with the court, at least five days prior to
29 the date of the trial, such professional's written report concerning the
30 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made
31 available by the court to counsel for all parties.
32 (d) In lieu of entering an order for an examination and evaluation as
33 provided for in this section, the court may determine that the report
34 accompanying the petition is in compliance with the requirements of this
35 section and that no further examination or evaluation should be required,
36 unless the respondent, or such person's attorney, requests such an
37 examination and evaluation in writing. Any such request shall be filed with
38 the court, and a copy thereof delivered to the petitioner, at least four days
39 prior to the date of the trial. Accompanying the request shall be a statement
40 of the reasons why an examination and evaluation is requested and the
41 name and address of a qualified professional or facility willing and able to
42 conduct this examination and evaluation. If the court orders a further
43 examination and evaluation, the court may continue the trial and fix a new

HB 2359 68
1 date, time and place of the trial at a time not to exceed 30 days from the
2 date of the filing of the request.
3 New Sec. 90. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
4 hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, may not proceed unless
5 the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably feasible for the
6 respondent to attend a hearing at the location court proceedings typically
7 are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to hold the hearing at an
8 alternative location convenient to the respondent or allow the respondent
9 to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual technology.
10 (b) A hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, may
11 proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court finds by clear
12 and convincing evidence that:
13 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
14 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
15 of failing to do so;
16 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
17 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services or
18 technological assistance; or
19 (3) the respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and
20 attendance would be harmful to the minor.
21 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under section 85, and
22 amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the respondent's choosing,
23 assistive technology or an interpreter or translator, or a combination of
24 these supports. If assistance would facilitate the respondent's participation
25 in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to the respondent, the court
26 shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.
27 (d) The respondent has a right to retain an attorney to represent the
28 respondent at a hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto.
29 (e) At a hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, the
30 respondent may:
31 (1) Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents;
32 (2) examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator or
33 court liaison; and
34 (3) otherwise participate in the hearing.
35 (f) Unless excused by the court for good cause, a proposed
36 conservator shall attend a hearing under section 85, and amendments
37 thereto.
38 (g) A hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, must be
39 closed on request of the respondent and a showing of good cause.
40 (h) Any person may request to participate in a hearing under section
41 85, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the request, with or
42 without a hearing, on determining that the best interest of the respondent
43 will be served. The court may impose appropriate conditions on the

HB 2359 69
1 person's participation.
2 New Sec. 91. (a) The existence of a proceeding for or the existence of
3 conservatorship is a matter of public record unless the court seals the
4 record after:
5 (1) The respondent, the individual subject to conservatorship or the
6 parent of a minor subject to conservatorship requests the record be sealed;
7 and
8 (2) either:
9 (A) The petition for conservatorship is dismissed; or
10 (B) the conservatorship is terminated.
11 (b) (1) The following court records are a matter of public record
12 unless sealed by the court:
13 (A) Letters of conservatorship;
14 (B) orders suspending or removing a conservator; and
15 (C) orders terminating a conservatorship.
16 (2) All other court records of a conservatorship proceeding are not a
17 matter of public record except as further provided.
18 (3) The following persons may access court records of the proceeding
19 and resulting conservatorship, including the conservator's plan under
20 section 103, and amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under
21 section 105, and amendments thereto:
22 (A) An individual subject to a proceeding for a conservatorship,
23 whether or not a conservator is appointed;
24 (B) an attorney designated by the individual;
25 (C) a person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and amendments
26 thereto, or a subsequent order; and
27 (D) a licensed attorney, abstractor or title insurance agent.
28 (4) A person not otherwise entitled to access to court records under
29 this section for good cause may request permission from the court for
30 access to court records of the conservatorship, including the conservator's
31 plan and report. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest
32 of the respondent or individual subject to conservatorship or furthers the
33 public interest and does not endanger the welfare or financial interests of
34 the respondent or individual.
35 (c) A report under section 87, and amendments thereto, of a court
36 liaison or professional evaluation under section 89, and amendments
37 thereto, is confidential and must be sealed on filing, but is available to:
38 (1) The court;
39 (2) the individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation,
40 without limitation as to use;
41 (3) the petitioner, court liaison and petitioner's and respondent's
42 attorneys, for purposes of the proceeding;
43 (4) unless the court directs otherwise, an agent appointed under a

HB 2359 70
1 power of attorney for finances in which the respondent is identified as the
2 principal; and
3 (5) any other person if it is in the public interest or for a purpose the
4 court orders for good cause.
5 New Sec. 92. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
6 court in appointing a conservator shall consider persons qualified to be a
7 conservator in the following order of priority:
8 (1) A conservator, other than a temporary or emergency conservator,
9 currently acting for the respondent in another jurisdiction;
10 (2) a person nominated as conservator by the respondent, including
11 the respondent's most recent nomination made in a power of attorney for
12 finances;
13 (3) an agent appointed by the respondent to manage the respondent's
14 property under a power of attorney for finances;
15 (4) a spouse of the respondent;
16 (5) a family member or other individual who has shown special care
17 and concern for the respondent; and
18 (6) a person nominated as conservator by the spouse, adult child or
19 other close family member of the respondent.
20 (b) If two or more persons have equal priority under subsection (a),
21 the court shall select as conservator the person the court considers best
22 qualified. In determining the best qualified person, the court shall consider
23 the person's relationship with the respondent, the person's skills, the
24 expressed wishes of the respondent, the extent to which the person and the
25 respondent have similar values and preferences and the likelihood the
26 person will be able to perform the duties of a conservator successfully.
27 (c) The court, acting in the best interest of the respondent, may
28 decline to appoint as conservator a person having priority under subsection
29 (a) and appoint a person having a lower priority or no priority.
30 (d) The following persons shall not be appointed as conservator
31 unless the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that the person is
32 the best qualified person available for appointment and the appointment is
33 in the best interest of the respondent:
34 (1) A person that provides paid services to the respondent, or an
35 individual who is employed by a person that provides paid services to the
36 respondent, or is the spouse, parent or child of an individual who provides
37 or is employed to provide paid services to the respondent;
38 (2) an owner, operator or employee of any entity at which the
39 respondent is receiving care; and
40 (3) a person who provides care or other services, or is an employee of
41 an agency, partnership or corporation that provides care or other services
42 to persons with needs similar to those of the respondent.
43 New Sec. 93. (a) A court order appointing a conservator for a minor

HB 2359 71
1 must include findings to support appointment of a conservator.
2 (b) A court order appointing a conservator for an adult must:
3 (1) Include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence has
4 established that the identified needs of the respondent cannot be met by a
5 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive
6 alternative, including use of appropriate supportive services, technological
7 assistance or supported decision making; and
8 (2) include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence
9 established the respondent was given proper notice of the hearing on the
10 petition.
11 (c) A court order establishing a full conservatorship for an adult must
12 state the basis for granting a full conservatorship and include specific
13 findings to support the conclusion that a limited conservatorship would not
14 meet the functional needs of the adult.
15 (d) A court order establishing a limited conservatorship must state the
16 specific property placed under the control of the conservator and the
17 powers granted to the conservator.
18 (e) A court order appointing a conservator must include the date of a
19 review hearing to be set 90 days after the order of appointment is entered.
20 At that hearing, the court shall review the conservator's plan filed pursuant
21 to section 103, and amendments thereto, and the inventory filed pursuant
22 to section 104, and amendments thereto.
23 (f) The court, as part of an order establishing a conservatorship, shall
24 identify any person that subsequently is entitled to:
25 (1) Notice of the rights of the individual subject to conservatorship
26 under section 94(b), and amendments thereto;
27 (2) notice of a sale or other disposition of, encumbrance of an interest
28 in, or surrender of a lease to any real or personal property of the
29 individual;
30 (3) notice that the conservator will be unavailable to perform the
31 conservator's duties for more than one month;
32 (4) a copy of the conservator's plan under section 103, and
33 amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under section 105, and
34 amendments thereto;
35 (5) access to court records relating to the conservatorship;
36 (6) notice of a transaction involving a substantial conflict between the
37 conservator's fiduciary duties and personal interests;
38 (7) notice of the death or significant change in the condition of the
39 individual;
40 (8) notice that a petition has been filed to limit or modify the powers
41 of the conservator or that the court has limited or modified the powers of
42 the conservator; and
43 (9) notice that a petition has been filed to remove the conservator or

HB 2359 72
1 that the court has removed the conservator.
2 (g) If an individual subject to conservatorship is an adult, the spouse
3 and adult children of the adult subject to conservatorship are entitled under
4 subsection (e) to notice unless the court determines notice would be
5 contrary to the preferences or prior directions of the adult subject to
6 conservatorship or not in the best interest of the adult.
7 (h) If an individual subject to conservatorship is a minor, each parent
8 and adult sibling of the minor is entitled under subsection (e) to notice
9 unless the court determines notice would not be in the best interest of the
10 minor.
11 New Sec. 94. (a) Not later than 14 days after the appointment, a
12 conservator appointed under section 93, and amendments thereto, shall
13 give to the individual subject to conservatorship and to all other persons
14 given notice under section 85, and amendments thereto, a copy of the
15 order of appointment.
16 (b) Not later than 30 days after appointment of a conservator under
17 section 93, and amendments thereto, the court or the court's designee shall
18 give to the individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator, and any
19 other person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and amendments
20 thereto, a statement of the rights of the individual subject to
21 conservatorship and procedures to seek relief if the individual is denied
22 those rights. The statement must be in plain language, in at least 16-point
23 font, and to the extent feasible, in a language in which the individual
24 subject to conservatorship is proficient. The statement must notify the
25 individual subject to conservatorship of the right to:
26 (1) Seek termination or modification of the conservatorship, or
27 removal of the conservator, and choose an attorney to represent the
28 individual in these matters;
29 (2) file a grievance against the conservator under section 50, and
30 amendments thereto;
31 (3) participate in decision making to the extent reasonably feasible;
32 (4) receive a copy of the conservator's plan under section 103, and
33 amendments thereto, the conservator's inventory under section 104, and
34 amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under section 105, and
35 amendments thereto; and
36 (5) object to the conservator's inventory, plan or report.
37 (c) If a conservator is appointed for the reasons stated in section 83(b)
38 (1)(B), and amendments thereto, and the individual subject to
39 conservatorship is missing, notice under this section to the individual is
40 not required. If the individual subject to conservatorship is a minor under
41 the age of 12, notice under this section to the minor is not required.
42 (d) Any person required to provide notice under this section shall file
43 proof of service of such notice with the court.

HB 2359 73
1 New Sec. 95. (a) On its own after a petition has been filed under
2 section 84, and amendments thereto, or on a verified petition by a person
3 interested in an individual's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
4 conservator for the individual if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
5 establish probable cause that:
6 (1) Appointment of an emergency conservator is necessary to prevent
7 imminent, substantial and irreparable harm to the individual's property or
8 financial interests;
9 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
10 circumstances; and
11 (3) a basis for appointment of a conservator under section 83, and
12 amendments thereto, exists.
13 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency conservator may not
14 exceed 30 days and the emergency conservator may exercise only the
15 powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency conservator's
16 authority may be extended up to three times for not more than 30 days per
17 extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions for
18 appointment of an emergency conservator under subsection (a) continue.
19 (c) Immediately on filing of a petition for an emergency conservator,
20 the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the respondent in the
21 proceeding. Except as otherwise provided in subsection (d), reasonable
22 notice of the date, time and place of a hearing on the petition must be
23 given to the respondent, the respondent's attorney and any other person the
24 court determines.
25 (d) The court may appoint an emergency conservator without notice
26 to the respondent and any attorney for the respondent only if the court
27 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the respondent's property or
28 financial interests will be substantially and irreparably harmed before a
29 hearing with notice on the appointment can be held. If the court appoints
30 an emergency conservator without giving notice under subsection (c), the
31 court must give notice of the appointment not later than 48 hours after the
32 appointment to:
33 (1) The respondent;
34 (2) the respondent's attorney; and
35 (3) any other person the court determines.
36 (e) Not later than five days after the appointment, the court shall hold
37 a hearing on the appropriateness of the appointment.
38 (f) Appointment of an emergency conservator under this section is
39 not a determination that a basis exists for appointment of a conservator
40 under section 83, and amendments thereto.
41 (g) The court may remove an emergency conservator appointed under
42 this section at any time. The emergency conservator shall make any report
43 the court requires.

1 New Sec. 96. An individual subject to conservatorship or a person
2 interested in the welfare of the individual may petition for an order:
3 (a) Modifying bond requirements;
4 (b) requiring an accounting for the administration of the
5 conservatorship estate;
6 (c) directing distribution;
7 (d) removing the conservator and appointing a temporary or
8 successor conservator;
9 (e) modifying the type of appointment or powers granted to the
10 conservator, if the extent of protection or management previously granted
11 is excessive or insufficient to meet the individual's needs, including
12 because the individual's abilities or supports have changed;
13 (f) rejecting or modifying the conservator's plan under section 103,
14 and amendments thereto, the conservator's inventory under section 104,
15 and amendments thereto, or the conservator's report under section 105, and
16 amendments thereto; or
17 (g) granting other appropriate relief.
18 New Sec. 97. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
19 court shall require a conservator to furnish a bond with a surety, or require
20 an alternative asset-protection arrangement, conditioned on faithful
21 discharge of all duties of the conservator. The court may waive the
22 requirement only if the court finds that a bond or other asset-protection
23 arrangement is not necessary to protect the interests of the individual
24 subject to conservatorship. Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c),
25 the court may not waive the requirement if the conservator is in the
26 business of serving as a conservator and is being paid for the conservator's
27 service.
28 (b) Unless the court directs otherwise, the bond required under this
29 section must be in the amount of the aggregate capital value of the
30 conservatorship estate, plus one year's estimated income, less the value of
31 property deposited under an arrangement requiring a court order for its
32 removal, and less the value of real property. The court, in place of surety
33 on a bond, may accept collateral for the performance of the bond,
34 including a pledge of securities or a mortgage of real property.
35 (c) A regulated financial-service institution qualified to do trust
36 business in this state is not required to give a bond under this section.
37 (d) If the conservator appointed is under contract with the Kansas
38 guardianship program, the Kansas department for children and families
39 shall act as surety on the bond.
40 New Sec. 98. (a) The following rules apply to the bond required
41 under section 97, and amendments thereto:
42 (1) Except as otherwise provided by the bond, the surety and the
43 conservator are jointly and severally liable.

HB 2359 75
1 (2) By executing a bond provided by a conservator, the surety
2 submits to the personal jurisdiction of the court that issued letters of office
3 to the conservator in a proceeding relating to the duties of the conservator
4 in which the surety is named as a party. Notice of the proceeding must be
5 given to the surety at the address shown in the records of the court in
6 which the bond is filed and any other address of the surety then known to
7 the person required to provide the notice.
8 (3) On petition of a successor conservator or person affected by a

11 (4) A proceeding against the bond may be brought until liability

22 New Sec. 99. (a) A conservator is a fiduciary and has duties of
23 prudence, loyalty, reasonable care and diligence to the individual subject to
24 conservatorship.
25 (b) A conservator shall promote the self-determination of the
26 individual subject to conservatorship and, to the extent feasible, encourage
27 the individual to participate in decisions, act on the individual's own
28 behalf, and develop or regain the capacity to manage the individual's
29 personal affairs. A conservator shall strive to assure that the personal, civil
30 and human rights of the individual subject to conservatorship are
31 protected.
32 (c) In making a decision for an individual subject to conservatorship,
33 the conservator shall make the decision that the conservator reasonably
34 believes the individual would make if able, unless doing so would fail to
35 preserve the resources needed to maintain the individual's well-being and
36 lifestyle or otherwise unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or
37 personal or financial interests of the individual. To determine the decision
38 the individual would make if able, the conservator shall consider the
39 individual's prior or current directions, preferences, opinions, values and
40 actions, to the extent actually known or reasonably ascertainable by the
41 conservator.
42 (d) If a conservator cannot make a decision under subsection (c)
43 because the conservator does not know and cannot reasonably determine

HB 2359 76
1 the decision the individual subject to conservatorship probably would
2 make if able, or the conservator reasonably believes the decision the
3 individual would make would fail to preserve resources needed to
4 maintain the individual's well-being and lifestyle or otherwise
5 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
6 interests of the individual, the conservator shall act in accordance with the
7 best interest of the individual. In determining the best interest of the
8 individual, the conservator shall consider:
9 (1) Information received from professionals and persons that
10 demonstrate sufficient interest in the welfare of the individual;
11 (2) other information the conservator believes the individual would
12 have considered if the individual were able to act; and
13 (3) other factors a reasonable person in the circumstances of the
14 individual would consider, including consequences for others.
15 (e) Except when inconsistent with the conservator's duties under
16 subsections (a) through (d), a conservator shall invest and manage the
17 conservatorship estate as a prudent investor would, by considering:
18 (1) The circumstances of the individual subject to conservatorship
19 and the conservatorship estate;
20 (2) general economic conditions;
21 (3) the possible effect of inflation or deflation;
22 (4) the expected tax consequences of an investment decision or
23 strategy;
24 (5) the role of each investment or course of action in relation to the
25 conservatorship estate as a whole;
26 (6) the expected total return from income and appreciation of capital;
27 (7) the need for liquidity, regularity of income and preservation or
28 appreciation of capital; and
29 (8) the special relationship or value, if any, of specific property to the
30 individual subject to conservatorship.
31 (f) The propriety of a conservator's investment and management of
32 the conservatorship estate is determined in light of the facts and
33 circumstances existing when the conservator decides or acts and not by
34 hindsight.
35 (g) A conservator shall make a reasonable effort to verify facts
36 relevant to the investment and management of the conservatorship estate.
37 (h) A conservator that has special skills or expertise, or is named
38 conservator in reliance on the conservator's representation of special skills
39 or expertise, has a duty to use the special skills or expertise in carrying out
40 the conservator's duties.
41 (i) In investing, selecting specific property for distribution, and
42 invoking a power of revocation or withdrawal for the use or benefit of the
43 individual subject to conservatorship, a conservator shall consider any

HB 2359 77
1 estate plan of the individual known or reasonably ascertainable to the
2 conservator and may examine the will or other donative, nominative or
3 appointive instrument of the individual.
4 (j) A conservator shall maintain insurance on the insurable real and
5 personal property of the individual subject to conservatorship, unless the
6 conservatorship estate lacks sufficient funds to pay for insurance or the
7 court finds:
8 (1) The property lacks sufficient equity; or
9 (2) insuring the property would unreasonably dissipate the
10 conservatorship estate or otherwise not be in the best interest of the
11 individual.
12 (k) A conservator has access to and authority over a digital asset of
13 the individual subject to conservatorship to the extent provided by the
14 revised uniform fiduciary access to digital assets act or court order.
15 (l) A conservator for an adult shall notify the court immediately if the
16 condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable of exercising
17 rights previously removed.

3 New Sec. 103. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment, and
4 whenever there is a significant change in circumstances or the conservator
5 seeks to deviate significantly from the existing conservator's plan, a
6 conservator shall file with the court a plan for protecting, managing,
7 expending and distributing the assets of the conservatorship estate. The
8 plan must be based on the needs of the individual subject to
9 conservatorship and take into account the best interest of the individual as
10 well as the individual's preferences, values and prior directions, to the
11 extent known to or reasonably ascertainable by the conservator. The
12 conservator shall include in the plan:
13 (1) A budget containing projected expenses and resources, including
14 an estimate of the total amount of fees the conservator anticipates charging
15 per year and a statement or list of the amount the conservator proposes to
16 charge for each service the conservator anticipates providing to the
17 individual;
18 (2) how the conservator will involve the individual in decisions about
19 management of the conservatorship estate;
20 (3) any step the conservator plans to take to develop or restore the
21 ability of the individual to manage the conservatorship estate; and
22 (4) an estimate of the duration of the conservatorship.
23 (b) A conservator shall give notice of the filing of the conservator's
24 plan under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to the
25 individual subject to conservatorship, any attorney representing the
26 individual subject to conservatorship, a person entitled to notice under
27 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any
28 other person the court determines. The notice must include a statement of
29 the right to object to the plan and must be given at the time of the filing.
30 (c) An individual subject to conservatorship and any person entitled
31 under subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the conservator's plan
32 may object to the plan in writing not later than 21 days after the filing.
33 (d) The court shall review the conservator's plan filed under
34 subsection (a) and determine whether to approve the plan or require a new
35 plan. In deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall consider an
36 objection under subsection (c) and whether the plan is consistent with the
37 conservator's duties and powers. The court shall review an initial
38 conservator's plan at the review hearing scheduled under section 93(e), and
39 amendments thereto. For subsequent conservator's plans, the court has
40 discretion whether to set the matter for hearing but may not approve the
41 plan until 30 days after the filing.
42 (e) After a conservator's plan under this section is approved by the
43 court, the conservator shall provide a copy of the plan to the individual

1 subject to conservatorship, any attorney representing the individual subject

5 New Sec. 104. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment, a

23 determines.

1 (6) anything of more than de minimis value which the conservator,
2 any individual who resides with the conservator, or the spouse, parent,
3 child or sibling of the conservator has received from a person providing
4 goods or services to the individual subject to conservatorship;
5 (7) any business relation the conservator has with a person the

7 individual subject to conservatorship;
8 (8) whether any co-conservator or successor conservator appointed to

10 (9) a copy of the bond renewal.
11 (c) The court may appoint a court liaison to review a report under this
12 section or conservator's plan under section 103, and amendments thereto,
13 interview the individual subject to conservatorship or conservator, or
14 investigate any other matter involving the conservatorship. In connection
15 with the report, the court may order the conservator to submit the
16 conservatorship estate to appropriate examination in a manner the court
17 directs.
18 (d) Notice of the filing under this section of a conservator's report,
19 together with a copy of the report, must be provided to the individual
20 subject to conservatorship, a person entitled to notice under section 93(f),
21 and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and other persons the
22 court determines. The notice and report must be given not later than 14
23 days after filing.
24 (e) The court shall establish procedures for monitoring a report
25 submitted under this section and review each report at least annually to
26 determine whether:
27 (1) The reports provide sufficient information to establish the
28 conservator has complied with the conservator's duties;
29 (2) the conservatorship should continue; and
30 (3) the conservator's requested fees, if any, should be approved.
31 (f) If the court determines there is reason to believe a conservator has
32 not complied with the conservator's duties or the conservatorship should
33 not continue, the court:
34 (1) Shall notify the individual subject to conservatorship, the
35 conservator and any other person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and
36 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order;
37 (2) may require additional information from the conservator;
38 (3) may appoint a court liaison to interview the individual subject to
39 conservatorship or conservator or investigate any matter involving the
40 conservatorship; and
41 (4) consistent with sections 112 and 113, and amendments thereto,
42 may hold a hearing to consider removal of the conservator, termination of
43 the conservatorship or a change in the powers granted to the conservator or

HB 2359 85
1 terms of the conservatorship.
2 (g) If the court has reason to believe fees requested by a conservator
3 are not reasonable, the court shall hold a hearing to determine whether to
4 adjust the requested fees.
5 (h) A conservator may petition the court for approval of a report filed
6 under this section. The court after review may approve the report. If the
7 court approves the report, there is a rebuttable presumption the report is
8 accurate as to a matter adequately disclosed in the report.
9 (i) An order, after notice and hearing, approving an interim report of a
10 conservator filed under this section adjudicates liabilities concerning a
11 matter adequately disclosed in the report, as to a person given notice of the
12 report or accounting.
13 (j) An order, after notice and hearing, approving a final report filed
14 under this section discharges the conservator from all liabilities, claims
15 and causes of action by a person given notice of the report and the hearing
16 as to a matter adequately disclosed in the report.
17 New Sec. 106. (a) The interest of an individual subject to
18 conservatorship in property included in the conservatorship estate is not
19 transferrable or assignable by the individual and is not subject to levy,
20 garnishment, or similar process for claims against the individual unless
21 allowed under section 110, and amendments thereto.
22 (b) If an individual subject to conservatorship enters into a contract
23 after having the right to enter the contract removed by the court, the
24 contract is void against the individual and the individual's property but is
25 enforceable against the person that contracted with the individual.
26 (c) A person other than the conservator that deals with an individual
27 subject to conservatorship with respect to property included in the
28 conservatorship estate is entitled to protection provided by law of this state
29 other than this act.
30 New Sec. 107. A transaction involving a conservatorship estate which
31 is affected by a substantial conflict between the conservator's fiduciary
32 duties and personal interests is voidable unless the transaction is
33 authorized by court order after notice to persons entitled to notice under
34 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order. A
35 transaction affected by a substantial conflict includes a sale, encumbrance
36 or other transaction involving the conservatorship estate entered into by
37 the conservator, an individual with whom the conservator resides, the
38 spouse, descendant, sibling, agent or attorney of the conservator, or a
39 corporation or other enterprise in which the conservator has a substantial
40 beneficial interest.
41 New Sec. 108. (a) A person that assists or deals with a conservator in
42 good faith and for value in any transaction, other than a transaction
43 requiring a court order under section 102, and amendments thereto, is

HB 2359 86
1 protected as though the conservator properly exercised any power in
2 question. Knowledge alone by a person that the person is dealing with a
3 conservator does not require the person to inquire into the existence of
4 authority of the conservator or the propriety of the conservator's exercise
5 of authority, but restrictions on authority stated in letters of office, or
6 otherwise provided by law, are effective as to the person. A person that
7 pays or delivers property to a conservator is not responsible for proper
8 application of the property.
9 (b) Protection under subsection (a) extends to a procedural
10 irregularity or jurisdictional defect in the proceeding leading to the
11 issuance of letters of office and does not substitute for protection for a
12 person that assists or deals with a conservator provided by comparable
13 provisions in law of this state other than this act relating to a commercial
14 transaction or simplifying a transfer of securities by a fiduciary.
15 New Sec. 109. (a) If an individual subject to conservatorship dies, the
16 conservator shall deliver to the district court any will of the individual that
17 is in the conservator's possession and inform the personal representative
18 named in the will if feasible. The conservator shall give notice of the
19 delivery of the will under this section to any person entitled to notice under
20 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
21 (b) On the death of an individual subject to conservatorship, the
22 conservator shall conclude the administration of the conservatorship estate
23 as provided in section 113, and amendments thereto.
24 New Sec. 110. (a) A conservator may pay a claim against the
25 conservatorship estate or the individual subject to conservatorship arising
26 before or during the conservatorship, on presentation and allowance in
27 accordance with the priorities under subsection (d). A claimant may
28 present a claim by:
29 (1) Sending or delivering to the conservator a statement in a record of
30 the claim, indicating its basis, the name and address of the claimant and
31 the amount claimed; or
32 (2) filing the claim with the court, in a form acceptable to the court,
33 and sending or delivering a copy of the claim to the conservator.
34 (b) A claim under subsection (a) is presented on receipt by the
35 conservator of the statement of the claim or the filing with the court of the
36 claim, whichever occurs first. A presented claim is allowed, if it is not
37 disallowed in whole or in part, by the conservator in a record sent or
38 delivered to the claimant not later than 60 days after its presentation.
39 Before payment, the conservator may change an allowance of the claim to
40 a disallowance in whole or in part, but not after allowance under a court
41 order or order directing payment of the claim. Presentation of a claim tolls
42 until 30 days after disallowance of the claim the running of a statute of
43 limitations that has not expired relating to the claim.

HB 2359 87
1 (c) A claimant whose claim under subsection (a) has not been paid
2 may petition the court to determine the claim at any time before it is barred
3 by a statute of limitations, and the court may order its allowance, payment
4 or security by encumbering property included in the conservatorship
5 estate. If a proceeding is pending against the individual subject to
6 conservatorship at the time of appointment of the conservator or is
7 initiated thereafter, the moving party shall give the conservator notice of
8 the proceeding if it could result in creating a claim against the
9 conservatorship estate.
10 (d) If a conservatorship estate is likely to be exhausted before all
11 existing claims are paid, the conservator shall distribute the estate in
12 money or in kind in payment of claims in the following order:
13 (1) Costs and expenses of administration;
14 (2) a claim of the federal or state government having priority under
15 law other than this act;
16 (3) a claim incurred by the conservator for support, care, education,
17 health or welfare previously provided to the individual subject to
18 conservatorship or an individual who is in fact dependent on the individual
19 subject to conservatorship;
20 (4) a claim arising before the conservatorship; and
21 (5) all other claims.
22 (e) Preference may not be given in the payment of a claim under
23 subsection (d) over another claim of the same class. A claim due and
24 payable may not be preferred over a claim not due unless:
25 (1) Doing so would leave the conservatorship estate without
26 sufficient funds to pay the basic living and healthcare expenses of the
27 individual subject to conservatorship; and
28 (2) the court authorizes the preference under section 102(a)(8), and
29 amendments thereto.
30 (f) If assets of a conservatorship estate are adequate to meet all
31 existing claims, the court, acting in the best interest of the individual
32 subject to conservatorship, may order the conservator to grant a security
33 interest in the conservatorship estate for payment of a claim at a future
34 date.
35 New Sec. 111. (a) Except as otherwise agreed by a conservator, the
36 conservator is not personally liable on a contract properly entered into in a
37 fiduciary capacity in the course of administration of the conservatorship
38 estate unless the conservator fails to reveal the conservator's representative
39 capacity in the contract or before entering into the contract.
40 (b) A conservator is personally liable for an obligation arising from
41 control of property of the conservatorship estate or an act or omission
42 occurring in the course of administration of the conservatorship estate only
43 if the conservator is personally at fault.

HB 2359 88
1 (c) A claim based on a contract entered into by a conservator in a
2 fiduciary capacity, an obligation arising from control of property included
3 in the conservatorship estate, or a tort committed in the course of
4 administration of the conservatorship estate may be asserted against the
5 conservatorship estate in a proceeding against the conservator in a
6 fiduciary capacity, whether or not the conservator is personally liable for
7 the claim.
8 (d) A question of liability between a conservatorship estate and the
9 conservator personally may be determined in a proceeding for accounting,
10 surcharge, or indemnification or another appropriate proceeding or action.
11 New Sec. 112. (a) The court may remove a conservator for failure to
12 perform the conservator's duties or other good cause and appoint a
13 successor conservator to assume the duties of the conservator.
14 (b) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether to remove a
15 conservator and appoint a successor on:
16 (1) Petition of the individual subject to conservatorship, conservator
17 or person interested in the welfare of the individual which contains
18 allegations that, if true, would support a reasonable belief that removal of
19 the conservator and appointment of a successor may be appropriate, but
20 the court may decline to hold a hearing if a petition based on the same or
21 substantially similar facts was filed during the preceding six months;
22 (2) communication from the individual subject to conservatorship,
23 conservator or person interested in the welfare of the individual which
24 supports a reasonable belief that removal of the conservator and
25 appointment of a successor may be appropriate;
26 (3) determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
27 interest of the individual subject to conservatorship; or
28 (4) determination by the court that the conservator's reports and
29 accountings are delinquent or deficient as filed.
30 (c) Notice of a petition under subsection (b)(1) or any hearing under
31 this section must be given to the individual subject to conservatorship, the
32 conservator, a person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and
33 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
34 determines.
35 (d) If the individual subject to conservatorship is not represented by
36 an attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the same conditions
37 as in section 88, and amendments thereto. The court shall award
38 reasonable attorney fees to the attorney as provided in section 42, and
39 amendments thereto.
40 (e) In selecting a successor conservator, the court shall follow the
41 priorities under section 92, and amendments thereto.
42 (f) Not later than 30 days after appointing a successor conservator,
43 the court or court's designee shall give notice of the appointment to the

HB 2359 89
1 individual subject to conservatorship and any person entitled to notice
2 under section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
3 New Sec. 113. (a) A conservatorship for a minor terminates on the
4 earliest of:
5 (1) A court order terminating the conservatorship;
6 (2) the minor becoming an adult except as provided in section 114,
7 and amendments thereto;
8 (3) emancipation of the minor; or
9 (4) death of the minor.
10 (b) A conservatorship for an adult terminates on order of the court or
11 when the adult dies.
12 (c) An individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator, or a
13 person interested in the welfare of the individual may petition for:
14 (1) Termination of the conservatorship on the ground that a basis for
15 appointment under section 83, and amendments thereto, does not exist or
16 termination would be in the best interest of the individual or for other good
17 cause; or
18 (2) modification of the conservatorship on the ground that the extent
19 of protection or assistance granted is not appropriate or for other good
20 cause.
21 (d) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether termination
22 or modification of a conservatorship is appropriate on:
23 (1) Petition under subsection (c) which contains allegations that, if
24 true, would support a reasonable belief that termination or modification of
25 the conservatorship may be appropriate, but the court may decline to hold
26 a hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts was
27 filed within the preceding six months;
28 (2) a communication from the individual subject to conservatorship,
29 conservator or person interested in the welfare of the individual which
30 supports a reasonable belief that termination or modification of the
31 conservatorship may be appropriate, including because the functional
32 needs of the individual or supports or services available to the individual
33 have changed;
34 (3) a report from a guardian or conservator which indicates that
35 termination or modification may be appropriate because the functional
36 needs or supports or services available to the individual have changed or a
37 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive
38 alternative is available; or
39 (4) a determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
40 interest of the individual.
41 (e) Notice of a petition under subsection (c) or of a hearing under this
42 section must be given to the individual subject to conservatorship, the
43 conservator, a person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and

HB 2359 90
1 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
2 determines.
3 (f) After the hearing, the court shall order termination unless it is
4 proven that a basis for appointment of a conservator under section 83, and
5 amendments thereto, continues to exist.
6 (g) The court shall modify the powers granted to a conservator if the
7 powers are excessive or inadequate due to a change in the abilities or
8 limitations of the individual subject to conservatorship, the individual's
9 supports or other circumstances.
10 (h) Unless the court otherwise orders for good cause, before
11 terminating a conservatorship, the court shall follow the same procedures
12 to safeguard the rights of the individual subject to conservatorship which
13 apply to a petition for conservatorship.
14 (i) An individual subject to conservatorship who seeks to terminate or
15 modify the terms of the conservatorship has the right to retain an attorney
16 to represent the individual in this matter. If the individual is not
17 represented by an attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the
18 same conditions as in section 88, and amendments thereto. The court shall
19 award reasonable attorney fees to the attorney as provided in section 42,
20 and amendments thereto.
21 (j) On termination of a conservatorship other than by reason of the
22 death of the individual subject to conservatorship, property of the
23 conservatorship estate passes to the individual. The order of termination
24 must direct the conservator to file a final report and petition for discharge
25 on approval by the court of the final report.
26 (k) On termination of a conservatorship by reason of the death of the
27 individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator promptly shall file a
28 final report and petition for discharge on approval by the court of the final
29 report. On approval of the final report, the conservator shall proceed
30 expeditiously to distribute the conservatorship estate to the individual's
31 estate or as otherwise ordered by the court. The conservator may take
32 reasonable measures necessary to preserve the conservatorship estate until
33 distribution can be made.
34 (l) The court shall issue a final order of discharge on the approval by
35 the court of the final report and satisfaction by the conservator of any other
36 condition the court imposed on the conservator's discharge.
37 (m) Not later than 30 days after entering an order under this section,
38 the court or the court's designee shall give notice of the order to the adult
39 subject to conservatorship and any person entitled to notice under section
40 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
41 New Sec. 114. (a) A conservatorship for a minor may be extended
42 beyond the minor's 18th birthday if the minor consents or the court finds by
43 clear and convincing evidence that substantial harm to the minor's interests

HB 2359 91
1 is otherwise likely. A conservatorship may be extended under this section
2 until the minor reaches the age of 21 and may be extended for two
3 additional two-year periods upon the same finding by the court or upon
4 consent of the minor. Consent to the extension of a conservatorship may be
5 withdrawn at any time.
6 (b) Any request to extend a minor conservatorship under this section
7 must be accompanied by:
8 (1) A description of the funds or assets of the minor's estate which the
9 conservator proposes to distribute to the minor over an extended period
10 following the minor's 18th birthday;
11 (2) the factual basis upon which the conservator alleges the need for
12 such an extended distribution plan; and
13 (3) a proposed conservator's plan that describes how the distribution
14 will occur.
15 (c) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent the minor as
16 provided in section 88, and amendments thereto.
17 (d) After a hearing, the court may extend a conservatorship for a
18 minor and grant to the conservator the authority to establish an extended
19 distribution plan if the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
20 (1) Substantial harm to the minor's interests is likely if the
21 conservatorship is not extended; and
22 (2) the plan approved by the court adequately provides for meeting
23 the expected needs of the minor from the minor's 18th birthday until the
24 final distribution of the funds or assets which the court authorizes to be set
25 aside or transferred from the estate are paid over to the minor, including
26 provisions for accelerated distribution in extraordinary circumstances,
27 which may require court approval.
28 (e) If the court orders a conservatorship for a minor to be extended
29 under this section, the court shall order the conservator to report any
30 expenditure or transfer of funds or assets from the minor's estate for the
31 purposes of effectuating an extended distribution plan within the
32 conservator's next accounting.
33 (f) The court may extend the conservatorship with regard to specific
34 funds or assets of the minor's estate, even though other funds or assets of
35 the minor's estate are paid over to the minor upon the minor's becoming 18
36 years of age.
37 (g) The minor shall be without the power, voluntarily or involuntarily,
38 to sell, mortgage, pledge, hypothecate, assign, alienate, anticipate, transfer
39 or convey any interest in the principal or the income from any funds or
40 assets of the minor's estate set aside or transferred to effectuate a plan for
41 extended distribution until such is actually paid to the minor.
42 New Sec. 115. (a) Unless a person required to transfer funds or other
43 property to a minor knows that a conservator for the minor has been

HB 2359 92
1 appointed or a proceeding is pending for conservatorship, the person may
2 transfer an amount or value not exceeding $25,000 in a 12-month period
3 to:
4 (1) A person that has care or custody of the minor and with whom the
5 minor resides;
6 (2) a guardian for the minor;
7 (3) a custodian under the uniform transfers to minors act; or
8 (4) a financial institution as a deposit in an interest-bearing account or
9 certificate solely in the name of the minor and shall give notice to the
10 minor of the deposit.
11 (b) A person that transfers funds or other property under this section
12 is not responsible for its proper application.
13 (c) A person that receives funds or other property for a minor under
14 subsection (a)(1) or (2) may apply it only to the support, care, education,
15 health or welfare of the minor, and may not derive a personal financial
16 benefit from it, except for reimbursement for necessary expenses. Funds
17 not applied for these purposes must be preserved for the future support,
18 care, education, health or welfare of the minor, and the balance, if any,
19 transferred to the minor when the minor becomes an adult or otherwise is
20 emancipated.
21 (d) Any accumulated balance under this section shall be subject to
22 other provisions of this act.
23 New Sec. 116. The parent of a minor has the right and responsibility
24 to hold in trust and manage for the minor's benefit all of the personal and
25 real property vested in such minor when the total of such property does not
26 exceed $25,000 in value, unless a guardian or conservator has been
27 appointed for the minor.
28 New Sec. 117. (a) Any court having either control over or possession
29 of any amount of money not exceeding $100,000, the right to which is
30 vested in a minor, shall have the discretion to authorize, without the
31 appointment of a conservator or the giving of bond, and notwithstanding
32 the authority of a parent as provided for in section 116, and amendments
33 thereto, the deposit of the money in a savings account of a bank, credit
34 union, savings and loan association or any other investment account that
35 the court may authorize, payable either to a conservator, if one shall be
36 appointed for the minor, or to the minor upon attaining 18 years of age.
37 (b) Any court having either control over or possession of any amount
38 of money not exceeding $25,000, the right to which is vested in a minor,
39 shall have the discretion to order the payment of the money to any person,
40 including the parent of the minor, or the minor. If the person is the
41 conservator for the minor, the court may waive or recommend the waiver
42 of the requirement of a bond. If the person is anyone other than the minor,
43 the court shall order that person to hold in trust and manage the minor's

HB 2359 93
1 estate for the minor's benefit.
2 New Sec. 118. Any court having either control over or possession of
3 any amount of money not exceeding $25,000, the right to which is vested
4 in an adult subject to guardianship, shall have the discretion to authorize,
5 without the appointment of a conservator or the giving of bond, the deposit
6 of the money in a savings account of a bank, credit union or savings and
7 loan association, payable to the guardian for the benefit of the adult subject
8 to guardianship if authorized pursuant to section 78(c), and amendments
9 thereto, payable to a conservator, if one shall be appointed for the adult, or

11 guardianship.
12 New Sec. 119. (a) On receiving a petition for a guardianship for an
13 adult, a court may order a protective arrangement instead of guardianship
14 as a less restrictive alternative to guardianship.
15 (b) On receiving a petition for a conservatorship for an individual, a
16 court may order a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship as a
17 less restrictive alternative to conservatorship.
18 (c) A person interested in an adult's welfare, including the adult or a
19 conservator for the adult, may petition under sections 119 through 130,
20 and amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of
21 guardianship.
22 (d) The following persons may petition under sections 119 through
23 130, and amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of
24 conservatorship:
25 (1) The individual for whom the protective arrangement is sought;
26 (2) a person interested in the property, financial affairs or welfare of
27 the individual, including a person that would be affected adversely by lack
28 of effective management of property or financial affairs of the individual;
29 and
30 (3) the guardian for the individual.
31 New Sec. 120. (a) After the hearing on a petition under section 65,
32 and amendments thereto, for a guardianship or under section 119(b), and
33 amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship,
34 the court may issue an order under subsection (b) for a protective
35 arrangement instead of guardianship if the court finds by clear and
36 convincing evidence that:
37 (1) The respondent lacks the ability to meet essential requirements for
38 physical health, safety or self-care because the respondent is unable to
39 receive and evaluate information or make or communicate decisions, even
40 with appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
41 decision making; and
42 (2) the respondent's identified needs cannot be met by a less
43 restrictive alternative.

HB 2359 94
1 (b) If the court makes the findings under subsection (a), the court,
2 instead of appointing a guardian, may:
3 (1) Authorize or direct a transaction necessary to meet the
4 respondent's need for health, safety or care, including:
5 (A) A particular medical treatment or refusal of a particular medical
6 treatment;
7 (B) a move to a specified place of dwelling; or
8 (C) visitation between the respondent and another person;
9 (2) order supervised visitation with, or restrict access to the
10 respondent by, a specified person whose access places the respondent at
11 serious risk of physical, psychological or financial harm; and
12 (3) order other arrangements on a limited basis that are appropriate.
13 (c) In deciding whether to issue an order under this section, the court
14 shall consider the factors under sections 76 and 77, and amendments
15 thereto, which a guardian must consider when making a decision on behalf
16 of an adult subject to guardianship.
17 (d) Any order issued under this section may include reporting
18 requirements, time limits, bond requirements or any other provisions
19 deemed necessary by the court.
20 New Sec. 121. (a) After the hearing on a petition under section 84,

37 care, education, health or welfare of the adult or an individual entitled to
38 the adult's support; and

1 conservatorship for a minor, the court may issue an order under subsection
2 (c) for a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship for the

5 (1) If the minor has a parent, the court gives weight to any

8 (2) either:
9 (A) The minor owns money or property requiring management or

11 (B) the minor has or may have financial affairs that may be put at

1 control caused or attempted to cause an action that would have resulted in

5 (e) Before issuing an order under subsection (c) or (d), the court shall

9 (f) Before issuing an order under subsection (c) or (d) for a
10 respondent who is a minor, the court also shall consider the best interest of
11 the minor, the preference of the parents of the minor and the preference of
12 the minor, if the minor is 12 years of age or older.
13 (g) Any order issued under this section may include reporting
14 requirements, time limits, bond requirements or any other provisions
15 deemed necessary by the court.
16 New Sec. 122. A verified petition for a protective arrangement
17 instead of guardianship or conservatorship must state the petitioner's name,

8 New Sec. 123. (a) On filing of a petition under section 119, and
9 amendments thereto, the court shall set a date, time and place for a hearing
10 on the petition.
11 (b) A copy of a petition under section 119, and amendments thereto,
12 and notice of a hearing on the petition must be served personally on the
13 respondent. The notice must inform the respondent of the respondent's
14 rights at the hearing, including the right to an attorney and to attend the
15 hearing. The notice must include a description of the nature, purpose and
16 consequences of granting the petition. The court may not grant the petition
17 if notice substantially complying with this subsection is not served on the
18 respondent. The court may order any of the following persons to serve the
19 notice upon the respondent:
20 (1) The petitioner or the attorney for the petitioner;
21 (2) the attorney appointed by the court to represent the respondent;
22 (3) any law enforcement officer; or
23 (4) any other person whom the court finds to be a proper person to
24 serve this notice.
25 (c) In a proceeding on a petition under section 119, and amendments
26 thereto, the notice required under subsection (b) must be given to the
27 persons required to be listed in the petition under section 122(a) through
28 (c), and amendments thereto, and any other person interested in the
29 respondent's welfare the court determines. Failure to give notice under this
30 subsection does not preclude the court from granting the petition.
31 (d) After the court has ordered a protective arrangement under
32 sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, notice of a hearing on
33 a petition for any other order filed under this act, together with a copy of
34 the petition, must be given to the respondent and any other person the
35 court determines.
36 New Sec. 124. (a) On filing of a petition under section 119, and
37 amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship,
38 the court may appoint a court liaison. The court liaison must be an
39 individual with training or experience in the type of abilities, limitations
40 and needs alleged in the petition.
41 (b) On filing of a petition under section 119, and amendments thereto,
42 for a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship for a minor, the
43 court may appoint a court liaison to investigate a matter related to the

HB 2359 99
1 petition or inform the minor or a parent of the minor about the petition or a
2 related matter.
3 (c) On filing of a petition under section 119, and amendments thereto,
4 for a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship for an adult, the
5 court may appoint a court liaison. The court liaison must be an individual
6 with training or experience in the types of abilities, limitations and needs
7 alleged in the petition.
8 (d) A court liaison appointed under subsection (a) or (c) shall
9 interview the respondent in person and in a manner the respondent is best
10 able to understand:
11 (1) Explain, in general, the petition, and the nature and purpose of the
12 proceeding including the potential loss of rights as a result of the
13 proceeding;
14 (2) obtain the respondent's views with respect to the order sought;
15 (3) if the petitioner seeks an order related to the dwelling of the
16 respondent, visit the respondent's present dwelling and any dwelling in
17 which it is reasonably believed the respondent will live if the order is
18 granted;

20 obtain information from any physician or other provider known to have
21 treated, advised or assessed the respondent's relevant physical or mental
22 condition, to the extent that such information has not already been
23 provided to the court;
24 (5) if a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is sought,
25 review financial records of the respondent, if relevant to the court liaison's
26 recommendation under subsection (e)(2); and

28 relating to the petition as directed by the court, including, but not limited
29 to, the respondent's family relationships, past conduct, the nature and
30 extent of any property or income of the respondent, whether the
31 respondent is likely to injure self or others and other matters as the court
32 may specify.

34 the court at least 10 days prior to the hearing on the petition or other

38 independent-living tasks and financial-management tasks the respondent:
39 (A) Can manage without assistance or with existing supports;
40 (B) could manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive
41 services, technological assistance or supported decision making; and
42 (C) cannot manage;
43 (2) a recommendation regarding the appropriateness of the protective

HB 2359 100
1 arrangement sought and whether a less restrictive alternative for meeting
2 the respondent's needs is available;

6 preference as to the respondent's dwelling;

15 New Sec. 125. (a) Unless the respondent in a proceeding under
16 sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, is represented by an
17 attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the respondent,
18 regardless of the respondent's ability to pay. The court shall give
19 preference in the appointment of an attorney to an attorney whom the
20 respondent has requested or to any attorney who has represented the
21 respondent in other matters if the court has knowledge of that prior
22 representation.
23 (b) An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding under
24 sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, shall:
25 (1) Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes;
26 (2) advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably
27 ascertainable; and
28 (3) if the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable,
29 advocate for the result that is the least restrictive alternative in type,
30 duration and scope, consistent with the respondent's interests.

32 who is the subject of a proceeding under sections 119 through 130, and
33 amendments thereto, if:
34 (1) The parent objects to the entry of an order for a protective
35 arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship;
36 (2) the court determines that counsel is needed to ensure that consent
37 to the entry of an order for a protective arrangement is informed; or
38 (3) the court otherwise determines the parent needs representation.
39 (d) An attorney representing the respondent shall interview the

41 understand:
42 (1) Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature,
43 purpose and effect of the proceeding, and the respondent's rights at the

1 hearing on the petition;
2 (2) determine the respondent's views about the order sought by the

7 New Sec. 126. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
8 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
9 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a protective
10 arrangement, the court shall order an examination and evaluation of the
11 respondent to be conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric
12 hospital, community mental health center, or community developmental
13 disability organization, or by a licensed physician, psychiatrist,
14 psychologist, physician assistant, nurse practitioner, social worker or other
15 professional appointed by the court who is qualified to evaluate the
16 respondent's alleged cognitive and functional abilities and limitations and
17 will not be advantaged or disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition
18 or otherwise have a conflict of interest.
19 (b) Unless otherwise specified by the court, the report of the
20 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:
21 (1) The respondent's name, age and date of birth;
22 (2) a description of the respondent's physical and mental condition;
23 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
24 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
25 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
26 (4) a summary of self-care and independent-living tasks the
27 respondent can manage without assistance or with existing supports, could
28 manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive services,
29 technological assistance or supported decision making, and cannot
30 manage;
31 (5) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
32 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;
33 (6) a list and description of any prior assessments, evaluations or
34 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
35 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;
36 (7) the date and location where this examination and evaluation
37 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals
38 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
39 qualifications;
40 (8) a statement by the professional that the professional has
41 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
42 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results
43 of that examination and evaluation, and the professional's opinion with

HB 2359 102
1 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
2 guardian and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance and
3 participation at the hearing on the petition; and
4 (9) the signature of the professional who prepared the report.
5 (c) The professional shall file with the court, at least five days prior to
6 the date of the trial, such professional's written report concerning the
7 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made
8 available by the court to counsel for all parties.
9 (d) In lieu of entering an order for an examination and evaluation as
10 provided for in this section, the court may determine that the report
11 accompanying the petition is in compliance with the requirements of this
12 section and that no further examination or evaluation should be required,
13 unless the respondent, or such person's attorney, requests such an
14 examination and evaluation in writing. Any such request shall be filed with
15 the court, and a copy thereof delivered to the petitioner, at least four days
16 prior to the date of the trial. Accompanying the request shall be a statement
17 of the reasons why an examination and evaluation is requested and the
18 name and address of a qualified professional or facility willing and able to
19 conduct this examination and evaluation. If the court orders a further
20 examination and evaluation, the court may continue the trial and fix a new
21 date, time and place of the trial at a time not to exceed 30 days from the
22 date of the filing of the request.
23 New Sec. 127. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
24 hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, may not
25 proceed unless the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably
26 feasible for the respondent to attend a hearing at the location where court
27 proceedings typically are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to
28 hold the hearing at an alternative location convenient to the respondent or
29 allow the respondent to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual
30 technology.
31 (b) A hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
32 thereto, may proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court
33 finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
34 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
35 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
36 of failing to do so;
37 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
38 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services and
39 technological assistance; or
40 (3) the respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and
41 attendance would be harmful to the minor.
42 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under sections 119
43 through 130, and amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the

HB 2359 103
1 respondent's choosing, assistive technology or an interpreter or translator,
2 or a combination of these supports. If assistance would facilitate the
3 respondent's participation in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to
4 the respondent, the court shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.
5 (d) The respondent has a right to retain an attorney to represent the
6 respondent at a hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
7 thereto.
8 (e) At a hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
9 thereto, the respondent may:
10 (1) Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents;
11 (2) examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and
12 the court liaison; and
13 (3) otherwise participate in the hearing.
14 (f) A hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
15 thereto, must be closed on request of the respondent and a showing of
16 good cause.
17 (g) Any person may request to participate in a hearing under sections
18 119 through 130, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the
19 request, with or without a hearing, on determining that the best interest of
20 the respondent will be served. The court may impose appropriate
21 conditions on the person's participation.
