27 New Sec. 129. (a) The existence of a proceeding for or the existence
28 of a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship is a
29 matter of public record unless the court seals the record after:
30 (1) The respondent, the individual subject to the protective
31 arrangement, or the parent of a minor subject to the protective arrangement
32 requests the record be sealed; and
33 (2) either:
34 (A) The proceeding is dismissed;
35 (B) the protective arrangement is no longer in effect; or
36 (C) an act authorized by the order granting the protective arrangement
37 has been completed.
38 (b) (1) An order of protective arrangement is a matter of public record
39 unless sealed by the court. All other court records of the proceeding
40 relating to the protective arrangement are not a matter of public record
41 except as further provided.
42 (2) The following persons may access court records of the proceeding
43 and resulting protective arrangement:

HB 2359 104
1 (A) A respondent;
2 (B) an individual subject to a protective arrangement instead of
3 guardianship or conservatorship;
4 (C) an attorney designated by the respondent or individual;
5 (D) a parent of a minor subject to a protective arrangement; and
6 (E) a licensed attorney, abstractor, or title insurance agent.
7 (3) A person not otherwise entitled to access to court records under
8 this subsection for good cause may request permission from the court for
9 access. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest of the
10 respondent or individual subject to the protective arrangement or furthers
11 the public interest and does not endanger the welfare or financial interests
12 of the respondent or individual.
13 (c) A report of a court liaison or professional evaluation generated in
14 the course of a proceeding under sections 119 through 130, and
15 amendments thereto, must be sealed on filing but is available to:
16 (1) The court;
17 (2) the individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation,
18 without limitation as to use;
19 (3) the petitioner, court liaison and petitioner's and respondent's
20 attorneys, for purposes of the proceeding;
21 (4) unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a
22 power of attorney for finances in which the respondent is the principal;
23 (5) if the order is for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship
24 and unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a power of
25 attorney for healthcare in which the respondent is identified as the
26 principal; and
27 (6) any other person if it is in the public interest or for a purpose the
28 court orders for good cause.
29 New Sec. 130. The court may appoint a facilitator to assist in
30 implementing a protective arrangement under sections 119 through 130,
31 and amendments thereto. The facilitator has the authority conferred by the
32 order of appointment and serves until discharged by court order.
33 New Sec. 131. For purposes of this act, the judicial council shall
34 develop a statement of rights form, petition forms and report and
35 accounting forms.
36 New Sec. 132. In applying and construing this uniform act,
37 consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law
38 with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.
39 New Sec. 133. This act modifies, limits or supersedes the electronic

42 U.S.C. § 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices

36 the beneficiary shall be valid unless executed in the form and manner

1 to K.S.A. 39-709, and amendments thereto, the balance of the owner's

21 provided in subsection (b)(1)(B);
22 (B) subsection (a)(1) is a severity level 2, person felony, when the
23 victim is a dependent adult who is a resident of an adult care home, as
24 described in subsection (e)(2)(A), during the commission of the offense;
25 (2) subsection (a)(2) if the aggregate amount of the value of the
26 personal property or financial resources is:
27 (A) $1,000,000 or more is a severity level 2, person felony;
28 (B) at least $250,000 but less than $1,000,000 is a severity level 3,
29 person felony;
30 (C) at least $100,000 but less than $250,000 is a severity level 4,
31 person felony;
32 (D) at least $25,000 but less than $100,000 is a severity level 5,
33 person felony;
34 (E) at least $1,500 but less than $25,000 is a severity level 7, person
35 felony;
36 (F) less than $1,500 is a class A person misdemeanor, except as
37 provided in subsection (b)(2)(G); and
38 (G) less than $1,500 and committed by a person who has, within five
39 years immediately preceding commission of the crime, been convicted of a
40 violation of this section two or more times is a severity level 7, person
41 felony; and
42 (3) (A) subsection (a)(3) is a severity level 8, person felony, except as
43 provided in subsection (b)(3)(B); and

HB 2359 109
1 (B) subsection (a)(3) is a severity level 5, person felony, when the
2 victim is a dependent adult who is a resident of an adult care home, as
3 described in subsection (e)(2)(A), during the commission of the offense.
4 (c) It shall be an affirmative defense to any prosecution for
5 mistreatment of a dependent adult or an elder person as described in
6 subsection (a)(2) that:
7 (1) The personal property or financial resources were given as a gift
8 consistent with a pattern of gift giving to the person that existed before the
9 dependent adult or elder person became vulnerable;
10 (2) the personal property or financial resources were given as a gift
11 consistent with a pattern of gift giving to a class of individuals that existed
12 before the dependent adult or elder person became vulnerable;
13 (3) the personal property or financial resources were conferred as a
14 gift by the dependent adult or elder person to the benefit of a person or
15 class of persons, and such gift was reasonable under the circumstances; or
16 (4) a court approved the transaction before the transaction occurred.
17 (d) No dependent adult or elder person is considered to be mistreated
18 under subsection (a)(1) or (a)(3) for the sole reason that such dependent
19 adult or elder person relies upon or is being furnished treatment by
20 spiritual means through prayer in lieu of medical treatment in accordance
21 with the tenets and practices of a recognized church or religious
22 denomination of which such dependent adult or elder person is a member
23 or adherent.
24 (e) As used in this section:
25 (1) "Adequate consideration" means the personal property or
26 financial resources were given to the person as payment for bona fide
27 goods or services provided by such person and the payment was at a rate
28 customary for similar goods or services in the community that the
29 dependent adult or elder person resided in at the time of the transaction.
30 (2) "Dependent adult" means an individual 18 years of age or older
31 who is unable to protect the individual's own interest. Such term shall
32 include, but is not limited to, any:
33 (A) Resident of an adult care home including, but not limited to,
34 those facilities defined by K.S.A. 39-923, and amendments thereto;
35 (B) adult cared for in a private residence;
36 (C) individual kept, cared for, treated, boarded, confined or otherwise
37 accommodated in a medical care facility;
38 (D) individual with intellectual disability or a developmental
39 disability receiving services through a community facility for people with
40 intellectual disability or residential facility licensed under K.S.A. 39-2001
41 et seq., and amendments thereto;
42 (E) individual with a developmental disability receiving services
43 provided by a community service provider as provided in the

HB 2359 110
1 developmental disability reform act; or
2 (F) individual kept, cared for, treated, boarded, confined or otherwise
3 accommodated in a state psychiatric hospital or state institution for people
4 with intellectual disability.
5 (3) "Elder person" means a person 60 years of age or older.
6 (f) An offender who violates the provisions of this section may also
7 be prosecuted for, convicted of, and punished for any other offense in
8 article 54, 55, 56 or 58 of chapter 21 of the Kansas Statutes Annotated, or
9 K.S.A. 21-6418, and amendments thereto.
10 Sec. 140. K.S.A. 38-2217 is hereby amended to read as follows: 38-

9 Sec. 144. K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-656 is hereby amended to read as
10 follows: 58-656. (a) An attorney in fact who elects to act under a power of
11 attorney is under a duty to act in the interest of the principal and to avoid
12 conflicts of interest that impair the ability of the attorney in fact so to act.
13 A person who is appointed an attorney in fact under a power of attorney
14 who undertakes to exercise the authority conferred in the power of
15 attorney, has a fiduciary obligation to exercise the powers conferred in the
16 best interests of the principal, and to avoid self-dealing and conflicts of
17 interest, as in the case of a trustee with respect to the trustee's beneficiary
18 or beneficiaries. The attorney in fact shall keep a record of receipts,
19 disbursements and transactions made on behalf of the principal and shall
20 not comingle funds or assets of the principal with the funds or assets of the
21 attorney in fact. In the absence of explicit authorization, the attorney in
22 fact shall exercise a high degree of care in maintaining, without
23 modification, any estate plan which the principal may have in place,
24 including, but not limited to, arrangements made by the principal for
25 disposition of assets at death through beneficiary designations, ownership
26 by joint tenancy or tenancy by the entirety, trust arrangements or by will or
27 codicil. Unless otherwise provided in the power of attorney or in a separate
28 agreement between the principal and attorney in fact, an attorney in fact
29 who elects to act shall exercise the authority granted in a power of attorney
30 with that degree of care that would be observed by a prudent person
31 dealing with the property and conducting the affairs of another, except that
32 all investments made on or after July 1, 2003, shall be in accordance with
33 the provisions of the Kansas uniform prudent investor act, K.S.A. 58-
34 24a01 et seq., and amendments thereto. If the attorney in fact has special
35 skills or was appointed attorney in fact on the basis of representations of
36 special skills or expertise, the attorney in fact has a duty to use those skills
37 in the principal's behalf.
38 (b) On matters undertaken or to be undertaken in the principal's
39 behalf and to the extent reasonably possible under the circumstances, an
40 attorney in fact has a duty to keep in regular contact with the principal, to
41 communicate with the principal and to obtain and follow the instructions
42 of the principal.
43 (c) If, following execution of a durable power of attorney, a court of

HB 2359 118
1 the principal's domicile appoints a conservator, guardian of the estate or
2 other fiduciary charged with the management of all of the principal's
3 property or all of the principal's property except specified exclusions, the
4 attorney in fact is accountable to the fiduciary as well as to the principal.
5 The fiduciary has the same power to revoke or amend the durable power of
6 attorney that the principal would have had if the principal were not an
7 adult with an impairment in need of a guardian or conservator or both as
8 defined by subsection (a) of K.S.A. 59-3051 section 25, and amendments
9 thereto.
10 (d) A principal may nominate by a power of attorney, a guardian or
11 conservator, or both, for consideration by the court. If a petition to appoint
12 a guardian or conservator, or both, is filed, the court shall make the
13 appointment in accordance with the principal's most recent nomination in
14 the power of attorney, so long as the individual nominated is a fit and
15 proper person.
16 (e) An attorney in fact shall exercise authority granted by the
17 principal in accordance with the instrument setting forth the power of
18 attorney, any modification made therein by the principal or the principal's
19 legal representative or a court, and the oral and written instructions of the
20 principal, or the written instructions of the principal's legal representative
21 or a court.
22 (f) An attorney in fact may be instructed in a power of attorney that
23 the authority granted shall not be exercised until, or shall terminate on, the
24 happening of a future event, condition or contingency, as determined in a
25 manner prescribed in the instrument.
26 (g) On the death of the principal, the attorney in fact shall follow the
27 instructions of the court, if any, having jurisdiction over the estate of the
28 principal, or any part thereof, and shall communicate with and be
29 accountable to the principal's personal representative, or if none, the
30 principal's successors. The attorney in fact shall promptly deliver to and
31 put in the possession and control of the principal's personal representative
32 or successors, any property of the principal and copies of any records of
33 the attorney in fact relating to transactions undertaken in the principal's
34 behalf that are deemed by the personal representative or the court to be
35 necessary or helpful in the administration of the decedent's estate.
36 (h) If an attorney in fact has a property or contract interest in the
37 subject of the power of attorney or the authority of the attorney in fact is
38 otherwise coupled with an interest in a person other than the principal, this
39 section does not impose any duties on the attorney in fact that would
40 conflict or be inconsistent with that interest.

4 the principal is a disabled person and that the attorney in fact has breached
5 such attorney in fact's fiduciary duty to the principal or that there is a
6 reasonable likelihood that such attorney in fact may do so in the immediate
7 future, the court, in its discretion, may issue an order that some or all of
8 the authority granted by the durable power of attorney be suspended or
9 modified, and that a different attorney in fact be authorized to exercise
10 some or all of the powers granted by the durable power of attorney. Such
11 attorney in fact may be designated by the court. The court may require any
12 person petitioning for any such order to file a bond in such amount and
13 with such sureties as required by the court to indemnify either the attorney
14 in fact who has been acting on behalf of the principal or the principal and
15 the principal's successors in interest for the expenses, including attorney
16 fees, incurred by any such persons with respect to such proceeding. The
17 court, after hearing, may allow payment or enter judgment. None of the
18 actions described in this subsection shall be taken by the court until after
19 hearing upon reasonable notice to all persons identified in a verified
20 statement supplied by the petitioner who is requesting such action
21 identifying the immediate relatives of the principal and any other persons
22 known to the petitioner to be interested in the welfare of the principal.
23 Except that in the event of an emergency as determined by the court, the
24 court, without notice, may enter such temporary order as seems proper to
25 the court, but no such temporary order shall be effective for more than 30
26 days unless extended by the court after hearing on reasonable notice to the
27 persons identified as herein provided in this subsection.
28 (g) If a power of attorney is suspended or terminated by the court or
29 the attorney in fact is removed by the court, the court may require an
30 accounting from the attorney in fact and order delivery of any property
31 belonging to the principal and copies of any necessary records of the
32 attorney in fact concerning the principal's property and affairs to a
33 successor attorney in fact or the principal's legal representative.
34 (h) In a proceeding under this act or in any other proceeding, or upon
35 petition of an attorney in fact or successor, the court may:
36 (1) Require or permit an attorney in fact under a power of attorney to
37 account;
38 (2) authorize the attorney in fact under a power of attorney to enter
39 into any transaction, or approve, ratify, confirm and validate any
40 transaction entered into by the attorney in fact that the court finds is, was
41 or will be beneficial to the principal and which the court has power to
42 authorize for a conservator pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3050 et seq. the Kansas
43 uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other protective arrangements

HB 2359 121
1 act, sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto; and
2 (3) relieve the attorney in fact of any obligation to exercise authority
3 for a disabled principal under a durable power of attorney.
4 (i) Unless previously barred by adjudication, consent or limitation,
5 any cause of action against an attorney in fact or successor for breach of
6 duty to the principal shall be barred as to any principal who has received
7 an account or other statement fully disclosing the matter unless a
8 proceeding to assert the cause of action is commenced within two years
9 after receipt of the account or statement by the principal or, if the principal
10 is a disabled person, by a guardian or conservator of the disabled person's
11 estate. If a disabled person has no guardian or conservator of the disabled
12 person's estate at the time an account or statement is presented, then the
13 cause of action shall not be barred until one year after the removal of the
14 principal's disability or incapacity, one year after the appointment of a
15 conservator for the principal or one year after the death of the principal.
16 The cause of action thus barred does not include any action to recover
17 from an attorney in fact or successor for fraud, misrepresentation or
18 concealment related to the settlement of any transaction involving the
19 agency relationship of the attorney in fact with the principal.

20 as a voluntary patient, then the head of the treatment facility shall notify, in
21 writing, the patient's attorney, the patient's legal guardian, if the patient has
22 a legal guardian, and the district court which has jurisdiction over the
23 patient of the patient's voluntary status. When a notice of voluntary
24 admission is received, the court shall file the same which shall terminate
25 the proceedings.

10 (c) "Law enforcement officer" means the same as defined in K.S.A.
11 22-2202, and amendments thereto.
12 (d) (1) "Mental health center" means any community mental health
13 center as defined in K.S.A. 39-2002, and amendments thereto, or a mental
14 health clinic organized as a not-for-profit or a for-profit corporation
15 pursuant to K.S.A. 17-1701 through 17-1775, and amendments thereto, or

21 services pursuant to the provisions of K.S.A. 39-1601 through 39-1612,
22 and amendments thereto.
23 (e) "Mentally ill person" means any person who is suffering from a
24 mental disorder that is manifested by a clinically significant behavioral or
25 psychological syndrome or pattern and associated with either a painful
26 symptom or an impairment in one or more important areas of functioning,
27 and involving substantial behavioral, psychological or biological
28 dysfunction, to the extent that the person is in need of treatment.
29 (f) (1) "Mentally ill person subject to involuntary commitment for
30 care and treatment" means a mentally ill person, as defined in subsection
31 (e), who also lacks capacity to make an informed decision concerning
32 treatment, is likely to cause harm to self or others, and whose diagnosis is
33 not solely one of the following mental disorders: Alcohol or chemical
34 substance abuse; antisocial personality disorder; intellectual disability;
35 organic personality syndrome; or an organic mental disorder.
36 (2) "Lacks capacity to make an informed decision concerning
37 treatment" means that the person, by reason of the person's mental
38 disorder, is unable, despite conscientious efforts at explanation, to
39 understand basically the nature and effects of hospitalization or treatment
40 or is unable to engage in a rational decision-making process regarding
41 hospitalization or treatment, as evidenced by an inability to weigh the
42 possible risks and benefits.
43 (3) "Likely to cause harm to self or others" means that the person, by

HB 2359 135
1 reason of the person's mental disorder: (A) Is likely, in the reasonably
2 foreseeable future, to cause substantial physical injury or physical abuse to
3 self or others or substantial damage to another's property, as evidenced by
4 behavior threatening, attempting or causing such injury, abuse or damage;
5 except that if the harm threatened, attempted or caused is only harm to the
6 property of another, the harm must be of such a value and extent that the
7 state's interest in protecting the property from such harm outweighs the
8 person's interest in personal liberty; or (B) is substantially unable, except
9 for reason of indigency, to provide for any of the person's basic needs,
10 such as food, clothing, shelter, health or safety, causing a substantial
11 deterioration of the person's ability to function on the person's own.
12 No person who is being treated by prayer in the practice of the religion
13 of any church that teaches reliance on spiritual means alone through prayer
14 for healing shall be determined to be a mentally ill person subject to

22 any class or classes thereof, and their spouses and dependents to pay an
23 amount equal to resident fees:
24 (1) Persons who are employees of a state educational institution;
25 (2) persons having special domestic relations circumstances;
26 (3) persons who have lost their resident status within six months of
27 enrollment;
28 (4) persons who are not domiciliary residents of the state, who have
29 graduated from a high school accredited by the state board of education
30 within six months of enrollment, who were domiciliary residents of the
31 state at the time of graduation from high school or within 12 months prior
32 to graduation from high school, and who are entitled to admission at a
33 state educational institution pursuant to K.S.A. 76-717b, and amendments
34 thereto;
35 (5) persons who are domiciliary residents of the state, whose
36 domiciliary residence was established in the state for the purpose of
37 accepting, upon recruitment by an employer, or retaining, upon transfer
38 required by an employer, a position of full-time employment at a place of
39 employment in Kansas, but the domiciliary residence of whom was not
40 timely enough established to meet the residence duration requirement of
41 subsection (a), and who are not otherwise eligible for authorization to pay
42 an amount equal to resident fees under this subsection.
43 (c) Pursuant to K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 48-3601, and amendments thereto,

HB 2359 143
1 a veteran, an active duty member of the armed forces and the spouse and
2 dependent child of such veteran or active duty member of the armed forces
3 shall be deemed residents of the state for fee purposes.
4 (d) As used in this section:
5 (1) "Parents" means and includes natural parents, adoptive parents,
6 stepparents, guardians and custodians.
7 (2) "Guardian" has the meaning ascribed thereto by K.S.A. 59-3051
8 means the same as defined in section 25, and amendments thereto.
9 (3) "Custodian" means a person, agency or association granted legal
10 custody of a minor under the revised Kansas code for care of children.
11 (4) "Domiciliary resident" means a person who has present and fixed
12 residence in Kansas where the person intends to remain for an indefinite
13 period and to which the person intends to return following absence.
14 (5) "Full-time employment" means employment requiring at least
15 1,500 hours of work per year.
16 (6) "Dependent" means: (A) A birth child, adopted child or stepchild;
17 or
18 (B) any child other than the foregoing who is actually dependent in
19 whole or in part on the person in military service and who is related to
20 such individual by marriage or consanguinity.
21 (7) "Academic year" means the twelve-month 12-month period
22 ending June 30.
23 Sec. 165. K.S.A. 76-12b04 is hereby amended to read as follows: 76-
24 12b04. If in the opinion of the superintendent an applicant for admission
25 meets the definition of a person in need of a guardian or a conservator, or
26 both, as provided in K.S.A. 59-3050 through 59-3095 the Kansas uniform
27 guardianship, conservatorship and other protective arrangements act,
28 sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto, the person shall not be
29 admitted to an institution except for the purposes of conducting a court
30 ordered evaluation pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3064 section 69, and
31 amendments thereto, until a court has determined the legal status of the
32 person under the act for obtaining a guardian or conservator, or both. The
33 provisions of this paragraph shall not be applicable if a court has already
34 determined the legal status of the applicant under the act.
35 Sec. 166. K.S.A. 77-201 is hereby amended to read as follows: 77-
36 201. In the construction of the statutes of this state the following rules
37 shall be observed, unless the construction would be inconsistent with the
38 manifest intent of the legislature or repugnant to the context of the statute:
39 First. The repeal of a statute does not revive a statute previously
40 repealed, nor does the repeal affect any right which accrued, any duty
41 imposed, any penalty incurred or any proceeding commenced, under or by
42 virtue of the statute repealed. The provisions of any statute, so far as they
43 are the same as those of any prior statute, shall be construed as a

HB 2359 144
1 continuation of the prior provisions and not as a new enactment.
2 Second. Words and phrases shall be construed according to the context
3 and the approved usage of the language, but technical words and phrases,
4 and other words and phrases that have acquired a peculiar and appropriate
5 meaning in law, shall be construed according to their peculiar and
6 appropriate meanings.
7 Third. Words importing the singular number only may be extended to
8 several persons or things, and words importing the plural number only
9 may be applied to one person or thing. Words importing the masculine
10 gender only may be extended to females.
11 Fourth. Words giving a joint authority to three or more public officers
12 or other persons shall be construed as given that authority to a majority of
13 them, unless it is otherwise expressed in the act giving the authority.
14 Fifth. "Highway" and "road" include public bridges and may be
15 construed to be equivalent to "county way," "county road," "common
16 road," "state road" and "territorial road."
17 Sixth. "Incompetent person" includes disabled persons and
18 incapacitated persons as defined herein in this section.
19 Seventh. "Issue," as applied to the descent of estates, includes all the
20 lawful lineal descendants of the ancestor.
21 Eighth. "Land," "real estate" and "real property" include lands,
22 tenements and hereditaments, and all rights to them and interest in them,
23 equitable as well as legal.
24 Ninth. "Personal property" includes money, goods, chattels, evidences
25 of debt and things in action, and digital assets as defined in the revised
26 uniform fiduciary access to digital assets act, K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-4801
27 through 58-4819, and amendments thereto.
28 Tenth. "Property" includes personal and real property.
29 Eleventh. "Month" means a calendar month, unless otherwise
30 expressed. "Year" alone, and also the abbreviation "A.D.," is equivalent to
31 the expression "year of our Lord."
32 Twelfth. "Oath" includes an affirmation in all cases where an
33 affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in similar cases "swear"
34 includes affirm.
35 Thirteenth. "Person" may be extended to bodies politic and corporate.
36 Fourteenth. If the seal of a court or public office or officer is required
37 by law to be affixed to any paper, "seal" includes an impression of the seal
38 upon the paper alone, as well as upon wax or a wafer affixed to the paper.
39 "Seal" also includes both a rubber stamp seal used with permanent ink and
40 the word "seal" printed on court documents produced by computer
41 systems, so that the seal may be legibly reproduced by photographic
42 process.
43 Fifteenth. "State," when applied to the different parts of the United

HB 2359 145
1 States, includes the District of Columbia and the territories. "United
2 States" may include that district and those territories.
3 Sixteenth. "Town" may mean a civil township, unless a different
4 meaning is plainly intended.
5 Seventeenth. "Will" includes codicils.
6 Eighteenth. "Written" and "in writing" may include printing, engraving,
7 lithography and any other mode of representing words and letters,
8 excepting those cases where the written signature or the mark of any
9 person is required by law.
10 Nineteenth. "Sheriff" may be extended to any person performing the
11 duties of the sheriff, either generally or in special cases.
12 Twentieth. "Deed" is applied to an instrument conveying lands but does
13 not imply a sealed instrument. "Bond" and "indenture" do not necessarily
14 imply a seal but in other respects mean the same kind of instruments as
15 above. "Undertaking" means a promise or security in any form where
16 required by law.
17 Twenty-first. "Executor" includes an administrator where the subject
18 matter applies to an administrator.
19 Twenty-second. Roman numerals and Arabic figures are to be taken as a
20 part of the English language.
21 Twenty-third. "Residence" means the place which is adopted by a
22 person as the person's place of habitation and to which, whenever the
23 person is absent, the person has the intention of returning. When a person
24 eats at one place and sleeps at another, the place where the person sleeps
25 shall be considered the person's residence.
26 Twenty-fourth. "Usual place of residence" and "usual place of abode,"
27 when applied to the service of any process or notice, means the place
28 usually occupied by a person. If a person has no family, or does not have
29 family with the person, the person's office or place of business or, if the
30 person has no place of business, the room or place where the person
31 usually sleeps shall be construed to be the person's place of residence or
32 abode.
33 Twenty-fifth. "Householder" means a person who is 18 or more years of
34 age and who owns or occupies a house as a place of residence and not as a
35 boarder or lodger.
36 Twenty-sixth. "General election" refers to the election required to be
37 held on the Tuesday following the first Monday in November of each
38 even-numbered year.
39 Twenty-seventh. "Under legal disability" includes persons who are
40 within the period of minority, or who are incapacitated, incompetent or
41 imprisoned.
42 Twenty-eighth. When a person is required to be disinterested or
43 indifferent in acting on any question or matter affecting other parties,

HB 2359 146
1 relationship within the degree of second cousin, inclusive, shall disqualify
2 the person from acting, except by consent of parties.
3 Twenty-ninth. "Head of a family" shall include any person who has
4 charge of children, relatives or others living with the person.
5 Thirtieth. "Mentally ill person" means a mentally ill person as defined
6 in K.S.A. 59-2946, and amendments thereto.
7 Thirty-first. "Incapacitated person" means an individual whose ability
8 to receive and evaluate relevant information, or to effectively
9 communicate decisions, or both, even with the use of assistive
10 technologies or other supports, is impaired to the degree that the person
11 lacks the capacity to manage the person's estate, or to meet essential needs
12 for the person's physical health, safety or welfare, as defined in K.S.A. 59-
13 3051 section 25, and amendments thereto, whether or not a guardian or a
14 conservator has been appointed for that person.
15 Thirty-second. "Guardian" means an individual or a nonprofit
16 corporation certified in accordance with K.S.A. 59-3070 section 35, and
17 amendments thereto, which has been appointed by a court to act on behalf
18 of a ward and possessed of some or all of the powers and duties set out in
19 K.S.A. 59-3075 sections 76 through 78, and amendments thereto.
20 "Guardian" does not mean natural guardian unless specified.
21 Thirty-third. "Natural guardian" means both the biological or adoptive
22 mother and father of a minor if neither parent has been found to be an
23 adult with an impairment in need of a guardian or has had parental rights
24 terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction. If either parent of a minor
25 is deceased, or has been found to be an adult with an impairment in need
26 of a guardian, as provided for in K.S.A. 59-3050 through 59-3095 the
27 Kansas uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other protective
28 arrangements act, sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto, or
29 has had parental rights terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction,
30 then the other parent shall be the natural guardian, unless also deceased, or
31 found to be an adult with an impairment in need of a guardian, or has had
32 parental rights terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction, in which
33 case no person shall qualify as the natural guardian.
34 Thirty-fourth. "Conservator" means an individual or corporation
35 appointed by the court to act on behalf of a conservatee and possessed of
36 some or all of the powers and duties set out in K.S.A. 59-3078 sections 99
37 through 102, and amendments thereto.
38 Thirty-fifth. "Minor" means any person defined by K.S.A. 38-101, and
39 amendments thereto, as being within the period of minority.
40 Thirty-sixth. "Proposed ward" means a person for whom a petition for
41 the appointment of a guardian pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3058, 59-3059, 59-
42 3060 or 59-3061 sections 17, 18, 28, 49, 52 or 65, and amendments
43 thereto, has been filed.

HB 2359 147
1 Thirty-seventh. "Proposed conservatee" means a person for whom a
2 petition for the appointment of a conservator pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3058,
3 59-3059, 59-3060 or 59-3061 sections 17, 18, 28, 49, 52 or 65, and
4 amendments thereto, has been filed.
5 Thirty-eighth. "Ward" means a person who has a guardian.
6 Thirty-ninth. "Conservatee" means a person who has a conservator.
7 Fortieth. "Manufactured home" means a structure which:
8 (1) Is transportable in one or more sections which, in the traveling
9 mode, is 8 body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length,
10 or, when erected on site, is 320 or more square feet, and which is built on a
11 permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling, with or without
12 permanent foundation, when connected to the required utilities, and
13 includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning and electrical systems
14 contained therein; and
15 (2) is subject to the federal manufactured home construction and
16 safety standards established pursuant to 42 U.S.C. § 5403.
17 Forty-first. "Mobile home" means a structure which:
18 (1) Is transportable in one or more sections which, in the traveling
19 mode, is 8 body feet or more in width and 36 body feet or more in length
20 and is built on a permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling,
21 with or without a permanent foundation, when connected to the required
22 utilities, and includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning and electrical
23 systems contained therein; and
24 (2) is not subject to the federal manufactured home construction and
25 safety standards established pursuant to 42 U.S.C. § 5403.
26 Forty-second. "Disabled person" includes incapacitated persons and
27 incompetent persons as defined herein in this section.
